Presidential elections were held in [[Venezuela]] on 28 July 2024 to choose a [[President of Venezuela|president]] for a six-year term beginning on 10 January 2025.<ref name= NPRWhatToKnow>{{cite news |url= https://www.npr.org/2024/07/26/nx-s1-5051813/venezuela-election-nicolas-maduro-opposition-edmundo-gonzalez |publisher= [[NPR]] |title= What to know about Venezuela's election, as Maduro faces stiff opposition |date= 26 July 2024 |first1= John |last1= Otis |first2= Carrie |last2= Kahn |access-date= 29 July 2024 |archive-date= 28 July 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240728210202/https://www.npr.org/2024/07/26/nx-s1-5051813/venezuela-election-nicolas-maduro-opposition-edmundo-gonzalez |url-status= live }}</ref><ref name="Barrons.com">{{Cite web |title=Venezuela Will Hold Presidential Elections On July 28: Official |url=https://www.barrons.com/news/venezuela-will-hold-presidential-elections-on-july-28-official-fdbedc52|access-date=15 March 2024 |website=Barrons.com |language=en-US |archive-date=11 June 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240611051359/https://www.barrons.com/news/venezuela-will-hold-presidential-elections-on-july-28-official-fdbedc52 |url-status=live }}</ref> The election was contentious, with international monitors calling it neither [[Free and fair election|free nor fair]],<ref name="Glatsky-2024">{{Cite news |last=Glatsky |first=Genevieve |date=31 July 2024 |title=Venezuela's Election Was Deeply Flawed. Here's How. |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2024/07/31/world/americas/venezuela-election-vote-flaws.html |access-date=2 August 2024 |work=The New York Times |language=en-US |issn=0362-4331 |quote=It had already been clear for months that Venezuela's presidential election on Sunday, would not be free or fair, as the government jailed opposition leaders or disqualified them from running for office, and prevented millions of Venezuelans abroad from voting.}}</ref> citing the incumbent [[Cabinet of Venezuela#Cabinet of Nicolás Maduro|Maduro administration]]'s having controlled most institutions and repressed the [[Venezuelan opposition|political opposition]] before, during,<ref name=NPRWhatToKnow/><ref>{{Cite web |date=24 July 2024 |title=Maduro regime doubles down on censorship and repression in lead-up to Venezuelan election |url=https://www.icij.org/inside-icij/2024/07/maduro-regime-doubles-down-on-censorship-and-repression-in-lead-up-to-venezuelan-election/ |website=ICIJ |language=en-US|access-date=29 July 2024 |archive-date=24 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240724233536/https://www.icij.org/inside-icij/2024/07/maduro-regime-doubles-down-on-censorship-and-repression-in-lead-up-to-venezuelan-election/ |url-status=live }}</ref> and after the election. Widely viewed as having won the election, former diplomat [[Edmundo González]] fled to asylum in Spain amid repression of dissent and a [[2024 Venezuelan political crisis|national and international political crisis]] that resulted when Venezuelan electoral authorities announced—without presenting any evidence—that [[Nicolás Maduro]] had won.<ref name=TimesFlees/>

Maduro ran for a third consecutive term, while González represented the [[Unitary Platform]] ({{langx|es|Plataforma Unitaria Democrática|italic=no|links=no}}; PUD), the main opposition political alliance. In June 2023, the Venezuelan government had barred leading candidate [[María Corina Machado]] from participating.<ref name= MCM>{{cite news |title=Líder da oposição nas pesquisas, María Corina Machado é inabilitada por 15 anos na Venezuela |url=https://oglobo.globo.com/mundo/noticia/2023/06/lider-da-oposicao-nas-pesquisas-maria-corina-machado-e-inabilitada-por-15-anos-na-venezuela.ghtml |access-date=31 July 2024 |work=O Globo |date=30 June 2023 |language=pt-br |archive-date=31 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240731201311/https://oglobo.globo.com/mundo/noticia/2023/06/lider-da-oposicao-nas-pesquisas-maria-corina-machado-e-inabilitada-por-15-anos-na-venezuela.ghtml |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Venezuela's Supreme Court disqualifies opposition leader from running for president |url= https://www.lemonde.fr/en/international/article/2024/01/27/venezuela-s-supreme-court-disqualifies-opposition-leader-from-running-for-president_6469941_4.html |access-date=31 July 2024 |date=27 January 2024 |language=en |archive-date=31 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240731195716/https://www.lemonde.fr/en/international/article/2024/01/27/venezuela-s-supreme-court-disqualifies-opposition-leader-from-running-for-president_6469941_4.html |url-status=live }}</ref> This move was regarded by the opposition as a violation of political human rights and was condemned by international bodies such as the [[Organization of American States]] (OAS),<ref name="OAS_report_VE_pres_elec_DECO" /> the [[European Union]],<ref name="EUopposition">{{cite web |title=Venezuela: Statement by the Spokesperson on banning opposition politicians |url=https://www.eeas.europa.eu/eeas/venezuela-statement-spokesperson-banning-opposition-politicians_en |website=EEAS |publisher=Diplomatic Service of the European Union |access-date=31 July 2024 |language=en |date=21 January 2024 |archive-date=31 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240731134424/https://www.eeas.europa.eu/eeas/venezuela-statement-spokesperson-banning-opposition-politicians_en |url-status=live }}</ref> and [[Human Rights Watch]],<ref>{{Cite web |date=2 February 2024 |title=Carta al presidente Gustavo Petro sobre inhabilitación de María Corina Machado en Venezuela |publisher= Human Rights Watch |url=https://www.hrw.org/es/news/2024/02/02/carta-al-presidente-gustavo-petro-sobre-inhabilitacion-de-maria-corina-machado-en |access-date=9 August 2024 |language=es}}</ref> as well as numerous countries.<ref>{{Cite web |date=27 January 2024 |title=US condemns ban on Venezuelan opposition leader's candidacy and puts sanctions relief under review |url=https://apnews.com/article/venezuela-opposition-candidate-ban-machado-maduro-548531e6db1dca250dc784f0dc2374c5 |access-date=12 August 2024 |website=AP News |language=en}}</ref>

Academics, news outlets and the opposition provided strong evidence showing that González won the election by a wide margin<ref name= GuardianEvidenceShows/><ref>{{Cite news |last1=Kurmanaev |first1=Anatoly |last2=Singer |first2=Ethan |date=31 July 2024 |title=Election Results Presented by Venezuela's Opposition Suggest Maduro Lost Decisively |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2024/07/31/world/americas/venezuela-maduro-election-results.html |access-date=2 August 2024 |work=The New York Times |language=en-US |issn=0362-4331 |quote=The Times analysis shows that the election tallies provided by the researchers are not compatible with a victory by Mr. Maduro, by any margin. |archive-date=2 August 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240802004857/https://www.nytimes.com/2024/07/31/world/americas/venezuela-maduro-election-results.html |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name=BBC2Aug>{{cite web|url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/articles/cd1d10453zno|title=Overwhelming evidence Venezuela opposition won election - Blinken|last=Wells|first=Ione|website=BBC News|date=2 August 2024|accessdate=2 August 2024}}</ref> with the opposition releasing copies of official [[#Electoral process|tally sheets]] collected by [[poll watchers]] from a majority of polling centers showing a landslide victory for González.<ref name="OAS_report_VE_pres_elec_DECO" /><ref name="opposition_results_website" /><ref name="LaPatilla_how2access_electoral_records" /> The government-controlled [[National Electoral Council (Venezuela)|National Electoral Council]] (CNE) announced<ref name="AlbaCTP_CNE_Maduro_victory_5120" /> [[election fraud|falsified]]<ref name="ElEspectador_decimal_places"/><ref name="Infobae_burdo"/> results claiming a narrow Maduro victory on 29 July; vote tallies were not provided.<ref name=GuardianPressureGrows/> The [[Carter Center]] was unable to verify the CNE's results, asserting the election failed to meet international democratic election standards.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Carter Center Statement on Venezuela Election |url=https://www.cartercenter.org/news/pr/2024/venezuela-073024.html |access-date=2024-12-14 |website=The Carter Center |language=en-US}}</ref>  The CNE's results were rejected by the OAS,<ref name="OAS_report_VE_pres_elec_DECO" /> and the [[United Nations]] declared that there was "no precedent in contemporary democratic elections" for announcing a winner without providing tabulated results.<ref name=UNBlasts/> Analyses by media sources found the CNE results statistically improbable and lacking in credibility.<ref name=APReview/><ref name="WAPOMaduroLost" /><ref name="ElEspectador_decimal_places" /> [[quick count|Parallel vote tabulation]] confirmed the win by González.<ref name="Figueiredo_method_vote_counts_limited_integrity" /><ref name="AtlanticDictatorLies" /><ref name="AltaVista_PVT_results" /> Political scientist [[Steven Levitsky]] called the official results "one of the most egregious electoral frauds in modern Latin American history".<ref name="Turkewitz-2024a">{{Cite news |last=Turkewitz |first=Julie |date=30 July 2024 |title=What Happened to Venezuela's Democracy? |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2024/07/30/world/americas/venezuela-election-maduro-chavez.html |access-date=2 August 2024 |work=[[The New York Times]] |language=en-US |issn=0362-4331|archive-url=https://archive.today/20240730091400/https://www.nytimes.com/2024/07/30/world/americas/venezuela-election-maduro-chavez.html|archive-date=30 July 2024|url-access=subscription}}</ref>

[[2024 Venezuelan protests|Protests occurred across the country and internationally]], as the Maduro administration initiated [[Operation Tun Tun]], a crackdown on dissent. [[International reactions to the 2024 Venezuelan presidential election|Some world leaders rejected the CNE's claimed results]] and recognized González as the election winner,<ref name=BBC2Aug/><ref name= HardtoBelieve/><ref name=reuters29jul /> while some other countries, including Russia, China, Iran, North Korea and Cuba recognized Maduro as the winner.<ref name= WorldLeadersCast/><ref name=TimesFlees/>  Maduro did not cede power,<ref name=GuardianRefusal>{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/article/2024/aug/14/venezuela-election-maduro|title=Nicolás Maduro's refusal to quit raises a troubling question for Venezuela: what next?|work=The Guardian|author=Phillips, Tom|date=14 August 2024|access-date=23 August 2024}}</ref> and instead asked the [[Supreme Tribunal of Justice (Venezuela)|Supreme Tribunal of Justice]] (TSJ), composed of justices loyal to Maduro,<ref name=GuardianPressureGrows/><ref name=WPBidenDeal/><ref name=LoyaltoMaduro/><ref name=HandPicked/> to audit and approve the results.<ref name=ReutersCourtRatifies/><ref name= BBCStayinPower/><ref name=CriesFoul/><ref name=APCourtCertifies/>  On 22 August, as anticipated,<ref name=BBCStayinPower/><ref name=LoyaltoMaduro/><ref name=HandPicked/> the TSJ described the CNE's statement of Maduro winning the election as "validated".<ref name=ReutersCourtRatifies/> The supreme court ruling was rejected by [[the United States]], [[the European Union]] and ten Latin American countries.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Phillips |first1=Tom |title=US and 10 Latin American states reject Nicolás Maduro's vote certification |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/article/2024/aug/23/latin-american-states-and-us-reject-maduro-vote-certification-election-venezuela-supreme-court |access-date=30 August 2024 |work=[[The Guardian]] |date=23 August 2024 |location=Rio de Janeiro}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Phillips |first1=Tom |title='No democratic legitimacy': EU rejects Maduro's Venezuela election win claim |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/article/2024/aug/29/eu-foreign-policy-chief-says-he-wont-accept-maduro-as-venezuelan-president |access-date=30 August 2024 |work=[[The Guardian]] |date=29 August 2024}}</ref> An arrest warrant was issued on 2 September for González for the alleged crimes of "usurpation of functions, falsification of public documents, instigation to disobey the law, conspiracy and association", according to Reuters.<ref name=APArrestWarrant/> After seeking asylum in the Spanish Embassy in Caracas, González left for Spain on 7 September.<ref name=ElDiarioAsylum/> Maduro was sworn in for a third term on 10 January 2025.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Venezuela’s Nicolas Maduro sworn in for third presidential term |url=https://edition.cnn.com/2025/01/10/americas/venezuelas-nicolas-maduro-sworn-in-intl/index.html |access-date=January 10, 2025 |website=www.cnn.com |language=en-US}}</ref>

{{Politics of Venezuela}} 
{{TOC limit|3}}

== Background ==

=== Democratic backsliding and consolidation of power===
{{See also|Economy of Venezuela}}
The 2024 elections occurred within an [[Authoritarianism|authoritarian]] regime with significant [[democratic backsliding]] under Maduro.<ref name=Turkewitz-2024a/><ref name=Corrales/>

Rampant [[Crime in Venezuela|crime]], [[Crisis in Venezuela#Inflation|hyperinflation]] and [[Shortages in Venezuela|shortages]] beginning in 2010 led to a [[crisis in Venezuela]];<ref name= SecondDay>{{cite news |url= https://www.nytimes.com/2019/03/08/world/americas/venezuela-blackout-power.html |work= New York Times |title= Venezuela blackout, in 2nd day, threatens food supplies and patient lives |date= 8 March 2019 |access-date= 18 March 2019|quote= The Maduro administration has been responsible for grossly mismanaging the economy and plunging the country into a deep humanitarian crisis in which many people lack food and medical care. He has also attempted to crush the opposition by jailing or exiling critics, and using lethal force against antigovernment protesters. |archive-date= 16 March 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190316205111/https://www.nytimes.com/2019/03/08/world/americas/venezuela-blackout-power.html|url-status= live }}</ref><ref name=Turkewitz-2024a/><ref>{{cite news|last = Corrales |first = Javier |title= The House That Chavez Built |url= https://foreignpolicy.com/2013/03/07/the-house-that-chavez-built/ |access-date = 6 February 2015 |work = [[Foreign Policy]] |date = 7 March 2013 |archive-date= 11 April 2020 |archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20200411142428/https://foreignpolicy.com/2013/03/07/the-house-that-chavez-built/ |url-status = live }}</ref> amid declining popularity of the government, the opposition was elected to the majority in the 2015 [[National Assembly (Venezuela)|National Assembly]].<ref name=Turkewitz-2024a/><ref name=NYTmuzzle>{{cite news |last1=Casey |first1=Nicholas |last2=Torres |first2=Patricia |title=Venezuela Muzzles Legislature, Moving Closer to One-Man Rule |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/03/30/world/americas/venezuelas-supreme-court-takes-power-from-legislature.html |access-date=31 March 2017 |work=[[The New York Times]] |date=30 March 2017 |page=A1 |archive-date=9 December 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201209043708/https://www.nytimes.com/2017/03/30/world/americas/venezuelas-supreme-court-takes-power-from-legislature.html |url-status=live }}</ref> Following that election, the [[Lame duck (politics)|lame duck]] National Assembly—with an outgoing pro-government majority—packed the [[Supreme Tribunal of Justice (Venezuela)|Supreme Tribunal of Justice]] (TSJ) with Maduro allies.<ref name=NYTmuzzle/><ref name=Bloomberg-2015>{{cite news |title = Venezuela's Lame-Duck Congress Names New Supreme Court Justices |url = https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2015-12-23/venezuela-s-lame-duck-congress-names-new-supreme-court-justices |access-date = 31 March 2017 |work = Bloomberg |date = 23 December 2015 |archive-date = 4 July 2019 |archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20190704033155/https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2015-12-23/venezuela-s-lame-duck-congress-names-new-supreme-court-justices |url-status = live }}</ref> The new tribunal stripped three opposition lawmakers of their assembly seats in 2016, citing alleged "irregularities" in their election, thereby preventing an opposition [[supermajority]] which would have been able to challenge Maduro.<ref name=NYTmuzzle/>

The TSJ granted Maduro more powers in 2017.<ref name=NYTmuzzle/> As [[2017 Venezuelan protests|protests mounted]], Maduro called a [[constituent assembly]] to rewrite the [[Constitution of Venezuela|1999 Venezuela Constitution]] created under [[Hugo Chávez]].<ref name=USAmay>{{cite news|title=Venezuela's embattled socialist president calls for citizens congress, new constitution|url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/world/2017/05/01/maduro-citizens-congress/101175468/|access-date=1 May 2017|newspaper=[[USA Today]]|agency=[[Associated Press]]|date=1 May 2017|archive-date=16 November 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191116080133/https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/world/2017/05/01/maduro-citizens-congress/101175468/|url-status=live}}</ref> Over 40 countries stated that they would not recognize the [[2017 Constituent National Assembly]] (ANC).<ref name=40nos>{{cite news|url=http://www.infobae.com/america/venezuela/2017/07/31/la-lista-de-los-40-paises-democraticos-que-hasta-el-momento-desconocieron-la-asamblea-constituyente-de-venezuela/|title=La lista de los 40 países democráticos que hasta el momento desconocieron la Asamblea Constituyente de Venezuela|date=31 July 2017|work=[[Infobae]]|access-date=1 August 2017|language=es-LA|archive-date=1 August 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170801050300/http://www.infobae.com/america/venezuela/2017/07/31/la-lista-de-los-40-paises-democraticos-que-hasta-el-momento-desconocieron-la-asamblea-constituyente-de-venezuela/|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name=VoteRigging>{{cite news|title=Venezuela: New assembly leader warns 'justice will come'|url=http://www.cnn.com/2017/08/04/americas/venezuela-assembly-first-day/index.html|date=4 August 2017|access-date=19 August 2017|archive-date=27 May 2023|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230527222851/https://www.cnn.com/2017/08/04/americas/venezuela-assembly-first-day/index.html|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|title=40 countries protest Venezuela's new assembly amid fraud accusations|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2017/aug/02/venezuela-voting-fraud-corruption-allegations-protests|access-date=4 August 2017|archive-date=14 April 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190414053444/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2017/aug/02/venezuela-voting-fraud-corruption-allegations-protests|url-status=live}}</ref> The opposition [[Democratic Unity Roundtable]] boycotted the election, saying that the ANC was "a trick to keep [the incumbent ruling party] in power";<ref name=Reuters-2017>{{Cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-venezuela-politics-idUSKBN18424I|title=Venezuela opposition boycotts meeting on Maduro assembly, clashes rage|date=8 April 2017|work=Reuters|access-date=7 August 2017|archive-date=4 September 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190904194556/https://www.reuters.com/article/us-venezuela-politics-idUSKBN18424I|url-status=live}}</ref> thus the coalition dominated by the [[United Socialist Party of Venezuela]] won almost all assembly seats.<ref name=Mogollon-2017>{{multiref|{{cite news|last1=Mogollon|first1=Mery|last2=Kraul|first2=Chris|title=As Venezuelan election nears, more upheaval and cries of fraud|url=http://www.latimes.com/world/mexico-americas/la-fg-venezuela-constitution-20170730-htmlstory.html|access-date=30 July 2017|work=[[The Los Angeles Times]]|date=29 July 2017|archive-date=3 August 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170803020957/http://www.latimes.com/world/mexico-americas/la-fg-venezuela-constitution-20170730-htmlstory.html|url-status=live}}|{{cite news|title=What are Venezuelans voting for and why is it so divisive?|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-latin-america-40704184|access-date=30 July 2017|work=BBC News|date=30 July 2017|archive-date=7 April 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190407075113/https://www.bbc.com/news/world-latin-america-40704184|url-status=live}}|{{Cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/venezuela-politics-idINKBN1AE0JM|title=Venezuelan opposition promises new tactics after Sunday's vote|last=Bronstein|first=Hugh|work=Reuters|date=29 July 2017|access-date=30 July 2017|archive-date=10 May 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190510175924/https://www.reuters.com/article/venezuela-politics-idINKBN1AE0JM|url-status=live}}}}</ref> On 8 August 2017, the ANC banned the National Assembly from performing actions that would interfere with the constituent assembly, effectively stripping the elected opposition-majority National Assembly of power.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Goodman|first1=Joshua|last2=Sanchez|first2=Fabiola|title=New Venezuela assembly declares itself superior government branch|url=http://www.chicagotribune.com/news/nationworld/ct-venezuela-political-assembly-20170808-story.html|access-date=9 August 2017|agency=Associated Press|newspaper=[[The Chicago Tribune]]|date=8 August 2017|archive-date=14 April 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190414150542/https://www.chicagotribune.com/news/nationworld/ct-venezuela-political-assembly-20170808-story.html|url-status=live}}</ref>

Scholars have argued that since [[Nicolás Maduro#Interim president|Maduro assumed the presidency]] in 2013, the nation has veered towards [[dictatorship]]. Maduro "consolidate[d] power" by creating an alternate legislative body (the 2017 ANC) to eliminate the National Assembly and then using a packed Supreme Court to sideline the legislature and bar the major opposition figures from the [[2018 Venezuelan presidential election]].<ref name=Turkewitz-2024a/><ref name=CRIES>{{cite journal|url=http://www.cries.org/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/PPN58-Digital.pdf#page=19|publisher= La Coordinadora Regional de Investigaciones Económicas y Sociales (CRIES)|pages=17–18|journal=Pensamiento Propio|date= July–December 2023|volume=28|title=Political Survival and... Authoritarian Consolidation? The Maduro Government and Venezuela's Political Crisis|first1=John |last1=Polga-Hecimovich|first2=Raúl |last2=Sánchez Urribarrí}}</ref><ref>{{cite journal |last=Corrales |first=Javier |date=3 July 2020 |title=Authoritarian survival: why Maduro hasn't fallen |url=https://cpo4303.info/assets/docs/why_Maduro_hasnt_fallen_2020.233145855.pdf |url-status=live |journal=[[Journal of Democracy]] |volume=31 |issue=3 |pages=39–53 |doi=10.1353/jod.2020.0044 |s2cid=226738491 |id={{ProQuest|2429461768}} |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230930195511/https://cpo4303.info/assets/docs/why_Maduro_hasnt_fallen_2020.233145855.pdf |archive-date=30 September 2023}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.populismstudies.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/ECPS-Leader-Profile-Series-5-2.pdf|pages=6–8|date=February 2021 |first=Imdat|last=Oner|title=Nicolas Maduro: A populist without popularity|publisher=European Center for Populism Studies}}</ref>

=== 2018 election and presidential crisis ===
{{Further|Venezuelan presidential crisis|Sanctions during the Venezuelan crisis}}

Maduro called for the [[2018 Venezuelan presidential election|2018 presidential election]] to occur months before the prescribed December date.<ref name=BBCweighs>{{cite news |title=Venezuela opposition weighs election run |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-latin-america-42984448 |work=BBC News |language=en-GB |date=8 February 2018 |access-date=8 February 2018 |archive-date=27 April 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190427225847/https://www.bbc.com/news/world-latin-america-42984448 |url-status=live }}</ref> He was declared the winner in May 2018 after multiple major opposition parties were banned from participating, among other irregularities.<ref name=ANCApproves>{{multiref|{{cite web |title=ANC aprobó un decreto para la validación de los partidos políticos |url=http://www.el-nacional.com/noticias/gobierno/anc-aprobo-decreto-para-validacion-los-partidos-politicos_216253 |website=El Nacional |language=es |date=20 December 2017 |access-date=25 May 2019 |archive-date=4 April 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230404012312/http://www.el-nacional.com/noticias/gobierno/anc-aprobo-decreto-para-validacion-los-partidos-politicos_216253 |url-status=live }}|{{Cite news |last=Olmo |first=Guillermo D. |date=10 January 2019 |title=Por qué es polémico que Maduro jure como presidente de Venezuela y por qué lo hace ahora si las elecciones fueron en mayo |url=https://www.bbc.com/mundo/noticias-america-latina-46805683 |website=BBC News Mundo |language=es |access-date=11 January 2019 |archive-date=27 April 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190427230023/https://www.bbc.com/mundo/noticias-america-latina-46805683 |url-status=live }}|{{cite web |title=Maduro gana con la abstención histórica más alta en comicios presidenciales |url=http://efectococuyo.com/politica/maduro-gana-con-la-abstencion-historica-mas-alta-en-comicios-presidenciales/ |website=Efecto Cocuyo |language=es |access-date=11 January 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181221101748/http://efectococuyo.com/politica/maduro-gana-con-la-abstencion-historica-mas-alta-en-comicios-presidenciales/ |archive-date=21 December 2018 |url-status=dead }}|{{cite web |title=Venezuela opposition banned from running in 2018 election |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-latin-america-42304594 |work=BBC News |language=en-GB |date=11 December 2017 |access-date=25 May 2019 |archive-date=14 February 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230214165554/https://www.bbc.com/news/world-latin-america-42304594 |url-status=live }}}}</ref> The election results were widely disputed both nationally and internationally,<ref name=ANCApproves/> and politicians considered him an ineffective dictator.<ref name=Corrales>{{multiref|{{cite web |last1=Corrales |first1=Javier |title=Venezuela's Odd Transition to Dictatorship |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161220103221/http://www.americasquarterly.org/content/venezuelas-odd-transition-dictatorship |archive-date=20 December 2016 |url-status=live}}|{{cite news |last1=Brodzinsky |first1=Sibylla |date=21 October 2016 |title=Venezuelans warn of 'dictatorship' after officials block bid to recall Maduro |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/oct/21/venezuela-president-maduro-recall-referendum |work=The Guardian |access-date=10 December 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161209230102/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/oct/21/venezuela-president-maduro-recall-referendum|archive-date=9 December 2016|url-status=live}}|{{cite news |title=Almagro: Maduro se transforma en dictador por negarles a venezolanos derecho a decidir su futuro |url=http://cnnespanol.cnn.com/2016/08/23/almagro-maduro-se-transforma-en-dictador-por-negarle-a-venezolanos-derecho-a-decidir-su-futuro/#0 |work=CNN en Español |language=es |date=24 August 2016 |access-date=10 December 2016 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161220135042/http://cnnespanol.cnn.com/2016/08/23/almagro-maduro-se-transforma-en-dictador-por-negarle-a-venezolanos-derecho-a-decidir-su-futuro/|archive-date=20 December 2016 |url-status=live}}}}</ref> In the months leading up to his 10 January 2019 inauguration, Maduro was pressured by international groups and other nations to step down; this pressure was increased after the new [[National Assembly (Venezuela)|National Assembly of Venezuela]] was sworn in on 5 January 2019.<ref>{{cite news |title=Venezuela Swears in an illegitimate President |url=https://www.ft.com/content/401e52a0-1405-11e9-a581-4ff78404524e |website=Financial Times |date=10 January 2019 |access-date=11 January 2019 |archive-date=20 September 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190920084639/https://www.ft.com/content/401e52a0-1405-11e9-a581-4ff78404524e |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name=HowDid>{{multiref|{{Cite news |last1=Herrero |first1=Ana Vanessa |last2=Specia |first2=Megan |date=10 January 2019 |title=Venezuela Is in Crisis. So How Did Maduro Secure a Second Term? |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/01/10/world/americas/venezuela-maduro-inauguration.html |work=The New York Times |issn=0362-4331 |language=en-US |access-date=11 January 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190111012015/https://www.nytimes.com/2019/01/10/world/americas/venezuela-maduro-inauguration.html |archive-date=11 January 2019|url-status=live}}|{{cite web |title=Peru, Paraguay recall diplomats over Maduro inauguration |url=https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2019/01/peru-paraguay-recall-diplomats-maduro-inauguration-190110180310100.html |website=Al Jazeera |language=en |date=10 January 2019 |access-date=11 January 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190110232447/https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2019/01/peru-paraguay-recall-diplomats-maduro-inauguration-190110180310100.html |archive-date=10 January 2019 |url-status=live}}}}</ref>

Maduro took [[Second inauguration of Nicolás Maduro|his official oath]] on 10 January 2019.<ref name=newtermoffical>{{cite web |title=Venezuela's Maduro begins second term |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-46821653 |website=BBC News |language=en-GB |date=10 January 2019 |access-date=4 December 2023 |archive-date=10 January 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190110231014/https://www.bbc.com/news/world-46821653 |url-status=live }}</ref> That same month, the National Assembly invoked clauses of the 1999 Venezuelan Constitution to install National Assembly Speaker [[Juan Guaidó]] as acting president, precipitating the [[Venezuelan presidential crisis]].<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://elpais.com/internacional/2019/01/24/actualidad/1548324278_362240.html|title=Los argumentos legales detrás de la batalla política|date=24 January 2019|work=El País|access-date=1 June 2019|language=es|issn=1134-6582}}</ref>

By January 2020, efforts led by Guaidó to create a transitional government had been unsuccessful and Maduro continued to control Venezuela's state institutions.<ref name=DWthousandsnovember>{{Cite web|date=16 November 2019|title=Venezuela: Thousands take to the streets of Caracas for rival protests|url=https://www.dw.com/en/venezuela-thousands-take-to-the-streets-of-caracas-for-rival-protests/a-51280074|access-date=4 December 2019|website=[[Deutsche Welle]]|language=en-GB|archive-date=4 December 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191204131921/https://www.dw.com/en/venezuela-thousands-take-to-the-streets-of-caracas-for-rival-protests/a-51280074|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name=AJnovGuaidocalls>{{Cite web|title=Venezuela: Rival rallies held as Guaido calls for daily protests|url=https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2019/11/venezuela-rival-rallies-held-guaido-calls-daily-protests-191117060107276.html|access-date=4 December 2019|website=[[Al Jazeera English|Al Jazeera]]|archive-date=2 December 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191202133038/https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2019/11/venezuela-rival-rallies-held-guaido-calls-daily-protests-191117060107276.html|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name=reutersmissedhismoment>{{Cite news|date=3 December 2019|title='Missed his moment': opposition corruption scandal undermines Venezuela's Guaido|language=en|work=[[Reuters]]|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-venezuela-politics-analysis-idUSKBN1Y72BB|access-date=4 December 2019|archive-date=4 December 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191204082956/https://www.reuters.com/article/us-venezuela-politics-analysis-idUSKBN1Y72BB|url-status=live}}</ref> In January 2021, the [[European Union]] stopped recognizing Guaidó as president, but still did not recognize Maduro as the legitimate president;<ref name=Emmott-2021>{{Cite news|last=Emmott|first=Robin|date=6 January 2021|title=EU no longer acknowledges Venezuela's Guaido as interim president|language=en|work=Reuters|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-venezuela-election-eu-idUSKBN29B2A9|access-date=7 January 2021|archive-date=19 November 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211119122244/https://www.reuters.com/article/us-venezuela-election-eu-idUSKBN29B2A9|url-status=live}}</ref> the [[European Parliament]] reaffirmed its recognition of Guaidó as president.<ref>{{Cite web |date=21 January 2021 |title=MEPs: Juan Guaidó is the legitimate interim President of Venezuela |url=https://www.europarl.europa.eu/news/en/press-room/20210114IPR95633/meps-juan-guaido-is-the-legitimate-interim-president-of-venezuela |access-date=21 January 2023 |website=[[European Parliament]] |archive-date=21 January 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230121164424/https://www.europarl.europa.eu/news/en/press-room/20210114IPR95633/meps-juan-guaido-is-the-legitimate-interim-president-of-venezuela |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |title=Juan Guaidó remains legitimate interim president, according to European Parliament |url=https://agenceurope.eu/en/bulletin/article/12641/9 |access-date=21 January 2023 |website=Agence Europe |archive-date=21 January 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230121163213/https://agenceurope.eu/en/bulletin/article/12641/9 |url-status=live }}</ref> After the announcement of regional elections in 2021, Guaidó proposed negotiations with Maduro with a schedule for free and fair elections in exchange for lifting [[International sanctions during the Venezuelan crisis|international sanctions]].<ref>{{Cite web|date=11 May 2021|title=Juan Guaidó abre la puerta a la negociación con Nicolás Maduro al invocar un acuerdo de salvación nacional|url=https://www.elmundo.es/internacional/2021/05/11/609ac387fc6c83506e8b460d.html|access-date=14 May 2021|website=[[El Mundo (Spain)|El Mundo]]|archive-date=18 February 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220218205303/https://www.elmundo.es/internacional/2021/05/11/609ac387fc6c83506e8b460d.html|url-status=live}}</ref>

In December 2022, three of the four main opposition political parties ([[Justice First]], [[Democratic Action (Venezuela)|Democratic Action]] and [[A New Era]]) backed and approved a reform to dissolve the interim government and create a commission of five members to manage foreign assets, as deputies sought a united strategy ahead of the 2024 elections,<ref>{{Cite news |last=Armas |first=Mayela |date=31 December 2022 |title=Venezuela opposition removes interim President Guaido |language=en |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuela-opposition-removes-interim-president-guaido-2022-12-31/ |access-date=31 December 2022 |archive-date=6 July 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230706001659/https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuela-opposition-removes-interim-president-guaido-2022-12-31/ |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |last=Martínez |first=Deisy |date=30 December 2022 |title=AN de 2015 aprueba su extensión por otro año y elimina gobierno interino |trans-title=2015 NA approves its extension for one more year and eliminates interim government |url=https://efectococuyo.com/politica/an-de-2015-aprueba-su-extension-por-un-ano-mas-y-elimina-gobierno-interino/ |access-date=31 December 2022 |website=[[Efecto Cocuyo]] |language=es |archive-date=30 December 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221230234206/https://efectococuyo.com/politica/an-de-2015-aprueba-su-extension-por-un-ano-mas-y-elimina-gobierno-interino/ |url-status=live }}</ref> stating that the interim government had failed to achieve its goals.<ref>{{Cite web |date=30 December 2022 |title=Mayoría de la AN-2015 ratifica disolución del Gobierno interino |url=https://talcualdigital.com/an-2015-debate-eliminacion-del-gobierno-interino-en-segunda-discusion/ |access-date=31 December 2022 |website=[[Tal Cual]] |language=es |quote=Hemos tenido algo que pasó de ser provisional a convertirse en algo perpetuo. Y no se celebraron las elecciones, de manera que el artículo 233 perdió su razón de ser para justificar el gobierno interino. |archive-date=30 December 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221230230840/https://talcualdigital.com/an-2015-debate-eliminacion-del-gobierno-interino-en-segunda-discusion/ |url-status=live }}</ref>

=== 2020 transitional government proposal ===
On 31 March 2020, the [[United States]] proposed a transitional government that would exclude both Maduro and Guaidó from the presidency.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Faiola|first1=Anthony|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/the_americas/us-proposes-transitional-government-for-venezuela-without-maduro-or-guaido/2020/03/31/8642a99a-7352-11ea-ad9b-254ec99993bc_story.html|title=U.S. proposes transitional government for Venezuela, without Maduro or Guaidó|date=31 March 2020|newspaper=[[The Washington Post]]|access-date=31 March 2020|last2=Morello|first2=Carol|archive-date=17 December 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211217221515/https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/the_americas/us-proposes-transitional-government-for-venezuela-without-maduro-or-guaido/2020/03/31/8642a99a-7352-11ea-ad9b-254ec99993bc_story.html|url-status=live}}</ref> The [[power-sharing]] deal provided for elections to be held within the year, and [[Foreign involvement in the Venezuelan presidential crisis|foreign militaries]], particularly Cuba and Russia, to leave the country. The US was seeking Maduro's arrest at the time of the announcement.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-52111805|title=US offers Venezuela deal to lift sanctions|date=31 March 2020|work=BBC News|access-date=31 March 2020|language=en-GB|archive-date=3 April 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200403204222/https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-52111805|url-status=live}}</ref> Experts stated that the deal explicitly mentioned who would lead a transitional government, something which stalled previous discussions, and coming shortly after the US indictment of Maduro, might pressure him to peacefully leave power.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Borger|first=Julian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/mar/31/venezuela-us-transition-plan-maduro-guaido|title=US calls on Maduro and Guaidó to stand down in Venezuela transition plan|date=31 March 2020|work=The Guardian|access-date=31 March 2020|language=en-GB|issn=0261-3077|archive-date=3 April 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200403205803/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/mar/31/venezuela-us-transition-plan-maduro-guaido|url-status=live}}</ref>

Guaidó accepted the proposal,<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.atlantico.net/articulo/mundo/guaido-acepta-gobierno-transicion-propone-eeuu/20200401004816766792.html|title=Guaidó acepta el gobierno de transición que propone EEUU|date=1 April 2020|website=Atlántico|language=es|access-date=10 April 2020|archive-date=15 July 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210715165523/https://www.atlantico.net/articulo/mundo/guaido-acepta-gobierno-transicion-propone-eeuu/20200401004816766792.html|url-status=live}}</ref> while Venezuela's foreign minister, [[Jorge Arreaza]], rejected it and declared that only the [[2020 Venezuelan parliamentary election|parliamentary election]] would take place in 2020.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.europapress.es/internacional/noticia-arreaza-rechaza-propuesta-eeuu-transicion-democratica-venezuela-20200331184928.html|title=Arreaza rechaza la propuesta de EEUU para una "transición democrática" en Venezuela|date=31 March 2020|website=[[Europa Press (news agency)|Europa Press]]|language=es|access-date=1 April 2020|archive-date=15 July 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210715032208/https://www.europapress.es/internacional/noticia-arreaza-rechaza-propuesta-eeuu-transicion-democratica-venezuela-20200331184928.html|url-status=live}}</ref>

== Opposition primaries launched==
{{Main|2023 Unitary Platform presidential primaries}}
In November 2022, [[Diosdado Cabello]], vice-president of the PSUV and president of the ANC, insisted that the presidential election be moved forward to the first semester of 2023.<ref>{{Cite web |date=5 November 2022 |title=Diosdado Cabello insistió en la posibilidad de adelantar las elecciones presidenciales para 2023 |trans-title=Diosdado Cabello insisted on the possibility of advancing the presidential election to 2023 |url=https://www.elnacional.com/venezuela/diosdado-cabello-insistio-en-adelantar-las-elecciones-presidenciales-para-2023/ |access-date=12 November 2022 |website=[[El Nacional (Venezuela)|El Nacional]] |language=es |archive-date=5 November 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221105143010/https://www.elnacional.com/venezuela/diosdado-cabello-insistio-en-adelantar-las-elecciones-presidenciales-para-2023/ |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 16 May 2023, the Unitary Platform announced it would hold a primary to elect a single candidate for the presidential election, the [[2023 Unitary Platform presidential primaries]], on 22 October 2023. On 24 July 2023, the application period ended, with 14 candidates registered.<ref name=BloombergSecondBulletin/><ref>{{cite web|access-date=21 October 2023|date=27 May 2023|language=es|title=Venezolanos podrán votar en 80 ciudades de 31 países en la primaria opositora|url=https://www.vozdeamerica.com/a/venezuela-voto-extranjero-primaria-80-ciudades-31-paises-/7111826.html|website=Voz de América|archive-date=13 June 2023|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230613170442/https://www.vozdeamerica.com/a/venezuela-voto-extranjero-primaria-80-ciudades-31-paises-/7111826.html|url-status=live}}</ref>

=== Disqualification of Machado and Capriles ===
On 30 June 2023, the {{ill|Comptroller General of the Republic of Venezuela|es|Contraloría General de la República (Venezuela)}} announced that former [[National Assembly of Venezuela|National Assembly]] member [[María Corina Machado]] was disqualified from holding public office for 15 years, claiming she was linked to alleged crimes committed by [[Juan Guaidó]] and had supported [[International sanctions during the Venezuelan crisis|international sanctions against Venezuela]]. She would be allowed to participate in the opposition primaries because they were not regulated by Maduro's government.<ref name="candidate Machado">{{Cite news |last1=Armas |first1=Mayela |last2=Sequera |first2=Vivian |date=30 June 2023 |title=Venezuela opposition candidate Machado barred from holding office-gov't |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuela-opposition-candidate-machado-barred-holding-office-govt-2023-06-30/ |access-date=30 June 2023 |archive-date=30 June 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230630171330/https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuela-opposition-candidate-machado-barred-holding-office-govt-2023-06-30/ |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|access-date=10 July 2023|date=30 June 2023|first=Luna|language=es|last=Perdomo|title=José Brito: Contraloría inhabilitó a María Corina Machado por 15 años|url=https://talcualdigital.com/jose-brito-contraloria-inhabilito-a-maria-corina-machado-por-15-anos/|website=[[Tal Cual]]|archive-date=10 July 2023|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230710151421/https://talcualdigital.com/jose-brito-contraloria-inhabilito-a-maria-corina-machado-por-15-anos/|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|access-date=10 July 2023|date=30 June 2023|first=Ronny|language=es|last=Rodríguez|title=Contraloría inhabilita a María Corina Machado por 15 años, dice José Brito|url=https://efectococuyo.com/politica/contraloria-inhabilita-a-maria-corina-machado-por-15-anos-dice-jose-brito/|website=[[Efecto Cocuyo]]|archive-date=10 July 2023|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230710151426/https://efectococuyo.com/politica/contraloria-inhabilita-a-maria-corina-machado-por-15-anos-dice-jose-brito/|url-status=live}}</ref> Capriles was given the same sentence and barred from holding office until 2032.<ref name="candidate Machado" /> Analysts stated that the accusations were incoherent, as Machado was not a member of the 2015 opposition National Assembly with Guaidó, having been disqualified by the Comptroller's Office, nor had she served in his government.<ref>{{cite web|access-date=12 July 2023|language=es|title=Los cinco vicios que hacen nula la inhabilitación de María Corina Machado|url=https://accesoalajusticia.org/cinco-vicios-hacen-nula-inhabilitacion-maria-corina-machado/|website=Acceso a la Justicia|archive-date=12 July 2023|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230712235041/https://accesoalajusticia.org/cinco-vicios-hacen-nula-inhabilitacion-maria-corina-machado/|url-status=live}}</ref> The disqualification was considered illegal and unconstitutional by several jurists, including constitutional lawyer {{Ill|Allan Brewer Carías|es}} and the [[Latin American and Caribbean Network for Democracy]].<ref>{{cite web|access-date=10 July 2023|language=es-CO|title=Alerta Venezuela: Inhabilitación inconstitucional de la candidata de la oposición María Corina Machado manipula elecciones en Venezuela|url=https://redlad.org/alerta-inhabilitacion-inconstitucional-de-la-candidata-de-la-oposicion-maria-corina-machado-manipula-elecciones-en-venezuela/|website=REDLAD|archive-date=10 July 2023|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230710152927/https://redlad.org/alerta-inhabilitacion-inconstitucional-de-la-candidata-de-la-oposicion-maria-corina-machado-manipula-elecciones-en-venezuela/|url-status=live}}</ref>

Machado's disqualification from holding office was pending a court decision<ref name=Armas2023>{{Cite news |last1=Armas |first1=Mayela |last2=Sequera |first2=Vivian |date=30 June 2023 |title=Venezuela opposition candidate Machado barred from holding office-gov't |language=en |work=Reuters |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuela-opposition-candidate-machado-barred-holding-office-govt-2023-06-30/ |access-date=30 June 2023 |archive-date=30 June 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230630171330/https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuela-opposition-candidate-machado-barred-holding-office-govt-2023-06-30/ |url-status=live }}</ref> when a debate was held on 12 July 2023 between eight of the thirteen opposition pre-candidates: Machado for [[Come Venezuela|Vente Venezuela]], {{ill|Carlos Prosperi|es}} for [[Democratic Action (Venezuela)|Democratic Action]], [[Freddy Superlano]] for [[Popular Will]], transgender candidate [[Tamara Adrián]] for Unidos por la Dignidad, [[Delsa Solórzano]] for Encuentro Ciudadano, [[Andrés Velásquez]] for [[Radical Cause|La Causa R]], [[César Pérez Vivas]] for Concertación Ciudadana and Andrés Caleca for Movimiento por Venezuela.<ref>{{Cite web |date=12 July 2023 |title=¡Histórico! Tuvieron que pasar 11 años para que se volviera a celebrar un debate electoral en Venezuela |url=https://expansion.mx/mundo/2023/07/12/venezuela-celebra-su-primer-debate-electoral-opositor-en-11-anos |access-date=13 July 2023 |website=Expansión |language=es |archive-date=13 July 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230713011622/https://expansion.mx/mundo/2023/07/12/venezuela-celebra-su-primer-debate-electoral-opositor-en-11-anos |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |date=12 July 2023 |title=Venezuela: ocho candidatos opositores realizaron el primer debate antes de las primarias |url=https://www.france24.com/es/am%C3%A9rica-latina/20230712-venezuela-ocho-candidatos-opositores-realizaron-el-primer-debate-antes-de-las-primarias |access-date=13 July 2023 |website=[[France24]] |archive-date=12 July 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230712234153/https://www.france24.com/es/am%C3%A9rica-latina/20230712-venezuela-ocho-candidatos-opositores-realizaron-el-primer-debate-antes-de-las-primarias |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |date=12 July 2023 |title=Hablan los candidatos: vea en vivo el debate de los opositores en la UCAB |work=[[El Nacional (Venezuela)|El Nacional]] |url=https://www.elnacional.com/venezuela/politica/hablan-los-candidatos-vea-en-vivo-el-debate-de-los-opositores-en-la-ucab/ |access-date=16 July 2023 |archive-date=12 July 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230712225320/https://www.elnacional.com/venezuela/politica/hablan-los-candidatos-vea-en-vivo-el-debate-de-los-opositores-en-la-ucab/ |url-status=live }}</ref>

=== Harassment and intimidation during primaries===
Pro-government militants tried to attack Machado during a 15 July campaign in [[Vargas (state)|Vargas]] and prevented a campaign rally in [[Petare]] the next day.<ref>{{Cite web |date=14 July 2023 |title=Chavistas intentaron agredir a María Corina Machado cuando se trasladaba a un acto de campaña en el estado La Guaira |url=https://www.ntn24.com/noticias-politica/chavistas-intentaron-agredir-a-maria-corina-machado-cuando-se-trasladaba-a-un-acto-de-campana-en-el-estado-la-guaira-431419 |access-date=26 July 2023 |website=[[NTN24]] |language=es |archive-date=26 July 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230726122652/https://www.ntn24.com/noticias-politica/chavistas-intentaron-agredir-a-maria-corina-machado-cuando-se-trasladaba-a-un-acto-de-campana-en-el-estado-la-guaira-431419 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |title=Turba chavista impidió acto de María Corina Machado en Petare, al este de Caracas |url=https://www.ntn24.com/noticias-politica/turba-chavista-impidio-acto-de-maria-corina-machado-en-petare-al-este-de-caracas-431602 |access-date=26 July 2023 |website=[[NTN24]] |language=es |archive-date=26 July 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230726122651/https://www.ntn24.com/noticias-politica/turba-chavista-impidio-acto-de-maria-corina-machado-en-petare-al-este-de-caracas-431602 |url-status=live }}</ref> On 22 July, [[Vente Venezuela]] denounced death threats to Machado by the [[National Liberation Army (Colombia)|National Liberation Army]] (ELN), a far-left Colombian guerrilla group, after her campaign headquarters in [[Táchira]] state were painted with messages of "death to María Corina" signed by the ELN. The group denied being the author of the threats.<ref>{{Cite web |date=22 July 2023 |title=Urgente: ELN amenaza de muerte a María Corina Machado en Venezuela: le exigen que se aparte de las elecciones primarias |url=https://www.semana.com/mundo/articulo/eln-amenaza-de-muerte-en-venezuela-a-maria-corina-machado-le-piden-que-se-aparte-de-las-elecciones-primarias/202306/ |access-date=26 July 2023 |website=[[Semana]] |language=es |archive-date=26 July 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230726122646/https://www.semana.com/mundo/articulo/eln-amenaza-de-muerte-en-venezuela-a-maria-corina-machado-le-piden-que-se-aparte-de-las-elecciones-primarias/202306/ |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |date=26 July 2023 |title=ELN niega autoría en grafitis que aparecieron en una sede de María Corina Machado |url=https://www.elnacional.com/venezuela/eln-niega-autoria-en-grafitis-que-aparecieron-en-una-sede-de-maria-corina-machado/ |access-date=10 August 2023 |archive-date=26 July 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230726132851/https://www.elnacional.com/venezuela/eln-niega-autoria-en-grafitis-que-aparecieron-en-una-sede-de-maria-corina-machado/ |url-status=live }}</ref>

Venezuelan fact checking outlet {{ill|Cazadores de Fake News|es}} published information relating to an operation to discredit Machado, carried out by a disinformation network which had formerly spread disinformation about [[Leopoldo López]], [[Juan Guaidó]] and other opposition politicians.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Alerta: hay una operación de influencia en contra de @MariaCorinaYA en curso. (...) |url=https://twitter.com/cazamosfakenews/status/1678486166876585985 |access-date=26 July 2023 |website=[[Twitter]] |language=es |publication-date=10 July 2023 |archive-date=29 October 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20231029021225/https://twitter.com/cazamosfakenews/status/1678486166876585985 |url-status=live }}</ref>

[[Henrique Capriles]] said he was physically assaulted in June by individuals associated with the ruling party.<ref>{{cite web|date=3 June 2023|title=El antichavista Henrique Capriles es agredido durante visita en el centro de Venezuela|url=https://www.swissinfo.ch/spa/venezuela-oposici%C3%B3n_el-antichavista-henrique-capriles-es-agredido-durante-visita-en-el-centro-de-venezuela/48563244|website=Swissinfo|access-date=17 June 2023|archive-date=27 October His followers said Chavistas attacked Capriles supporters at an August rally, which they said was the seventh aggression since 29 May.<ref>{{cite news|access-date=6 September 2023|date=15 August 2023|periodical=[[El Nacional (Venezuela)|El Nacional]]|title=Simpatizantes del chavismo agredieron a seguidores de Henrique Capriles durante un acto en Apure|url=https://www.elnacional.com/venezuela/simpatizantes-del-chavismo-agredieron-a-seguidores-de-henrique-capriles-durante-un-acto-en-apure/|archive-date=15 August On 27 July, [[Popular Will]] denounced that [[Freddy Superlano]]'s passport was confiscated by authorities at the Colombian border.<ref>{{cite news|access-date=6 September 2023|date=27 July [[Delsa Solórzano]] complained in August of death threats, including messages on social media such as "the collective forces of the ELN are going to kill you".<ref>{{cite news|access-date=6 September 2023|date=14 August 2023|periodical=[[El Nacional (Venezuela)|El Nacional]]|title=La Fiscalía investigará amenazas de muerte contra Delsa Solórzano|url=https://www.elnacional.com/venezuela/la-fiscalia-investigara-amenazas-de-muerte-contra-delsa-solorzano/|archive-date=15 August 2023|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230815221838/https://www.elnacional.com/venezuela/la-fiscalia-investigara-amenazas-de-muerte-contra-delsa-solorzano/|url-status=live}}</ref>

On the morning of the 22 October primary, in Caracas, [[Colectivo (Venezuela)|colectivos]] prevented the installation of a voting center and violence with a firearm was registered.<ref>{{cite news|access-date=22 October 2023|periodical=[[El Carabobeño]]|title=Colectivos impiden instalar centros de votación en el Guarataro, denounced that voters were threatened by colectivos, and that a voting center had to be moved.<ref>{{cite web|date=22 October 2023|first=Raylí|last=Luján|title=Elección primaria en Venezuela: Así transcurrió la jornada para definir un candidato único opositor|url=https://www.bloomberglinea.com/latinoamerica/venezuela/en-vivo-eleccion-primaria-en-venezuela-minuto-a-minuto-se-definira-candidato-unico-opositor/|website=[[Bloomberg News|Bloomberg Línea]]|access-date=23 October 2023|archive-date=23 October 2023|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20231023102246/https://www.bloomberglinea.com/latinoamerica/venezuela/en-vivo-eleccion-primaria-en-venezuela-minuto-a-minuto-se-definira-candidato-unico-opositor/|url-status=live}}</ref> Armed civilians entered a voting point and pointed at the coordinator, firing several shots.<ref name="Ramírez-2023">{{cite web|date=22 October 2023|first1=Lucía Fernanda|last1=Ramírez|first2=Norma|last2=Rivas|title=En el municipio Sucre inicio de la elección primaria fluyó a pesar de las trabas de funcionarios y 2023|archive-date=23 October Motorcyclists threw a tear gas cannister in the vicinity of a voting center,<ref>{{cite web|date=22 October 2023|language=es|title=Motorizados lanzan lacrimógena en centro de votación en Caracas, electores vuelven a la fila|url=https://elpitazo.net/gran-caracas/primaria-motorizados-lanzan-lacrimogena-en-centro-de-votacion-en-caracas-electores-vuelven-a-la-fila/|website=[[El Pitazo]]|access-date=23 October 2023|archive-date=23 October 2023|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20231023102251/https://elpitazo.net/gran-caracas/primaria-motorizados-lanzan-lacrimogena-en-centro-de-votacion-en-caracas-electores-vuelven-a-la-fila/|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite and two men fired shots into the air at another voting center.<ref name="Ramírez-2023"/>

The vice-president of the Regional Board of [[Monagas]] state, Dexcy Moya, denounced that colectivos shouted expletives and threats in several voting centers in [[Maturín|Maturin]].<ref>{{cite web|access-date=23 October 2023|title=Primaria en Oriente: Electores reportaron lentitud en la jornada|url=https://elpitazo.net/oriente/primaria-en-oriente-alta-participacion-de-electores-durante-la-tarde/amp/|website=[[El Pitazo]]|archive-date=23 October 2023|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20231023102255/https://elpitazo.net/oriente/primaria-en-oriente-alta-participacion-de-electores-durante-la-tarde/amp/|url-status=live}}</ref>

=== Exclusion of Machado and broken 2023 deal ===
{{further|Barbados Agreement|U.S. sanctions during the Venezuelan crisis}}
[[File:Tarek William Saab como defensor del pueblo.jpg|thumb|[[Tarek William Saab]], Venezuela's Prosecutor General]]
[[María Corina Machado]] won the October [[2023 Unitary Platform presidential primaries|2023 Unitary Platform primary]] by a landslide.<ref name=MachadoWinner>{{cite web | last=Garcia Cano | first=Regina | title=María Corina Machado is winner of Venezuela opposition primary that the government has denounced | website=Associated Press | date=26 October 2023 | url=https://apnews.com/article/venezuela-opposition-primary-machado-winner-5d3c4c4b9a4cd42f52729fc0e798954f | access-date=8 May 2024 | archive-date=11 May 2024 | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240511030721/https://apnews.com/article/venezuela-opposition-primary-machado-winner-5d3c4c4b9a4cd42f52729fc0e798954f | url-status=live }}</ref>

In October 2023, the Maduro government and representatives of the opposition signed the [[Barbados Agreement]]. Both parties agreed to hold free and fair elections, and accept their results, in exchange for [[U.S. sanctions during the Venezuelan crisis#Petroleum|sanctions imposed by the US on petroleum sales]] to be eased.<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Spetalnick |first1=Matt |last2=Parraga |first2=Marianna |date=19 October 2023 |title=US broadly eases Venezuela oil sanctions after election deal |language=en |work=Reuters |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/us-easing-venezuela-oil-sanctions-response-election-deal-official-2023-10-18/ |access-date=11 July 2024 |archive-date=19 October 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20231019012345/https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/us-easing-venezuela-oil-sanctions-response-election-deal-official-2023-10-18/ |url-status=live }}</ref> Despite the agreement, Machado's disqualification was confirmed by the TSJ in January 2024.<ref name=lemonde270124>{{cite web |title=Venezuela's Supreme Court disqualifies opposition leader from running for president |url=https://www.lemonde.fr/en/international/article/2024/01/27/venezuela-s-supreme-court-disqualifies-opposition-leader-from-running-for-president_6469941_4.html |website=Le Monde.fr |publisher=AFP |access-date=8 March 2024 |language=en |date=27 January 2024 |archive-date=27 March 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240327102951/https://www.lemonde.fr/en/international/article/2024/01/27/venezuela-s-supreme-court-disqualifies-opposition-leader-from-running-for-president_6469941_4.html |url-status=live }}</ref>

Following poor turnout in the [[2023 Venezuelan referendum]], the chief prosecutor of Venezuela, [[Tarek William Saab]], accused [[Venezuelan opposition|opposition]] leaders of sabotaging the referendum and issued [[arrest warrant]]s for 15 of them, with charges such as treason and conspiracy.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2023/12/06/world/americas/venezuela-opposition-arrest-orders.html |title=Venezuela Orders Arrest of Top Opposition Figures, Claiming Treason |newspaper=The New York Times |author1=Genevieve Glatsky |author2=Isayen Herrera |date=6 December 2023 |access-date=7 December 2023 |archive-date=14 December 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20231214092211/https://www.nytimes.com/2023/12/06/world/americas/venezuela-opposition-arrest-orders.html?searchResultPosition=2 |url-status=live }}</ref> Saab—under [[Venezuelan sanctions|sanctions for multiple alleged offenses]]—is charged by human rights organizations as "being one of the key people in the regime's efforts to use the Venezuelan justice system as an instrument of political persecution", according to an August 2024 ''Miami Herald'' article.<ref name=MHCouldCharge/>

Machado and her supporters said they were attacked by [[Colectivo (Venezuela)|colectivos]] during a February 2024 campaign rally in [[Charallave]], [[Miranda (state)|Miranda state]]. Machado denounced that the attack occurred in front of security officials, who did not intervene.<ref>{{Cite news |date=8 February 2024 |title=María Corina Machado denunció ante el mundo el violento ataque que sufrió en Charallave |trans-title=María Corina Machado denounced the violent attack she suffered in Charallave to the world |url=https://www.elnacional.com/venezuela/maria-corina-machado-denuncio-ante-el-mundo-el-violento-ataque-que-sufrio-en-charallave/ |work=[[El Nacional (Venezuela)|El Nacional]] |language=es |access-date=9 February 2024 |archive-date=8 February 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240208123411/https://www.elnacional.com/venezuela/maria-corina-machado-denuncio-ante-el-mundo-el-violento-ataque-que-sufrio-en-charallave/ |url-status=live }}</ref> With the main opposition candidate banned from running, the US stated that Maduro's government had "fallen short" on its commitments, and [[U.S. sanctions during the Venezuelan crisis#2022–2024: sanctions relief|reinstated some sanctions]] in April 2024.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.ft.com/content/85a4e5b9-c536-4bfb-8dee-32bbed60311e | title=US reimposes oil sanctions on Venezuela after broken election promises | access-date=11 July 2024 | archive-date=11 July 2024 | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240711230348/https://www.ft.com/content/85a4e5b9-c536-4bfb-8dee-32bbed60311e | url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news | url=https://www.nytimes.com/2024/04/17/world/americas/us-oil-sanctions-venezuela-maduro.html | title=U.S. Restores Oil Sanctions on Venezuela as Hopes Dim for Free Election | work=The New York Times | date=17 April 2024 | last1=Glatsky | first1=Genevieve | access-date=11 July 2024 | archive-date=11 July 2024 | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240711230348/https://www.nytimes.com/2024/04/17/world/americas/us-oil-sanctions-venezuela-maduro.html | url-status=live }}</ref>

Organizations such as the [[United Nations]], the [[Organization of American States]], the [[European Union]], and [[Human Rights Watch]] along with several countries and their leaders rejected or condemned Machado's disqualification.<ref>{{cite news |date=8 July 2023 |title=¿Cómo ha sido el apoyo de la comunidad internacional a María Corina Machado? |periodical=[[El Nacional (Venezuela)|El Nacional]] |url=https://www.elnacional.com/venezuela/como-ha-sido-el-apoyo-de-la-comunidad-internacional-a-maria-corina-machado/ |access-date=12 July 2023 |archive-date=9 July 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230709215845/https://www.elnacional.com/venezuela/como-ha-sido-el-apoyo-de-la-comunidad-internacional-a-maria-corina-machado/ |url-status=live |language= es |trans-title=How has the international community supported María Corina Machado?}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |last=Maza |first=Jesús |date=4 July 2023 |title=Mercosur: Luis Lacalle pide 'alzar la voz' por la inhabilitación de María Corina Machado |trans-title=Mercosur: Luis Lacalle asks to 'raise our voices' for the disqualification of María Corina Machado|url=https://larepublica.pe/mundo/venezuela/2023/07/04/mercosur-luis-lacalle-pide-alzar-la-voz-por-la-inhabilitacion-de-maria-corina-machado-lacalle-pou-cumbre-mercosur-en-vivo-lacalle-defiende-a-maria-corina-machado-uruguay-venezuela-lrtmv-259416 |access-date=10 July 2023 |website=[[La República (Peru)|La República]] |location=Lima |language=es |archive-date=29 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240729022911/https://larepublica.pe/mundo/venezuela/2023/07/04/mercosur-luis-lacalle-pide-alzar-la-voz-por-la-inhabilitacion-de-maria-corina-machado-lacalle-pou-cumbre-mercosur-en-vivo-lacalle-defiende-a-maria-corina-machado-uruguay-venezuela-lrtmv-259416 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite web |date=4 July 2023 |title=Presidente de Paraguay denuncia veto a María Corina Machado |url=https://www.diariolasamericas.com/videos/presidente-paraguay-denuncia-veto-maria-corina-machado-n5338866 |access-date=10 July 2023 |website=[[Diario Las Américas]] |language=es-US === Election dates and new law ===
The presidential election was scheduled to be held in 2024; according to the Venezuelan Constitution, presidential elections are to take place no later than December in the election year.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Singer |first=Florantonia |author-link=Florantonia Singer |date=18 October 2023 |title=El chavismo y la oposición acuerdan celebrar las elecciones presidenciales en el segundo semestre de 2024 |url=https://elpais.com/america/2023-10-18/el-chavismo-y-la-oposicion-acuerdan-celebrar-las-elecciones-presidenciales-en-el-segundo-semestre-de-2024.html |access-date=23 November 2023 |website=[[El País]] |language=es |archive-date=23 November 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20231123053506/https://elpais.com/america/2023-10-18/el-chavismo-y-la-oposicion-acuerdan-celebrar-las-elecciones-presidenciales-en-el-segundo-semestre-de-2024.html |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |last=Olloqui |first=Álvaro |date=18 October 2023 |title=Maduro acuerda con la oposición la celebración de elecciones presidenciales en 2024 |url=https://www.larazon.es/internacional/maduro-acuerda-oposicion-celebracion-elecciones-presidenciales-2024_20231018652f829c8160fc00013a8690.html |access-date=23 November 2023 |website=[[La Razón (Madrid)|La Razón]] |language=es |archive-date=23 November 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20231123082202/https://www.larazon.es/internacional/maduro-acuerda-oposicion-celebracion-elecciones-presidenciales-2024_20231018652f829c8160fc00013a8690.html |url-status=live }}</ref>

The [[National Electoral Council (Venezuela)|National Election Council]] (CNE) announced on 5 March 2024, the date of [[Hugo Chávez]]'s death, that the election would be held on 28 July, the day that would have been his 70th birthday,<ref name=ChavezBirthday>{{cite news|url=https://elpais.com/america/2024-03-05/venezuela-anuncia-la-celebracion-de-elecciones-para-el-28-de-julio-el-dia-del-nacimiento-de-chavez.html|work=El País|date=5 March 2024|access-date=24 August 2024|language=es|title=Venezuela celebrará las elecciones presidenciales el 28 de julio, el día del nacimiento de Chávez|trans-title=Venezuela will hold presidential elections on July 28, Chavez's birthday|author=Quesada, Juan Diego }}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.dw.com/es/elecciones-presidenciales-de-venezuela-ser%C3%A1n-el-28-de-julio/a-68449063 |title=Elecciones |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240305212508/https://www.dw.com/es/elecciones-presidenciales-de-venezuela-ser%C3%A1n-el-28-de-julio/a-68449063 |url-status=live }}</ref> with filing of candidacies taking place from 21 to 25 March<ref name="f24">{{cite web |date=12 March 2024 |title=Venezuela's Maduro selected as ruling party election candidate |url=https://www.france24.com/en/americas/20240312-venezuela-s-maduro-selected-as-ruling-party-election-candidate |access-date=12 March 2024 |website=France 24 |language=en |archive-date=12 March 2024 campaigning from 4 to 25 July.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://apnews.com/article/venezuela-presidential-election-july-28-fb270567897dbc2641e2062c3e877ce2 |title=Venezuela sets its presidential election On 2 April, [[Delcy Rodríguez]] presented the [[Law against Fascism, Neofascism and Similar Expressions]] to the Maduro-controlled [[V National Assembly of Venezuela]];<ref name= Itriago2April>{{cite === Negotiations with United States ===
{{Further|Foreign policy of the United States}}
Direct talks between senior Venezuelan and United States officials that had been stalled since mid-April were restarted in early July, a few weeks prior to the election.<ref name="l494">{{cite web | last=Garcia Cano | first=Regina | title=Venezuela's opposition coalition welcomes President Maduro's plan to jumpstart dialogue with the US | website=Associated Press | date=2 July 2024 | url=https://apnews.com/article/venezuela-maduro-opposition-machado-ac96fd2f93a5a8d702e7e8a905f1ca29 | access-date=6 July 2024 | archive-date=14 July 2024 | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240714135312/https://apnews.com/article/venezuela-maduro-opposition-machado-ac96fd2f93a5a8d702e7e8a905f1ca29 | url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="l525">{{cite web | author1=Vivian Sequera | author2=Matt Spetalnick | title=US resumes talks with Venezuela, pushes for fair July 28 election | website=Reuters | date=3 July 2024 | url=https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuela-us-conclude-virtual-meeting-pledging-constructive-talks-2024-07-03/ | access-date=6 July 2024 | archive-date=5 July 2024 | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240705003004/https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuela-us-conclude-virtual-meeting-pledging-constructive-talks-2024-07-03/ | url-status=live }}</ref><ref name= WPBidenDeal>{{cite news |last1=Herrero |first1=Ana Vanessa |last2=Schmidt |first2=Samantha |last3=DeYoung |first3=Karen |title=Biden made a bold deal with Venezuela's strongman. Will it pay off? |newspaper=[[Washington Post]] |date=15 July 2024 |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2024/07/15/venezuela-election-maduro-biden-deal/ |access-date=29 July 2024 |archive-date=15 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240715122425/https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2024/07/15/venezuela-election-maduro-biden-deal/ |url-status=live }}</ref>  According to ''The Washington Post'', the US had been willing to remove {{em|all}} sanctions if [[Barbados Agreement]] conditions were met, but the Maduro-controlled Venezuelan Supreme Court made Machado ineligible for the presidency in January 2024.<ref name=WPBidenDeal/> The opposition was not included in the negotiations. Former US ambassador to Venezuela Bill Brownfield stated that the US deal was "looser than it should have been" and "Maduro got, front-ended, all of the benefits he was supposed to get in exchange for promises to comply with in the future. He didn't comply, but he got the stuff he really wanted."<ref name= WPBidenDeal/> Several proposals to grant immunity to the loser of the election have been proposed; while the US restarted talks in the hope of furthering a fair election, the opposition held out "that a strong showing will force Maduro to the table".<ref name= WPBidenDeal/>

== Electoral process ==
{{See also|Elections in Venezuela#Polling procedure}}

The [[President of Venezuela]] is elected by plurality in a single round of voting.<ref>[http://www.electionguide.org/elections/id/2248/ Bolivarian Republic of Venezuela] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180515112333/http://www.electionguide.org/elections/id/2248/ |date=15 May 2018 }} IFES</ref> On 5 March 2024, the [[National Electoral Council (Venezuela)|National Electoral Council]] (CNE) set the presidential election for 28 July and set the electoral schedule:<ref>{{cite web |author=Pablo Zapata |date=6 June 2024 |title=Cronograma electoral CNE 2024: revisa plazos y fechas de las elecciones presidenciales en Venezuela |url=https://larepublica.pe/mundo/venezuela/2024/03/06/cronograma-electoral-cne-2024-revisa-plazos-y-fechas-de-las-elecciones-presidenciales-en-venezuela-lrtmv-425352 |access-date=17 March 2024 |archive-date=11 March 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240311095531/https://larepublica.pe/mundo/venezuela/2024/03/06/cronograma-electoral-cne-2024-revisa-plazos-y-fechas-de-las-elecciones-presidenciales-en-venezuela-lrtmv-425352 |url-status=live }}<!-- auto-translated from Spanish by Module:CS1 translator --></ref>
