Venezuelan elections are overseen by the CNE, with poll workers drafted via a lottery of registered voters. Polling places are equipped with multiple high-tech [[Touchscreen|touch-screen]] [[DRE voting machine]]s, one to a ''"mesa electoral"'', or voting "table". After the vote is cast, each machine prints out a [[paper ballot]], also known as a [[voter-verified paper audit trail]], which is inspected by the voter and deposited in a ballot box at the machine's table. The voting machines perform in a stand-alone fashion, disconnected from any network until the polls close.<ref name=manual>[http://www.cne.gov.ve/elecciones/presidencial2006/documentos/ManualPresidencial2006.zip Manual Operativo para Miembros, Secretaria o Secretario de Mesa Electoral] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070927013043/http://www.cne.gov.ve/elecciones/presidencial2006/documentos/ManualPresidencial2006.zip|date=27 September 2007}} Consejo Nacional Electoral. Retrieved 28 November 2006 {{in lang|es}}</ref><ref name=APPaperSheets>{{cite news |url= https://apnews.com/world-news/general-news-24358044cea98b3ce4f6a316bdbd3508 |work = [[Associated Press]] |date= 30 July 2024 |access-date= 30 July 2024| title= Little-known paper sheets are key to declaring victory in Venezuela's election|archive-url=https://archive.today/20240730221113/https://apnews.com/world-news/general-news-24358044cea98b3ce4f6a316bdbd3508|archive-date=30 July 2024|url-status=live}}</ref> Voting session closure at each voting station is determined either by the lack of voters after the lines have emptied, or by the hour, at the discretion of the president of the voting table.{{Citation needed|date=September 2023}}

=== Poll witnesses ===
Venezuelan law provides for representatives to observe at each voting place; anyone can witness the electoral process.<ref name= BBCStayinPower/> Each machine prints tally sheets (''actas de escrutinio'' or ''actas''<ref name=Actas>{{cite news |url= https://cnnespanol.cnn.com/2024/07/29/como-es-sistema-conteo-verificacion-votos-venezuela-orix/ |publisher= CNN en espanol |date= 29 July 2024 |access-date= 30 July 2024 |title= ¿Cómo es el sistema de conteo y verificación de votos en Venezuela? |language= es |trans-title= What is the vote counting and verification system in Venezuela? |archive-date= 29 July 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240729201452/https://cnnespanol.cnn.com/2024/07/29/como-es-sistema-conteo-verificacion-votos-venezuela-orix/ |url-status= live }}</ref>) after the polls close, showing how many votes were received by each candidate, and representatives of the parties receive a copy.<ref name=APPaperSheets/> After the secretary of the voting table and the witnesses accredited by the CNE agree that the ''acta'' tally matches the paper receipts in the ballot boxes, they sign the ''acta'', which is transmitted to the CNE and signed copies are given to the witnesses.<ref name= BBCStayinPower>{{cite news |url= https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/cyj439myd1jo |publisher= BBC |title= Maduro manoeuvring to stay in power in Venezuela |first= Vanessa |last= Buschschlüter |date= 1 August 2024 |access-date= 1 August 2024 |archive-date= 1 August 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240801185207/https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/cyj439myd1jo |url-status= live |quote= Mr Maduro has turned to Venezuela's top court ...&nbsp;But instead of making the tallies public, he took the unusual step of filing a 'writ of amparo' - a legal move normally used by citizens who think their constitutional rights have been violated. He asked the top court to audit the voting tallies with a view to confirming the results provided by the CNE which handed him another six-year term in power. ...&nbsp;However, this move has already been dismissed by independent bodies, including the Carter Center.}}</ref><ref name= Actas/>  CNE typically posts counts, but not images of the tally sheets.<ref name="APPaperSheets" />

Lester Toledo, a strategist for the opposition, told the ''Miami Herald'' that—anticipating fraud in the vote tally—the opposition coordinated for several months before the election to arrange 600,000 volunteers into "command" groups of 10 (''comanditos'') to include "witnesses for each voting machine, lookouts outside the centers to ensure everything ran smoothly and monitors who made sure the ''actas'' were printed and then taken to outside locations to be scanned and, ultimately, uploaded to a centralized cloud".<ref name=InsideOppositionEffort/> The Associated Press reported that 90,000 opposition party representatives were trained to use a custom-made app to report results and irregularities, and had been instructed not to leave polling centers before obtaining a copy of the tally sheets.<ref name=AP-pollwatchers>{{cite news |title=Venezuela's opposition secured over 80% of crucial vote tally sheets. Here's how they did it |url=https://apnews.com/article/venezuela-election-maduro-machado-edmundo-chorizo-6d9f3999c60c09eb30e69c757ce80b11 |access-date=8 August 2024 |work=AP News |date=2 August 2024 |language=en}}</ref>  Volunteers obtained over 80% of the ''actas'',<ref name=AP-pollwatchers/> uploaded 24,576 of them, and tallied the votes by using the [[QR code]]s printed on each one.<ref name= InsideOppositionEffort>{{cite news |url= https://www.miamiherald.com/news/nation-world/world/americas/venezuela/article290667524.html|title= Inside the Venezuelan opposition's effort to prove Maduro lost the presidential election |date= 2 August 2024 |work=[[Miami Herald]] |access-date= 2 August 2024 |first1= Ana Claudio |last1= Chacin |first2= Antonio Maria |last2= Delgado|archive-url=https://archive.today/20240802193050/https://www.miamiherald.com/news/nation-world/world/americas/venezuela/article290667524.html|archive-date=2 August 2024|url-status=live}}</ref>

Following the election, the opposition published a database and searchable website with images of the tally sheets, which registered voters could check<ref name="OAS_report_VE_pres_elec_DECO" /><ref name="opposition_results_website" /><ref name="LaPatilla_how2access_electoral_records" /> and which they provided to international observers.<ref name="resultadosconvzla_csv_mesas_v1" />

Parties and countries disputing the government results have urged the CNE to produce the tally sheets to verify its count.<ref name="APPaperSheets" />

=== Number of voters and voting stations ===
The Electoral Gazette number 1023 of 25 May 2023 reported that Venezuela's Electoral Registry had 21,010,514 registered voters. Of these, 20,675,478 were in Venezuela, 107,836 were abroad, and 227,200 were foreign citizens in the country. The NGO [[Súmate]] noted a decline in registered voters over the past six publications in 2021 and 2022, with 84,115 fewer voters since the last publication. They also highlighted that 53,991 voters had objections and couldn't vote, urging them to check their status on the Electoral Council's website and file a claim if necessary.<ref name="Impulso_Sumate_alerto_50000">{{Cite web |last=Suarez |first=Enrique |date=25 July 2023 |title=Súmate alertó que más de 50.000 electores no podrán votar en las presidenciales de 2024 #25Jul |url=https://www.elimpulso.com/2023/07/25/sumate-alerto-que-mas-de-50-000-electores-no-podran-votar-en-las-presidenciales-de-2024-25jul/ |access-date=26 July 2023 |website=[[El Impulso (Venezuela)|El Impulso]] |language=es |archive-date=26 July 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230726022024/https://www.elimpulso.com/2023/07/25/sumate-alerto-que-mas-de-50-000-electores-no-podran-votar-en-las-presidenciales-de-2024-25jul/ |url-status=live }} Referring to [https://web.archive.org/web/20230606133736/http://www.cne.gob.ve/web/gacetas_electorales/gacetas/2023/gaceta_electoral_1023.pdf Gaceta Electoral Número 1023],  25 May 2023.</ref>

On election day, 15,767 poll stations had been set up by 08:20&nbsp;am local time, which amounted to 95% of the total, according to CNE.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Amaya |first=Sol |date=28 July 2024 |title=Elecciones presidenciales en Venezuela de 2024, en vivo: votaciones, noticias y última hora |url=https://cnnespanol.cnn.com/2024/07/28/elecciones-presidenciales-en-venezuela-de-2024-en-vivo-votaciones-noticias-y-ultima-hora-orix/ |access-date=28 July 2024 |website=CNN |language=es |archive-date=28 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240728135052/https://cnnespanol.cnn.com/2024/07/28/elecciones-presidenciales-en-venezuela-de-2024-en-vivo-votaciones-noticias-y-ultima-hora-orix/ |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |date=28 July 2024 |title=Abren los centros electorales en Venezuela para las presidenciales |url=https://efe.com/mundo/2024-07-28/venezuela-elecciones-presidenciales/ |access-date=28 July 2024 |website=EFE Noticias |language=es-ES |archive-date=29 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240729022918/https://efe.com/mundo/2024-07-28/venezuela-elecciones-presidenciales/ |url-status=live }}</ref>

=== Observers ===
There were very few independent international election observers.<ref name= BBCVenezuelansVote>{{cite news |first= Vanessa |last= Buschschlüter |url= https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/c1we220ew71o |publisher= [[BBC News]] |title= Venezuelans vote in election challenging Maduro's grip on power |date= 28 July 2024 |access-date= 29 July 2024 |archive-date= 28 July 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240728204849/https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/c1we220ew71o |url-status= live }}</ref><ref name=BBCFiveThings>{{cite news |url= https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/c720dr48g1po |publisher= [[BBC News]] |date= 25 July 2024 |access-date= 29 July 2024 |title= Venezuela election: Five things you need to know |first= Vanessa |last= Buschschlüter |archive-date= 28 July 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240728160440/https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/c720dr48g1po |url-status= live }}</ref><ref name=UNBlasts/>

==== Carter Center ====
On 20 June 2024, the [[Carter Center]] agreed to send observers in response to concerns about the lack of sufficient independent monitors, which could undermine the legitimacy of the election results.<ref>{{cite news | url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2024-06-19/carter-center-to-send-a-team-to-observe-venezuelan-election | title=Carter Center to Send a Team to Observe Venezuelan Election | newspaper=Bloomberg | date=19 June 2024 | access-date=6 July 2024 | archive-date=18 July 2024 | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240718042852/https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2024-06-19/carter-center-to-send-a-team-to-observe-venezuelan-election | url-status=live }}</ref> It sent only "small technical team", according to the BBC<ref name= BBCVenezuelansVote/> of 17 experts to 4 cities.<ref name= CarterCenterBlasts/>

The [[Carter Center]] stated on 30 July that it could not verify the [[#Results|results from the election authorities]] and that the election "cannot be considered democratic".<ref name=CarterCenterBlasts/><ref name= CarterCenterPressRelease/>

==== United Nations ====
On 25 June 2024, the [[United Nations]] announced that it would send four monitors, following the opposition's refusal to sign an agreement recognizing the presidential vote's results. The UN team planned to independently produce a confidential report for the [[Secretary-General of the United Nations]], including recommendations for future elections in Venezuela.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.yahoo.com/news/un-deploy-electoral-monitors-venezuela-175941698.html | title=UN to Deploy Electoral Monitors to Venezuela Presidential Vote | date=25 June 2024 | access-date=6 July 2024 | archive-date=6 July 2024 | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240706230719/https://www.yahoo.com/news/un-deploy-electoral-monitors-venezuela-175941698.html | url-status=live }}</ref><ref name=BBCVenezuelansVote/>

The UN released their report publicly on 13 August;<ref name=UNExperts>{{cite news |title= U.N. experts say Venezuela election results lack basic transparency |newspaper= The Washington Post |date= 13 August 2024 |first= Samantha |last= Schmidt| access-date= 14 August 2024 |url= https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2024/08/13/venezuela-election-results-un-report/}}</ref> it stated that there was a lack of “transparency and integrity measures that are essential to holding credible elections".<ref name=UNExperts/>

==== Other invited participants ====

Following the requirements stipulated in the [[Barbados Agreement]] for transparent elections with observers, the Maduro administration invited over 600 international participants.<ref name= France24Observers>{{cite news |url= https://www.france24.com/es/am%C3%A9rica-latina/20240727-quienes-ser%C3%A1n-los-observadores-electorales-en-las-presidenciales-de-venezuela |work= [[France 24]] |title= ¿Quiénes serán los observadores electorales en las presidenciales de Venezuela? |language= es |trans-title= Who will be the electoral observers in the Venezuelan presidential elections? |date= 27 July 2024 |access-date= 6 August 2024 |archive-date= 4 August 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240804041705/https://www.france24.com/es/am%C3%A9rica-latina/20240727-quienes-ser%C3%A1n-los-observadores-electorales-en-las-presidenciales-de-venezuela |url-status= live }}</ref><ref name=ClarinEnviados>{{cite news |url= https://www.clarin.com/mundo/enviados-iran-china-rusia-nicaragua-observadores-elecciones-venezuela_0_kAM8XQf9d3.html |work= Clarin |language= es |title= Enviados de Irán, China, Rusia y Nicaragua serán observadores de las elecciones en Venezuela |trans-title= Envoys from Iran, China, Russia and Nicaragua will be observers of the elections in Venezuela |date= 26 July 2024 |access-date= 6 August 2024 |first= Ludmila|last= Vinogradoff}}</ref><ref name= SwissInfoObservers>{{cite news |url= https://www.swissinfo.ch/spa/venezuela-recibir%C3%A1-a-m%C3%A1s-de-630-observadores-internacionales-para-las-elecciones/83375716 |work= SWI swissinfo |title= Venezuela recibirá a más de 630 observadores internacionales para las elecciones |language= es |date= 10 July 2024 |access-date= 6 August 2024 |trans-title= Venezuela will receive more than 630 international observers for the elections |archive-date= 25 July 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240725101155/https://www.swissinfo.ch/spa/venezuela-recibir%C3%A1-a-m%C3%A1s-de-630-observadores-internacionales-para-las-elecciones/83375716 |url-status= live }}</ref> Along with groups such as the United Nations, invitees were members from the [[Community of Latin American and Caribbean States]] and the [[African Union]]<ref name=France24Observers/> and representatives from Iran, China, Russia and Nicaragua, among others.<ref name=ClarinEnviados/>

[[BBC News]] stated that Maduro "welcomed hundreds of guests from countries allied with his government, who he says will 'accompany' the vote."<ref name=BBCVenezuelansVote/> Argentina's ''[[Clarin (Argentine newspaper)|Clarin]]'' newspaper wrote that some invited envoys "were allowed entry on the condition that they belong to leftist organizations and not criticize the government", stating that "The observers are limited and cannot declare or express their opinion within Venezuela."<ref name= ClarinEnviados/>

According to [[France 24]], "numerous international actors, who were expected to participate in the oversight" stated that "Chavismo has revoked their accreditations, while the opposition denounce[d] obstacles for their guests", adding that "not all actors accredited to verify the functioning of Venezuelan democracy have the same powers" and that the "Carter Center and the United Nations mission were the only missions accredited to carry out mere technical observation work, that is, limited."<ref name= France24Observers/>

''[[Infobae]]'' wrote that the guests received as observers were "allies" of the Maduro administration who would not criticize, while others were not allowed to enter.<ref name=InfobaeObservers>{{cite news |url= https://www.infobae.com/venezuela/2024/07/27/maduro-expulsa-a-observadores-criticos-pero-recibe-a-veedores-de-rusia-china-y-regimenes-afines-para-las-elecciones-de-venezuela/ |work= Infobae |title= Maduro expulsa a observadores críticos, pero recibe a veedores de Rusia, China y regímenes afines para las elecciones de Venezuela |language= es |trans-title= Maduro expels critical observers, but receives observers from Russia, China and related regimes for Venezuelan elections |date= 27 July 2024 |access-date= 6 August 2024 |archive-date= 28 July 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240728170057/https://www.infobae.com/venezuela/2024/07/27/maduro-expulsa-a-observadores-criticos-pero-recibe-a-veedores-de-rusia-china-y-regimenes-afines-para-las-elecciones-de-venezuela/ |url-status= live }}</ref>

==== European Union ====
On 28 May 2024, the CNE revoked its invitation for observers from the [[European Union]], citing existing sanctions against [[Elvis Amoroso]], the head of the CNE and a Maduro ally.<ref name=BBCVenezuelansVote/><ref>{{cite web |date=29 May 2024 |title=Venezuela revokes invitation for EU to observe July election |url=https://www.france24.com/en/americas/20240528-venezuela-revokes-invitation-for-eu-to-observe-july-election |work=France 24 |access-date=29 May 2024 |archive-date=29 May 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240529023401/https://www.france24.com/en/americas/20240528-venezuela-revokes-invitation-for-eu-to-observe-july-election |url-status=live }}</ref>

After the [[European Parliament]] passed a resolution condemning the political disqualification of opposition pre-candidate [[María Corina Machado]], the president of the pro-government National Assembly, [[Jorge Rodríguez (Venezuelan politician)|Jorge Rodríguez]], declared on 13 July 2023 that the Venezuelan government would not allow a [[European Union]] electoral observation mission.<ref>{{cite web |last=Moleiro |first=Alonso |date=14 July 2023 |title=Venezuela anuncia que no aceptará la observación europea en las elecciones presidenciales de 2024 |url=https://elpais.com/internacional/2023-07-14/venezuela-anuncia-que-no-aceptara-la-observacion-europea-en-las-elecciones-presidenciales-de-2024.html |access-date=6 September 2023 |website=[[El País]] |archive-date=6 September 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230906003827/https://elpais.com/internacional/2023-07-14/venezuela-anuncia-que-no-aceptara-la-observacion-europea-en-las-elecciones-presidenciales-de-2024.html |url-status=live }}<!-- auto-translated by Module:CS1 translator --></ref><ref>{{cite web |date=14 July 2023 |title=Venezuela niega el acceso a observadores europeos para las elecciones de 2024 |url=https://www.europapress.es/internacional/noticia-venezuela-niega-acceso-observadores-europeos-elecciones-2024-20230714060851.html |access-date=6 September 2023 |website=[[Europa Press (news agency)|Europa Press]] |archive-date=6 September 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230906003827/https://www.europapress.es/internacional/noticia-venezuela-niega-acceso-observadores-europeos-elecciones-2024-20230714060851.html |url-status=live }}<!-- auto-translated by Module:CS1 translator --></ref><ref>{{cite web |last=Gómez Piña |first=Shirley |date=13 July 2023 |title=Rodríguez asegura que no aceptarán observadores europeos en elecciones del 2024 |url=https://www.radiofeyalegrianoticias.com/jorge-rodriguez-asegura-que-no-aceptaran-observadores-europeos-en-elecciones-del-2024/ |access-date=6 September 2023 |website=Radio Fe y Alegría Noticias |language=es |archive-date=6 September 2023 }}<!-- auto-translated by Module:CS1 translator --></ref>

====Argentina and Brazil ====

On 17 July 2024, the [[Superior Electoral Court]] (TSE) of [[Brazil]], which had previously rejected the invitation from Maduro's government to send observers, announced a reversal of its decision, stating that it would send two observers.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://bitlyanews.com/principales/brasil-revierte-decision-y-anuncia-que-enviara-observadores-para-las-elecciones-presidenciales-en-venezuela/ | title=Brasil revierte decisión y anuncia que enviará observadores para las elecciones presidenciales en Venezuela | date=17 July 2024 | access-date=18 July 2024 | archive-date=18 July 2024 | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240718004657/https://bitlyanews.com/principales/brasil-revierte-decision-y-anuncia-que-enviara-observadores-para-las-elecciones-presidenciales-en-venezuela/ | url-status=live }}</ref>

On 22 July 2024, Brazilian President [[Lula da Silva]] stated: "If Maduro wants to contribute for growth to return to Venezuela, for people who left Venezuela to come back and to establish a state of economic growth, he needs to respect the democratic process." Lula, who had previously refused to openly criticize Maduro, said he would send former foreign minister [[Celso Amorim]] to watch the election.<ref name=ap22july>{{Cite web|url=https://apnews.com/article/brazil-venezuela-lula-maduro-elections-7f75e9f4eac2208772d639a3b9fb5793|title=Brazil's Lula urges Venezuela's Maduro to respect vote results, is 'frightened' by talk of bloodbath|date=22 July 2024|website=Associated Press|first=Mauricio|last=Savarese|access-date=22 July 2024|archive-date=22 July 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240722192939/https://apnews.com/article/brazil-venezuela-lula-maduro-elections-7f75e9f4eac2208772d639a3b9fb5793|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 24 July 2024, TSE announced it would no longer send observers to the election in light of statements by Maduro in which, without proof, he accused the Brazilian electoral system of not being auditable.<ref>{{cite web |title=TSE desiste de enviar observadores à Venezuela após fala de Maduro |date=25 July 2024 |url=https://www.poder360.com.br/poder-justica/tse-desiste-de-enviar-observadores-a-venezuela-apos-fala-de-maduro/ |publisher=Poder360 |access-date=2 August 2024}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Sem provas, Maduro critica Brasil por "não auditar" urnas |url=https://www.poder360.com.br/poder-internacional/sem-provas-maduro-critica-brasil-por-nao-auditar-urnas/ |access-date=2 August 2024 |work=Poder360 |date=24 July 2024 |archive-date=24 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240724103531/https://www.poder360.com.br/poder-internacional/sem-provas-maduro-critica-brasil-por-nao-auditar-urnas/ |url-status=live }}</ref> Nonetheless, Brazil's observation went on as planned.<ref>{{cite news |title=Eleição na Venezuela: Maduro recebeu Amorim no Palácio Miraflores e disse que entregará atas eleitorais 'nos próximos dias' |url=https://oglobo.globo.com/mundo/noticia/2024/07/29/eleicao-na-venezuela-maduro-recebeu-amorim-no-palacio-miraflores.ghtml |access-date=2 August 2024 |work=O Globo |date=29 July 2024 |language=pt-br |archive-date=2 August 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240802144913/https://oglobo.globo.com/mundo/noticia/2024/07/29/eleicao-na-venezuela-maduro-recebeu-amorim-no-palacio-miraflores.ghtml |url-status=live }}</ref>

Former Argentine president [[Alberto Fernández]] was uninvited to observe after agreeing with Lula.<ref name= BBCVenezuelansVote/><ref name= ReutersArgentinaBrazil>{{cite news |url= https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/argentinas-fernandez-brazilian-court-withdraw-venezuelan-election-observer-2024-07-25/ |title= Argentina's Fernandez, Brazilian court withdraw from Venezuelan election observer mission |work= Reuters |date= 25 July 2024 |access-date= 29 July 2024}}</ref>

==== Other countries ====
Spanish left-wing parties [[Podemos (Spanish political party)|Podemos]], [[United Left (Spain)|United Left]], [[Galician Nationalist Bloc]] and [[EH Bildu]] sent observers.<ref>{{cite web |last=Redondo |first=Víctor |date=30 July 2024 |title=Podemos, IU, EH Bildu y BNG felicitan al pueblo venezolano |url=https://www.diario.red/articulo/actualidad/podemos-iu-eh-bildu-bng/20240729152534033413.html |access-date=30 July 2024 |work=[[Canal Red|Diario Red]] |language=es |archive-date=30 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240730132908/https://www.diario.red/articulo/actualidad/podemos-iu-eh-bildu-bng/20240729152534033413.html |url-status=live }}</ref> Officials from Spain (ten members of its parliament), Portugal,<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://albertonews.com/internacionales/impiden-a-cayetana-alvarez-de-toledo-y-comision-del-partido-popular-ingresar-a-venezuela-seran-deportados-en-proximas-horas/|title=Retenida en Caracas la delegación del Partido Popular español que viajó a las elecciones: serán deportados en próximas horas|date=26 July 2024|access-date=27 July 2024|archive-date=27 July 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240727080732/https://albertonews.com/internacionales/impiden-a-cayetana-alvarez-de-toledo-y-comision-del-partido-popular-ingresar-a-venezuela-seran-deportados-en-proximas-horas/|url-status=live}}</ref> and Colombia (senator Angelica Lozano) said they were denied entry to Venezuela days before the election.<ref name= AFPConcernGrows>{{cite news |url= https://www.voanews.com/a/concern-grows-as-venezuela-blocks-election-observers/7715124.html |publisher= [[Voice of America]] |title= Concern grows as Venezuela blocks election observers |agency= [[Agence France-Presse]] |date= 27 July 2024 |access-date= 29 July 2024 |archive-date= 28 July 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240728012935/https://www.voanews.com/a/concern-grows-as-venezuela-blocks-election-observers/7715124.html |url-status= live }}</ref>

A [[Copa Airlines]] flight from Panama<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://albertonews.com/internacionales/ultima-hora-dos-vuelos-de-copa-airlines-retenidos-en-panama-por-tener-a-bordo-a-expresidentes-de-la-region-que-intentan-viajar-a-venezuela-para-las-presidenciales/|title=Impiden despegar de Panamá a vuelo con expresidentes que iban a Venezuela como observadores invitados por la oposición|date=26 July 2024|access-date=27 July 2024|archive-date=27 July 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240727092131/https://albertonews.com/internacionales/ultima-hora-dos-vuelos-de-copa-airlines-retenidos-en-panama-por-tener-a-bordo-a-expresidentes-de-la-region-que-intentan-viajar-a-venezuela-para-las-presidenciales/|url-status=live}}</ref> bound for Caracas the day before the vote with former presidents [[Mireya Moscoso]] (Panama), [[Miguel Angel Rodriguez]] (Costa Rica), [[Jorge Quiroga]] (Bolivia) and [[Vicente Fox]] (Mexico), as well as [[Marta Lucia Ramirez]] (former Colombian vice president), was unable to depart Panama until the former officials deplaned.<ref name=AFPConcernGrows/><ref name= BBCVenezuelaAccused>{{cite news |url= https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/cn4v963pzm2o |publisher= [[BBC News]] |title= Venezuela accused of grounding Latin American ex-leaders' flight |date= 27 July 2024 |access-date= 29 July 2024 |first= Leonardo |last= Rocha |archive-date= 29 July 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240729182314/https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/cn4v963pzm2o |url-status= live }}</ref><ref name="x586">{{cite web |author1=Elida Moreno |author2=Vivian Sequera | title=Panama says flights operating normally after Venezuela plane was blocked | website=Reuters | date=26 July 2024 | url=https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/panamas-mulino-says-plane-with-ex-presidents-heading-venezuela-not-allowed-leave-2024-07-26/ | access-date=27 July 2024}}</ref>

[[Chile]]an Senators [[Felipe Kast]] and [[Rojo Edwards]] were deported by Venezuelan authorities a day after arriving to observe the vote.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.cnnchile.com/pais/se-suma-al-rojo-edwards-felipe-kast-tampoco-pudo-ingresar-a-venezuela-y-es-deportado-por-el-regimen-de-nicolas-maduro_20240726/|title=Se suma a Rojo Edwards: |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240728081143/https://bitlyanews.com/internacionales/ultima-hora-deportan-de-venezuela-a-diputado-uruguayo-pablo-viana-invitado-por-la-oposicion-para-las-presidenciales-del-28j-detalles/ |url-status=live }}</ref>

Colombia was invited but did not send observers, with officials stating that the timing of the electoral process was inadequate for technical preparations.<ref>{{cite news |first= Carol |last= Salazar |url= https://www.infobae.com/colombia/2024/07/18/registraduria-confirmo-que-no-tendra-ningun-tipo-de-participacion-en-las-elecciones-de-venezuela/ |language= es |title= Registraduría confirmó que no tendrá ningún tipo de participación en las elecciones de Venezuela |trans-title= The Registrar's Office confirmed that it will not have any kind of participation in the Venezuelan elections |work= Infobae |date= 18 July 2024 |access-date= 6 August 2024 |archive-date= 18 July 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240718222723/https://www.infobae.com/colombia/2024/07/18/registraduria-confirmo-que-no-tendra-ningun-tipo-de-participacion-en-las-elecciones-de-venezuela/ |url-status= live }}</ref>

== Candidates ==

=== United Socialist Party of Venezuela ===
On 16 March 2024, the [[United Socialist Party of Venezuela]] (PSUV) announced that incumbent Maduro would be their candidate in the presidential election, making it his third run for a six-year term.<ref name=MaduroCandidacy>{{Cite web|url=https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuelas-maduro-run-presidential-elections-set-july-socialist-party-says-2024-03-16/|title=Venezuela's Maduro announces candidacy for July re-election|work=[[Reuters]]|first=Mayela|last=Armas|date=17 March 2024|access-date=22 July 2024|archive-date=31 March 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240331135753/https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuelas-maduro-run-presidential-elections-set-july-socialist-party-says-2024-03-16/|url-status=live}}</ref> Maduro officially registered his candidacy on 25 March.<ref>{{cite web |date=25 March 2024 |title=Venezuela's Maduro makes his candidacy official while a would-be rival struggles to register |url=https://apnews.com/article/venezuela-opposition-candidate-corina-yoris-7a7abaea209ea632ad5c3a56a5500ac6 |access-date=26 March 2024 |website=Associated Press |first1=Joshua |last1=Goodman |first2=Jorge |last2=Rueda |language=en |archive-date=25 March 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240325213011/https://apnews.com/article/venezuela-opposition-candidate-corina-yoris-7a7abaea209ea632ad5c3a56a5500ac6 |url-status=live }}</ref>

Maduro stated in July that there would be a bloodbath or civil war if he lost the election, and that his party would win "by hook or by crook".<ref>{{cite news |url= https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/cz7ek27j7j3o |title=Venezuelans in tense wait for election results |publisher=BBC News |date=28 July 2024|access-date=19 August 2024|first1=Ione|last1=Wells|first2=Robert |last2=Plummer}}</ref><ref name= AlmagroSolicitara/><ref>{{cite news|url= https://cnnespanol.cnn.com/video/nicolas-maduro-venezuela-bano-sangre-guerra-civil-elecciones-panorama-mundial-tv/|work=CNN en Español|title='Baño de sangre' y 'guerra civil', las advertencias de Maduro si pierde la elección|language=es|trans-title='Bloodbath' and 'civil war': Maduro's warnings if he loses the election|first=Osmary |last=Hernández|date=17 July 2024|access-date=19 August 2024}}</ref>

=== Unitary Platform ===
The preliminary winner of the 22 October [[2023 Unitary Platform presidential primaries]] was Machado, sweeping more than 90% of the vote. On 23 October, the second electoral bulletin of the National Primary Commission stated that with 92.65% counted, Machado won more than 90% of the votes and would be the candidate for the Unitary Platform for the 2024 presidential election.<ref name=BloombergSecondBulletin>{{cite web |date=23 October 2023 |title=Comisión de Primaria en Venezuela publica segundo boletín con 64,88% de las actas escrutadas |url=https://www.bloomberglinea.com/latinoamerica/venezuela/comision-de-primaria-en-venezuela-publica-segundo-boletin-con-6488-de-las-actas-escrutadas/ |website=Bloomberg en Línea |quote=voceros del chavismo como Diosdado Cabello han cuestionado el resultado obtenido |access-date=25 October 2023 |archive-date=24 October 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20231024115650/https://www.bloomberglinea.com/latinoamerica/venezuela/comision-de-primaria-en-venezuela-publica-segundo-boletin-con-6488-de-las-actas-escrutadas/ |url-status=live }}</ref>

After her disqualification by the TSJ, on 22 March 2024, Machado announced that historian and professor [[Corina Yoris]] would be the replacement candidate.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Herrero|first1=Ana Vanessa|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2024/03/22/maria-corina-machado-corina-yori-maduro/|title=Maduro's strongest challenger, barred from running, picks a stand-in|date=22 March 2024|newspaper=[[The Washington Post]]|access-date=27 June 2024}}</ref>

Yoris was unable to officially register in the election; Unitary Platform representatives said that the electoral commission had blocked her registration. Following outcry from countries including the US, Brazil, Colombia, and Guatemala the Unitary Platform registered former diplomat [[Edmundo González]] as its temporary candidate pending the selection of another one.<ref>{{cite web |last1=Rueda |first1=Jorge |last2=Janetsky |first2=Megan |date=26 March 2024 |title=Venezuelan opposition coalition able to register provisional candidate after electoral outcry |url=https://apnews.com/article/venezuela-opposition-candidate-corina-yoris-a4e562ea579e7e63ab1ba067041c4b66 |accessdate=27 March 2024 |website=Associated Press |archive-date=26 March 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240326195242/https://apnews.com/article/venezuela-opposition-candidate-corina-yoris-a4e562ea579e7e63ab1ba067041c4b66 |url-status=live }}</ref>

=== A New Era withdraws===
[[Zulia]] Governor [[Manuel Rosales]], founder of [[Un Nuevo Tiempo|A New Era]] party,<ref name=AQWish/> launched a last-minute candidacy in March, taking the Unitary Platform by surprise, although he indicated he would cede his position to a unified opposition candidate.<ref>{{cite web |date=26 March 2024 |title=Venezuela opposition overcomes hurdles to register candidate |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-latin-america-68664242 |access-date=27 March 2024 |website=BBC |language=en |archive-date=26 March 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240326233118/https://www.bbc.com/news/world-latin-america-68664242 |url-status=live }}</ref> Rosales is known as a more moderate opposition candidate who has negotiated with the Maduro government; he recognized Maduro's contested 2018 election and condemned [[U.S. sanctions during the Venezuelan crisis|sanctions on Venezuela enacted by the United States]].<ref>{{Cite news |first2=Kejal |last2=Vyas|first1=Juan|last1=Forero |title=Venezuela's Strongman Decides Who Will Run Against Him in Presidential Election |url= https://www.wsj.com/world/americas/venezuelas-strongman-decides-who-will-run-against-him-in-presidential-election-dd9f87c6 |access-date=28 March 2024 |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |language=en-US |archive-date=27 March 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240327211013/https://www.wsj.com/world/americas/venezuelas-strongman-decides-who-will-run-against-him-in-presidential-election-dd9f87c6 |url-status=live }}</ref> In what an ''[[Americas Quarterly]]'' article described as "Venezuela’s long-standing political crisis", the appearance of a candidate "distrusted by others in the opposition as a pro-system contender" seemed to lower the chances a united opposition could defeat Maduro.<ref name=AQWish>{{cite journal|url=https://www.americasquarterly.org/article/maduro-gets-his-wish-a-divided-venezuelan-opposition/|journal=[[Americas Quarterly]]|title=Maduro Gets His Wish: A Divided Venezuelan Opposition|first=Tony|last=Mawad|date=4 April 2024|access-date=19 August 2024}}</ref> According to an article published by [[Deutsche Welle]], his candidacy led to an "uproar" in which "Machado accused him of treason".<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.dw.com/en/in-venezuela-a-divided-opposition-weighs-its-chances/a-68695061|publisher=[[Deutsche Welle]]|title=In Venezuela, a divided opposition weighs its chances|first=Jan D.|last=Walter|date=30 March 2024|access-date=19 August 2024}}</ref>

On 19 April 2024, a day before the deadline to register an opposition candidate,<ref>{{cite web |last=Armas |first=Mayela |date=20 April 2024 |title=Edmundo Gonzalez, Venezuela's low-profile and last-minute opposition candidate |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/edmundo-gonzalez-venezuelas-low-profile-last-minute-opposition-candidate-2024-04-20/ |accessdate=20 April 2024 |work=[[Reuters]]}}</ref> [[Omar Barboza]], executive secretary of the PUD and president of A New Era, announced that, after a unanimous vote in support of a unity candidate, Rosales would withdraw from the race and endorse Edmundo González, uniting the PUD around a single candidate.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://elpais.com/america/2024-04-20/la-oposicion-venezolana-apura-las-ultimas-horas-de-plazo-de-sustitucion-para-encontrar-un-candidato-unico.html|work=El País|title=La oposición venezolana elige como candidato de consenso a Edmundo González Urrutia|language=es|trans-title=Venezuelan opposition chooses Edmundo González Urrutia as consensus candidate|date=19 April 2024|access-date=19 August 2024|first=Florantonia|last=Singer}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/mundo/articles/crgyde4k35ko|publisher=BBC News|title=La principal coalición opositora de Venezuela confirma a Edmundo González como su candidato de unidad para las elecciones presidenciales|language=es|trans-title=Venezuela's main opposition coalition confirms Edmundo González as its unity candidate for presidential elections|date=20 April 2024|access-date=19 August 2024}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.infobae.com/venezuela/2024/04/20/la-oposicion-venezolana-designo-por-unanimidad-al-embajador-edmundo-gonzalez-urrutia-como-su-candidato-presidencial/|work=Infobae|title=La oposición venezolana designó por unanimidad a Edmundo González Urrutia como su candidato presidencial|language=es|trans-title=The Venezuelan opposition unanimously designated Edmundo González Urrutia as its presidential candidate|date=19 April 2024|access-date=19 August 2024}}</ref>

===Other candidates===

The [[Democratic Alliance (Venezuela)|Democratic Alliance]] did not participate in the primary.<ref>{{cite web |last=Martínez |first=Deisy |date=9 March 2023 |title=Alianza Democrática aún no discute candidatura presidencial unitaria para 2024 |url=https://efectococuyo.com/politica/alianza-democratica-candidatura-presidencial-unitaria-2024/ |access-date=2 May 2023 |website=Efecto Cocuyo |language=en |archive-date=2 May 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230502190952/https://efectococuyo.com/politica/alianza-democratica-candidatura-presidencial-unitaria-2024/ |url-status=live }}</ref>

Eleven candidates without significant representation were registered following the Maduro administration's veto of opposition candidates Machado and Corina.<ref name="da Costa-2024">{{cite web |url=https://www.infobae.com/venezuela/2024/03/31/quienes-son-y-de-donde-vienen-los-candidatos-que-le-hacen-el-juego-a-maduro-en-su-farsa-electoral/ |title=Quiénes son y de dónde vienen los candidatos que le hacen el juego a Maduro en su farsa electoral |last=da Costa |first=Rocío |date=31 March 2024 |website=Infobae |language=es |access-date=18 July 2024 |archive-date=18 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240718032404/https://www.infobae.com/venezuela/2024/03/31/quienes-son-y-de-donde-vienen-los-candidatos-que-le-hacen-el-juego-a-maduro-en-su-farsa-electoral/ |url-status=live }}</ref> Authorities allowed the registration of candidates considered to be collaborators, false opposition, and politicians aligned with the Bolivarian strategy for the July 2024 presidential election, while blocking genuine opposition candidates.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.elmundo.es/internacional/2024/03/25/6600b844e9cf4aee328b45a5.html |title=El chavismo sólo acepta un candidato "potable" de la oposición real a la medida de Maduro |date=24 March 2024 |website=ELMUNDO |language=es |access-date=18 July 2024 |archive-date=29 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240729194432/https://www.elmundo.es/internacional/2024/03/25/6600b844e9cf4aee328b45a5.html |url-status=live }}</ref> Among these candidates are individuals with ties to Chavismo and diverse figures such as a comedian and an evangelical pastor.<ref name="da Costa-2024" />

Luis Eduardo Martínez, a deputy for [[Acción Democrática]], has held positions as governor and councilor.<ref name="da Costa-2024" /> {{ill|Daniel Ceballos|es|Daniel Ceballos (político)}}, former mayor of San Cristóbal, has been favored by the [[Supreme Tribunal of Justice (Venezuela)|Supreme Tribunal of Justice]] (TSJ).<ref name="da Costa-2024" /> {{ill|Antonio Ecarri|es|Antonio Ecarri Angola}}, with a background in education and public management, has declined multiple candidacies in his political career.<ref name="da Costa-2024" /> [[Juan Carlos Alvarado]], Secretary-General of [[COPEI]], was appointed by the TSJ and has validated [[chavismo]] control of the Parliament.<ref name="da Costa-2024" /> [[Benjamín Rausseo]], a comedian and businessman, has made previous attempts for public office. [[Javier Bertucci]], an [[Evangelicalism|evangelical]] pastor and deputy, has a criminal record related to diesel smuggling. [[José Brito]], a former member of [[Primero Justicia]], has been accused of corruption and collaborating with the administration to prevent the re-election of [[Juan Guaidó]].<ref name="da Costa-2024" /> [[Claudio Fermín]], with extensive political experience and positions in the Executive Branch, has been an unsuccessful presidential candidate several times. [[Luis Ratti]], a businessman and preacher, requested the suspension of opposition primaries. Enrique Márquez, a former rector of the [[National Electoral Council (Venezuela)|National Electoral Council]] (CNE), has held seats in the National Assembly and served as its vice president (2016–2017, after the [[2015 Venezuelan parliamentary election|electoral victory of the opposition]]).

==Conduct and irregularities==

=== Disqualification of political parties ===
On 17 March, the CNE disqualified 16 political parties from nominating candidates in the presidential election, after not reaching 1% of the minimum votes in the [[2021 Venezuelan regional elections]], without offering a validation or repair process required by electoral law. The parties disqualified included:<ref>{{cite web |last=Quintero |first=Luisa |date=17 March 2024 |title=16 partidos quedaron vetados por el CNE para postular en las presidenciales 2024 |url=https://talcualdigital.com/16-partidos-quedaron-vetados-por-el-cne-para-postular-en-las-presidenciales-2024/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240729025845/https://talcualdigital.com/16-partidos-quedaron-vetados-por-el-cne-para-postular-en-las-presidenciales-2024/ |archive-date=29 July 2024 |access-date=1 June 2024 |website=Tal Cual |language=es}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |last=Luna |first=Perdomo |date=16 March 2024 |title=Plataforma Unitaria solo tendrá a la MUD y UNT para postular candidato presidencial |url=https://talcualdigital.com/solo-la-mud-y-unt-podran-postular-candidatos-para-la-eleccion-presidencial/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240521155631/https://talcualdigital.com/solo-la-mud-y-unt-podran-postular-candidatos-para-la-eleccion-presidencial/ |archive-date=21 May 2024 |access-date=1 June 2024 |website=Tal Cual |language=es}}</ref> Adelante, Centrados, Única, [[National Convergence]], Suma País, Encuentro Ciudadano, Generación Independiente (Gente), Partido Unión y Entendimiento (Puente), [[Movimiento al Socialismo (Venezuela)]] (MAS), Fuerza del Cambio (FDC), Nueva Visión para mi País (Nuvipa), Unidad Política Popular 89 (UPP-89), Unión y Progreso (Venezuela), Prociudadanos (LPC), Compromiso País (Compa).

===Blocking of the CNE portal===
Following the end of the registration period for candidates on 25 March, Machado said that the [[Unitary Platform]] was prevented from registering [[Corina Yoris]]'s candidacy, and Rosales said that he did not represent the Unitary Platform.<ref>{{cite web |date=26 March 2024 |title=¿Qué preguntas quedan después de la hora loca del CNE? |url=https://correodelcaroni.com/pais-politico/que-preguntas-quedan-despues-de-la-hora-loca-del-cne/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240410154343/https://correodelcaroni.com/pais-politico/que-preguntas-quedan-despues-de-la-hora-loca-del-cne/ |archive-date=10 April 2024 |access-date=2 June 2024 |website=Correo del Caroní |language=es}}</ref> Shortly afterwards, the CNE, following international pressure, authorized a 12-hour extension to register candidates, which enabled the Unitary Platform card to provisionally register its candidate, [[Edmundo González Urrutia]].<ref>{{cite web |last=Quintero |first=Luisa |date=26 March 2024 |title=CNE confirma 13 candidatos a las presidenciales 'sin ningún tipo de restricción' |url=https://talcualdigital.com/cne-confirma-13-candidatos-a-las-presidenciales-sin-ningun-tipo-de-restriccion/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240416100105/https://talcualdigital.com/cne-confirma-13-candidatos-a-las-presidenciales-sin-ningun-tipo-de-restriccion/ |archive-date=16 April 2024 |access-date=2 June 2024 |website=Tal Cual |language=es}}</ref>

=== Obstruction in overseas voting ===
{{See also|Voter suppression}}
{{Multiple image|total_width=280|direction=vertical
|image1=Huelga de hambre de Venezuela en Madrid 2024.jpg|caption1=Hunger strike in Madrid demanding the opening of the Electoral Registry abroad
|image2=Manifestantes venezolanos anti-Maduro en el lado colombiano del puente Simon Bolivar.jpg|caption2=Venezuelan [[Opposition to Chavismo|opposition]] on the Colombian side of the [[Simón Bolívar International Bridge]]
}}
The requirements for voters to register abroad were restrictive and not contemplated in the constitution. Requirements included a current passport (one of the most expensive in the world to obtain) and having permanent residence; the majority of voters abroad had Temporary Permission to Stay or Permission for Temporary Protection, and did not have residence, consequently, very few were registered.<ref name=CNESuma>{{cite web |last=Figuera |first=Roison |date=23 March 2024 |title=CNE suma una semana en mora con el Registro Electoral en el exterior |url=https://talcualdigital.com/cne-suma-una-semana-en-mora-con-el-registro-electoral-en-el-exterior/#google_vignette |website=Tal Cual |language=es |access-date=12 July 2024 |archive-date=29 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240729033335/https://talcualdigital.com/cne-suma-una-semana-en-mora-con-el-registro-electoral-en-el-exterior/#google_vignette |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 16 April, registration and updating of the Electoral Registry of Venezuela concluded. With approximately 7.7 million Venezuelans abroad, 80% of whom have the right to vote, the CNE only authorized some consulates to hold registration; many Venezuelans could not register because there was no authorized consulate or it was very far from their location. In many of the consulates, delays were observed and the CNE registered little political interest in solving the problem; the majority of voters abroad register an opposition tendency.<ref>{{cite web |last=Álvarez |first=Ramón Cardozo |date=19 April 2024 |title=Maduro cercena el derecho electoral de migrantes venezolanos |url=https://www.dw.com/es/maduro-cercena-el-derecho-electoral-de-los-migrantes-venezolanos/a-68873638 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240615003850/https://www.dw.com/es/maduro-cercena-el-derecho-electoral-de-los-migrantes-venezolanos/a-68873638 |archive-date=15 June 2024 |access-date=5 July 2024 |website=[[Deutsche Welle]] |publisher= |language=es}}</ref> [[David Smolansky]], former mayor of [[El Hatillo Municipality|El Hatillo]], accused the administration of blocking the registration of at least 4.5 million Venezuelans abroad through "a policy of systematic and generalized discrimination" as well as its "requirements to register and change residence address" that led to "queues at the consulates".<ref>{{cite web |last=Vinogradoff |first=Ludmila |date=16 April 2024 |title=Las trabas que el régimen de Nicolás Maduro pone a los venezolanos en el exterior para inscribirse para las elecciones presidenciales |url=https://www.clarin.com/mundo/trabas-regimen-nicolas-maduro-pone-venezolanos-exterior-inscribirse-elecciones-presidenciales_0_V7uxRkjTi6.html |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240521195704/https://www.clarin.com/mundo/trabas-regimen-nicolas-maduro-pone-venezolanos-exterior-inscribirse-elecciones-presidenciales_0_V7uxRkjTi6.html |archive-date=21 May 2024 |access-date=1 June 2024 |website=El Clarín |language=es}}</ref>

The special day for voter registration abroad was marred by delays in the process of up to five days, as occurred in Spain, Argentina, Peru and Chile. Citizens complained that they were not able to register or update their data.<ref name=CNESuma/>

According to a 2 May preliminary CNE report, of the almost 7.7 million Venezuelans abroad, only 69,189 were allowed to vote, of which only 6,020 managed to change their voting center in Venezuela to the country where they reside. The number of new people registered to vote abroad was negligible due to the requirements imposed by the CNE and the Foreign Ministry: in Mexico 69 people managed to register as new voters, in Spain 97, in Argentina 27, in Colombia only 25, in Ecuador 13 and in Peru only six. The exact total number of citizens able to vote was 21,402,220.<ref>{{cite web |last=Valduza |first=Enrique |date=2 May 2024 |title=Apenas 69 mil venezolanos en el exterior podrán votar en comicios del 28 de julio, según primer corte del RE |url=https://www.diarioultimahoradigital.com.ve/2024/05/02/apenas-69-mil-venezolanos-en-el-exterior-podran-votar-en-comicios-del-28-de-julio-segun-primer-corte-preliminar-del-re/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240602132728/https://www.diarioultimahoradigital.com.ve/2024/05/02/apenas-69-mil-venezolanos-en-el-exterior-podran-votar-en-comicios-del-28-de-julio-segun-primer-corte-preliminar-del-re/ |archive-date=2 June 2024 |access-date=1 June 2024 |website=Diario Última Hora |language=es}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cne.gob.ve/web/gacetas_electorales/gacetas/2024/gaceta_electoral_1055.pdf|title=Gaceta electoral N° 1055, Resolución Nº 240429-036 Cuadro Estadístico del Registro Electoral Preliminar correspondiente al Corte del Registro Electoral al 16 de abril de 2024, el cual alcanza una cantidad de veintiún millones seiscientos treinta mil novecientos veintisiete (21.630.927)|date=29 April 2024|publisher=Gaceta Electoral del CNE|website=Lista: Distribución de Electoras y Electores Por Estado|access-date=12 July 2024|archive-date=24 July 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240724031255/http://www.cne.gob.ve/web/gacetas_electorales/gacetas/2024/gaceta_electoral_1055.pdf|url-status=live}}</ref>

In mid-June the [[Inter-American Commission on Human Rights]] (IACHR) demanded that Venezuela "adopt the necessary measures" to guarantee the right to vote for compatriots abroad for the presidential elections, stating that "a genuine commitment to democracy requires that the State immediately reestablish the separation and independence of public powers".<ref>{{cite web |date=18 June 2024 |title=CIDH insta a Venezuela a garantizar derecho al voto de connacionales en el extranjero |url=https://talcualdigital.com/cidh-insta-a-venezuela-a-garantizar-derecho-al-voto-de-connacionales-en-el-extranjero/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240712143852/https://talcualdigital.com/cidh-insta-a-venezuela-a-garantizar-derecho-al-voto-de-connacionales-en-el-extranjero/ |archive-date=12 July 2024 |access-date=12 July 2024 |website=Tal Cual |language=es}}</ref>

=== Harassment, intimidation and other irregularities===
Along with the issues in overseas voter registration and voting that "effectively disenfranchised most of the migrant population", the [[Carter Center]] listed other problems with the electoral process. Checkpoints were placed near polling stations to intimidate voters.  Individuals and companies providing services to the opposition were harassed and intimidated. The TSJ replaced the leadership of opposition political parties with those who supported Maduro. The Maduro campaign frequently used government vehicles and social programs to promote their campaign.<ref name= BBCStayinPower/><ref name= CarterCenterPressRelease/>

''[[The New York Times]]'' stated that irregularities on election day throughout the country "provoked fury". Intimidation of voters with violence and threats, and by state forces, included an example in [[Cumaná]], where dozens of armed authorities lined up at a polling station. In one city, voters reported that government security forces tried to replace designated witnesses with their own personnel. The Venezuelan Electoral Observatory said that 17,000 voters found their polling place changed at the last minute; a ''New York Times'' reporter was detained after trying to enter an unofficial polling place. Voting centers stayed open past the required closing time to allow Maduro supporters to round up more votes. Some voting centers refused to print the vote tallies as required by law.<ref name=NYTLasElecciones>{{cite news |url= https://www.nytimes.com/es/2024/07/31/espanol/elecciones-venezuela-irregularidades-ejemplos.html |work= The New York Times |title= Las elecciones en Venezuela tuvieron profundas irregularidades. Estas son algunas |language= es |trans-title= The elections in Venezuela had deep irregularities. Here are some of them |first= Genevieve |last= Glatsky |date= 31 July 2024 |access-date= 2 August 2024 |archive-date= 2 August 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240802030525/https://www.nytimes.com/es/2024/07/31/espanol/elecciones-venezuela-irregularidades-ejemplos.html |url-status= live }}</ref> Between January and 26 July 2024, [[Foro Penal]] said that 135 individuals associated with the González campaign had been arrested.<ref>{{cite news |url= https://www.france24.com/es/minuto-a-minuto/20240726-más-de-130-detenidos-en-venezuela-vinculados-a-la-campaña-opositora-según-una-ong |publisher= [[France 24]] |title= Más de 130 detenidos en Venezuela vinculados a la campaña opositora, según una ONG |language= es |trans-title= More than 130 people arrested in Venezuela linked to the opposition campaign, according to an NGO |date = 26 July 2024 |access-date= 6 August 2024}}</ref>

According to Lester Toledo, as the polls were about to close, "he received reports from about 90% of the volunteers that the government had ordered election workers to not print the ''actas''. But after a tense period of back-and-forth, soldiers with the national guard allowed most volunteers to take the actas home anyway."<ref name= InsideOppositionEffort/> Inside the CNE as the machine vote tallies were being received, the two witnesses from the opposition were denied entry, and according to the ''Miami Herald'', "Enrique Marquez, one of a handful of presidential candidates, said his own campaign monitor was allowed in the room and reported that the Council did not print the results of the election."<ref name= InsideOppositionEffort/>

=== Violence ===
Pares (the Colombian [[Peace & Reconciliation Foundation]]) released three reports on violence that occurred during the elections.<ref name=MHCouldCharge/><ref name=ElDiarioParesFoundation/><ref name=DiariolasAmericasPares>{{cite news|url=https://www.diariolasamericas.com/america-latina/en-venezuela-reportan-una-victima-violencia-politica-cada-dos-dias-precampana-electoral-n5358333|title=En Venezuela reportan una víctima de violencia política cada dos días durante precampaña electoral|language=es|trans-title=In Venezuela, one victim of political violence is reported every two days during the pre-election campaign|work=[[Diario Las Américas]]|date=14 June 2024|access-date=20 August 2024|first=Olgalinda|last=Pimentel}}</ref> The reports encompassed the time periods:

#5 March to 25 May<ref name=Pares1>{{cite report|url=https://www.pares.com.co/post/primer-informe-sobre-violencia-pol%C3%ADtico-electoral-en-venezuela|title=Primer informe sobre violencia político electoral en Venezuela|language=es|trans-title=First report on political-electoral violence in Venezuela|date=14 June 2024|publisher=Pares: Fundación Paz y Reconciliación|location=Bogota, Colombia|access-date=20 August 2024}}</ref>
#26 May to 26 June<ref name=Pares2>{{cite report|url=https://www.pares.com.co/post/no-para-la-violencia-de-maduro-contra-sus-opositores|title=Segundo Informe de Violencia Político—Electoral en Venezuela|language=es|trans-title=Second Report on Political-Electoral Violence in Venezuela|date=12 July 2024|publisher=Pares: Fundación Paz y Reconciliación|location=Bogota, Colombia|access-date=20 August 2024}}</ref>
#27 June to 28 July<ref name=Pares3>{{cite report|url=https://www.pares.com.co/post/desapariciones-deportaciones-y-detenciones-arbitrarias-los-resultados-del-tercer-informe-de-violen|title= Desapariciones, deportaciones y detenciones arbitrarias: Los resultados del Tercer Informe de Violencia Político-Electoral en Venezuela|language=es|trans-title=Disappearances, deportations and arbitrary detentions: The results of the Third Report on Political-Electoral Violence in Venezuela|publisher=Pares: Fundación Paz y Reconciliación|location=Bogota, Colombia|date=16 August 2024|access-date=20 August 2024}}</ref>

In the first report, Pares stated there were 25 incidents with 38 victims, of which 17 were affiliated with [[Vente Venezuela]].<ref name=DiariolasAmericasPares/> Pares found Venezuelan armed and security forces responsible for the majority, and stated that "no possible victims of political-electoral violence who are part of the official parties or the government bloc of Venezuela were found".<ref name=DiariolasAmericasPares/> In its third report (27 June to 28 July) Pares stated that most of the victims were "members of the main opposition parties", along with 10 journalists, and that over 91% of the violent acts that affected 129 victims were committed by Venezuelan security forces.<ref name=MHCouldCharge/><ref name=Pares3/><ref name=ElDiarioParesFoundation>{{cite news|url=https://eldiario.com/2024/08/14/fundacion-pares-responsabilizo-autoridades-venezuela-violencia-elecciones/|work=[[El Diario de Caracas]]|title=Fundación Pares responsabilizó a las autoridades de Venezuela por la violencia durante las elecciones|language=es|trans-title=Pares Foundation blamed Venezuelan authorities for violence during elections|first=Jose|last=Villa|date=14 August 2024|access-date=19 August 2024}}</ref>

=== CNE rectors ===
In August 2023, the NGO [[Súmate]] denounced that at least 92 candidates for rectors of the CNE were linked to Chavismo, pointing out that Article 9 of the Organic Law of Electoral Processes prohibits members of the Council to have any political affiliation. Sumate also stated that one of the nominees had been convicted for homicide and extortion in 1998, that 46 candidates repeated the candidacy after running in 2021 and that by that time they were deputies of the pro-government National Assembly.<ref>{{cite news |date=5 August 2023 |title=Súmate: "Al menos 92 candidatos al CNE están vinculados al chavismo" |url=https://www.elnacional.com/venezuela/sumate-al-menos-92-candidatos-al-cne-estan-vinculados-al-chavismo/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230805185537/https://www.elnacional.com/venezuela/sumate-al-menos-92-candidatos-al-cne-estan-vinculados-al-chavismo/ |archive-date=5 August 2023 |access-date=6 September 2023 |periodical=[[El Nacional (Venezuela)|El Nacional]]}}</ref> On 15 August, the pro-government National Assembly declared itself in permanent session to appoint the new CNE rectors.<ref>{{cite news |date=16 August 2023 |title=AN electa en 2020 se declaró en sesión permanente para designar a nuevos rectores del CNE |url=https://www.elnacional.com/venezuela/an-electa-en-2020-se-declaro-en-sesion-permanente-para-designar-a-nuevos-rectores-del-cne/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20231119075405/https://www.elnacional.com/venezuela/an-electa-en-2020-se-declaro-en-sesion-permanente-para-designar-a-nuevos-rectores-del-cne/ |archive-date=19 November 2023 |access-date=6 September 2023 |periodical=[[El Nacional (Venezuela)|El Nacional]]}}</ref>

=== Censorship ===
{{Further|Censorship in Venezuela}}
''[[TechRadar]]'' reported that websites, including Wikipedia and voting information websites, were blocked in Venezuela beginning on 28 July.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Castro |first=Chiara |date=31 July 2024 |title=VPN usage in Venezuela soars in the aftermath of presidential elections |url=https://www.techradar.com/pro/vpn/vpn-usage-in-venezuela-soars-in-the-aftermath-of-presidential-elections |website=[[TechRadar]] |access-date=1 August 2024 |archive-date=31 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240731200313/https://www.techradar.com/pro/vpn/vpn-usage-in-venezuela-soars-in-the-aftermath-of-presidential-elections |url-status=live }}</ref>

{{ill|VE Sin Filtro|es}}, a non-governmental organization that monitors internet censorship, reported that more than 60 news providers are blocked in Venezuela, including 17 new sites that were blocked after the election campaigns started.<ref name= VOAonWSJ/><ref>{{cite news |url= https://efectococuyo.com/la-humanidad/bloquean-the-wall-street-journal-en-venezuela/ |work= [[Efecto Cocuyo]] |title= Bloquean The Wall Street Journal en Venezuela |language=es |trans-title= The Wall Street Journal blocked in Venezuela |date= 2 August 2024 |access-date= 7 August 2024}}</ref>

=== Ex Clé  ===
The sanctioned Argentine firm Ex Clé provided the technological platform for voting in the presidential election.<ref name=Patrick-2024>{{Cite web |last=Fitz Patrick |first=Mariel |date=8 August 2024 |title=Los millonarios movimientos de dinero de la empresa argentina proveedora del sistema electoral en Venezuela que activaron las alertas de la UIF |url=https://www.infobae.com/politica/2024/08/08/los-millonarios-movimientos-de-dinero-de-la-empresa-argentina-proveedora-del-sistema-electoral-en-venezuela-que-activaron-las-alertas-de-la-uif/ |access-date=8 August 2024 |website=infobae |language=es-ES |trans-title= The millionaire money movements of the Argentine company that provides the electoral system in Venezuela that triggered the UIF alerts}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://armando.info/como-privatizar-unas-elecciones/|website=Armando.info|title=Cómo privatizar unas elecciones |language=es|trans-title=How to privatize elections|date=18 August 2024|access-date=6 September 2024}}</ref> Significant transactions moving from Venezuela through Ex Clé's accounts in banks in Uruguay and the United States triggered alerts from Argentina's [[Anti-Money Laundering Improvement Act|Anti-Money Laundering Unit]].<ref name="Patrick-2024" /> The firm, which owns the voting machines and electronic counting software, came under suspicion, according to ''[[Infobae]]'', when the Argentine anti-money laundering unit reported "the triangulation of funds (by EX Clé) through third countries without apparent economic justification" and "transfers abroad whose destinations could be questionable", among other concerns according to Argentine Law No. 25,246 on money laundering.<ref name="Patrick-2024" />

== Endorsements ==
{{main|List of endorsements in the 2024 Venezuelan presidential election}}
After she was barred from running, Machado's endorsement of González was an important factor in the election<ref>{{cite news |url= https://cnnespanol.cnn.com/2024/06/18/analisis-maria-corina-machado-edmundo-gonzalez-urrutia-elecciones-venezuela-orix/ |title= 
ANÁLISIS: El factor María Corina Machado, decisivo para las oportunidades de Edmundo González Urrutia en las elecciones de Venezuela|trans-title= Analysis: The Maria Corina Machado factor is decisive for Edmundo Gonzalez Urrutia's chances in Venezuela's elections |first= Anabella |last= Gonzalez |date= 18 June 2024 |access-date= 10 August 2024 |work= [[CNN en Español]] |language=es}}</ref> as he gained support from even former socialist supporters of the government,<ref>{{cite news|url= https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuela-opposition-sees-military-ensuring-respect-vote-results-2024-07-25/ |title= Venezuela candidates close campaigns, opposition trusts military to back result |work= Reuters |date= 25 July 2024 |access-date= 10 August 2024}}</ref> along with support from the Machado-led opposition.<ref>{{cite news |url= https://ca.news.yahoo.com/venezuela-opposition-leader-provides-hope-130720995.html |work= The Canadian Press |title= Venezuela opposition leader provides hope for many, even though she isn't on the presidential ballot |publisher = Associated Press |first1= Regina |last1=Garcia Cano |first2= Fabiola |last2=Sanchez |date= 26 July 2024 |access-date= 10 August 2024}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url= https://www.vozdeamerica.com/a/el-candidato-que-no-queria-ser-presidente-edmundo-gonzalez-eleccion-presidencial-venezuela/7702371.html |work= Voice of America |date= 23 July 2024 |access-date= 10 August 2024 |first= Nicole |last= Kolster |title= La carrera de obstáculos que llevó a Edmundo González a ser candidato presidencial en Venezuela |language=es |trans-title= The obstacle course that led Edmundo González to become a presidential candidate in Venezuela}}</ref>

== Opinion polls ==
{{further|Polls in Venezuela}}
As of July 2024, most polls favored González to win by a wide margin; this trend was particularly true from the [[Polls in Venezuela#2024 presidential election|higher-quality pollsters in Venezuela]].<ref name= NYT24June>{{cite news |url= https://www.nytimes.com/es/2024/06/25/espanol/venezuela-maduro-elecciones-gonzalez.html |title= El presidente de Venezuela acordó ir a las urnas, }}</ref><ref name=Reuters20June>{{cite news |url= https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuelan-presidential-candidates-agree-respect-election-results-main-2024-06-20/ |title= Venezuelan presidential candidates agree to respect election results, main opposition abstains |first= Vivian |last= Sequera |publisher= Reuters |date= 20 June 2024 |access-date= 28 June 2024}}</ref><ref>{{cite journal |url= https://americasquarterly.org/article/political-guarantees-for-all-are-crucial-to-venezuelas-election/ |title= Political Guarantees for All Are Crucial to Venezuela's Election |first= Michael |last= Penfold |date= 28 May 2024 |access-date= 28 June 2024 |journal= [[Americas Quarterly]] |archive-date= 28 June 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240628151632/https://americasquarterly.org/article/political-guarantees-for-all-are-crucial-to-venezuelas-election/ |url-status= live }}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |last=Vyas |first=Kejal |title=A Little-Known Retiree Is Challenging Venezuela's Strongman—and Leading Big in Polls |url=https://www.wsj.com/world/americas/edmundo-gonzalez-venezuela-presidential-candidate-polls-d74d4a9c |access-date=16 July 2024 |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |language=en-US |archive-date=15 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240715163238/https://www.wsj.com/world/americas/edmundo-gonzalez-venezuela-presidential-candidate-polls-d74d4a9c |url-status=live }}</ref>

=== Alleged manipulation of polls ===
{{further-text|[[Polling in Venezuela#2024 presidential election|Polling in Venezuela § 2024 presidential election]]}}
[[File:Election campaign 2024 Venezuela 09.jpg|thumb|upright=1.4|Election campaign of González]]
During the run-up to the election, [[Polls in Venezuela#2024 presidential election|several news outlets reported on the proliferation of polls favoring Maduro]] published since May 2024 by previously unknown polling firms,<ref name= ET28May>{{cite news |url= https://www.eltiempo.com/mundo/venezuela/venezuela-guerra-de-encuestas-por-liderar-voto-para-elecciones-presidenciales-del-28-de-julio-3346982 |language= es |title= ¿Nicolás Maduro o Edmundo González? La 'guerra de encuestas' por quién lidera la intención de voto en elecciones de Venezuela |trans-title= Nicolás Maduro or Edmundo González? The 'poll war' over who leads voting intentions in Venezuelan elections |first= Ana Maria |last= Rodrigues Brazon |date= 28 May 2024 |access-date= 27 June 2024 |work= [[El Tiempo (Colombia)|El Tiempo]] |archive-date= 27 June 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240627173644/https://www.eltiempo.com/mundo/venezuela/venezuela-guerra-de-encuestas-por-liderar-voto-para-elecciones-presidenciales-del-28-de-julio-3346982 |url-status= live }}</ref><ref name=NTN2Jun/><ref name=Medianli>{{cite web|url=https://www.medianalisis.org/seis-encuestadoras-sospechosas-promocionan-coordinadamente-a-nicolas-maduro-como-favorito-para-el-28-j/|title= Seis encuestadoras sospechosas promocionan coordinadamente a Nicolás Maduro como favorito para el 28-J |date=3 July 2024|website=Medianalisis|access-date=15 July 2024|quote=DataViva, Ideadatos, Insight by Contrapunto, Data Política Consultores, Encuestadora Paramétrica y Mass Behavior Research|archive-date=15 July 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240715103956/https://www.medianalisis.org/seis-encuestadoras-sospechosas-promocionan-coordinadamente-a-nicolas-maduro-como-favorito-para-el-28-j/|url-status=live |language=es |trans-title= Six suspicious pollsters are promoting Nicolás Maduro as the favorite for 28 July}}</ref> fuelling concerns that some polls were being used as [[Bolivarian propaganda|propaganda tools]] by [[Chavismo]].<ref name="www.lapatilla.com">{{cite web|url=https://www.lapatilla.com/2024/07/15/la-guerra-de-encuestas-se-desata-en-venezuela-en-un-clima-de-propaganda-y-desinformacion/|title=La 'guerra de encuestas' se desata en Venezuela en un clima de propaganda y desinformación|access-date=16 July 2024|website=www.lapatilla.com|archive-date=16 July 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240716010122/https://www.lapatilla.com/2024/07/15/la-guerra-de-encuestas-se-desata-en-venezuela-en-un-clima-de-propaganda-y-desinformacion/|url-status=live |language=es |trans-title= The 'poll war' breaks out in Venezuela in a climate of propaganda and disinformation}}</ref> These poll results differed significantly from those published by more traditional pollsters, which showed Maduro trailing.<ref name= NTN2Jun/>
	
According to [[Medianálisis]], [[Efecto Cocuyo]], Cazadores de Fake News and Probox, working with the Latin American Center for Investigative Journalism, these polls were being used to discredit opposition candidates<ref name=Medianli/><ref name= NTN2Jun/> Polls showing Maduro ahead were predominantly disseminated by media outlets claimed to be pro-Maduro, such as [[Globovisión]], [[El Universal (Venezuela)|El Universal]], {{ill|Venezuela News|es}}, [[Correo del Orinoco (2009)|Correo del Orinoco]] and [[Notitarde|NotiTarde]].<ref name="Gutiérrez-2024a">{{cite web|url=http://efectococuyo.com/cocuyo-chequea/ics-latam-encuestadora-inconsistette/|title=ICS resucitó para publicar encuesta inconsistente con 56,9% para Maduro|access-date=16 July 2024|last=Gutiérrez|first=Jeanfreddy|date=11 July 2024|website=Efecto Cocuyo|language=es|trans-title= ICS resurrected to publish inconsistent survey with 56.9% for Maduro|archive-date=16 July 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240716013432/https://efectococuyo.com/cocuyo-chequea/ics-latam-encuestadora-inconsistette/|url-status=live}}</ref>
	
Six pollsters consistently placed opposition candidate González in first place, while others placed Maduro in front. Well-known pollsters in the Venezuelan political sphere, such as Datanálisis, Datincorp, Delphos, and Consultores 21, along with the emerging Poder y Estrategia, indicated that Urrutia had more than 50% of voting intentions.<ref name="www.lapatilla.com" /> Results by lesser-known firms Hinterlaces, ICS Latam, IMC Orientación, and DataViva, among others, showed Maduro with between 54% and 70% of votes.<ref name="www.lapatilla.com" /> Results by CECA Consultores showed a technical tie slightly favoring the opposition.<ref name="www.lapatilla.com" />

On 28 May, [[Colombia]]n newspaper ''[[El Tiempo (Colombia)|El Tiempo]]'' named IdeaDatos and Data Viva as examples of suspicious pollsters.<ref name= ET28May/> [[NTN24]] singled out Insight in June 2024, writing that "Eight of ten [recent] polls give the winner to the opposition candidate, Edmundo González Urrutia, and the only two that give victory to ...&nbsp;Maduro, are unknown firms and their social media accounts are recent", adding that IdeaDatos and PoliAnalítico "actively campaign for Nicolás Maduro".<ref name= NTN2Jun>{{cite news |url= https://www.ntn24.com/noticias-politica/guerra-de-encuestas-estos-son-los-diez-sondeos-que-perfilan-al-proximo-presidente-de-venezuela-493950 |title= Guerra de encuestas: Estos son los diez sondeos que perfilan al próximo Presidente de Venezuela |language= es   |date= 2 June 2024 |first= Maryorin |last= Méndez |trans-title= Poll war: These are the ten polls that outline the next President of Venezuela |publisher= [[NTN24]] |access-date= 27 June 2024 |archive-date= 27 June 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240627173647/https://www.ntn24.com/noticias-politica/guerra-de-encuestas-estos-son-los-diez-sondeos-que-perfilan-al-proximo-presidente-de-venezuela-493950 |url-status= live }}</ref><ref name= EN20June>{{cite news |url= https://www.elnacional.com/opinion/se-activa-la-guerra-de-encuestas/ |title= Se activa la guerra de encuestas |language= es |trans-title= The poll war is activated |first= Marcos |last= Hernández López |date= 20 June 2024 |publisher= [[El Nacional (Venezuela)|El Nacional]] |access-date= 27 June 2024 |archive-date= 20 June 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240620085122/https://www.elnacional.com/opinion/se-activa-la-guerra-de-encuestas/ |url-status= live }}</ref>

Venezuelan independent journalism website [[Efecto Cocuyo]] published several detailed exposés of pollsters, alleging faulty methodology, systematic bias in favor of Maduro, and repeated dissemination of their polls by pro-Maduro outlets. Polling firms alleged to be unreliable include IdeaDatos, CMIDE, Parametrica, Hinterlaces, IMC Orientación, and ICS Latam.<ref name= EC12June>{{cite news |url= https://efectococuyo-com.translate.goog/cocuyo-chequea/idea-datos-inconsistente-tercera-vez/ |title= IdeaDatos le otorga 56,1% a Maduro en su tercera encuesta, repitiendo vacíos empresariales y estadísticas |first= Jeanfreddy |last= Gutiérrez |date= 12 June 2024 |publisher= [[Efecto Cocuyo]] |work= Cocuyo Chequea (Cocuyo Factcheck) |language=es|trans-title= IdeaDatos gives 56.1% to Maduro in its third survey, repeating business gaps and statistics |access-date= 27 June 2024}}</ref><ref name= EC12April>{{cite news |url= https://efectococuyo.com/cocuyo-chequea/data-viva-maduro-julio-2023/ |title= Inconsistente: encuestadora alabada por Maduro fue creada en julio de 2023 |first= Jeanfreddy |last= Gutiérrez |date= 12 June 2024 |publisher= [[Efecto Cocuyo]] |work= Cocuyo Chequea (Cocuyo Factcheck) |language= es |trans-title= Inconsistent: pollster praised by Maduro was created in July 2023 |access-date= 27 June 2024 |archive-date= 27 June 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240627173644/https://efectococuyo.com/cocuyo-chequea/data-viva-maduro-julio-2023/ |url-status= live }}</ref><ref name=EC14May>{{cite news |url= https://efectococuyo.com/cocuyo-chequea/cmide-501-encuesta-memes/ |title= Encuestadora CMIDE 50.1 es una cuenta de memes, fútbol y poesía que borró todos sus posts anteriores |first= Jeanfreddy |last= Gutiérrez |date= 14 May 2024 |publisher= [[Efecto Cocuyo]] |work= Cocuyo Chequea (Cocuyo Factcheck) |language= es |trans-title= Pollster CMIDE 50.1 is a meme, football and poetry account that deleted all its previous posts |access-date= 27 June 2024 |archive-date= 27 June 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240627183822/https://efectococuyo.com/cocuyo-chequea/cmide-501-encuesta-memes/ |url-status= live }}</ref>

=== Exit polls ===
An [[exit poll]] by [[Edison Research]]—which, according to ''[[The Guardian]]'', "conducts high-profile election polling in the US and other countries"—gave González 65% of the vote and Maduro 31%.<ref name=KnifeEdge/><ref name=ReutersBreakOut>{{cite news| first=Vivian| last=Sequera | title=Venezuelan protests break out as government claims election win | work=Reuters | date=29 July 2024 | url=https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/government-opposition-both-claim-venezuela-election-win-official-results-2024-07-29/ | access-date=29 July 2024}}</ref>
