== Results ==
{{Commons category|Tally sheets of the Vote Count for the 2024 Presidential Elections in Venezuela|italic=no}}

According to ''[[The New York Times]]'', "Maduro was declared the winner in a presidential vote ...&nbsp;marred by irregularities"; these irregularities included "polling places [that] refused to release paper tallies of the electronic vote count, and ...&nbsp;widespread reports of fraud and voter intimidation", results that varied "wildly" from public opinion polls and voting center samples, "major irregularities and problems at those voting centers", and blocking of legal monitors from polling places.<ref name="NYTWhatToKnow">{{cite news |first= Anatoly |last= Kurmanaev |title= Here's what to know about Venezuela's flawed election |url= https://www.nytimes.com/2024/07/29/world/americas/venezuela-election-takeaways.html |work= The New York Times |date= 29 July 2024 |access-date= 29 July 2024 |archive-date= 29 July 2024 |archive-url= https://archive.today/20240729161527/https://www.nytimes.com/2024/07/29/world/americas/venezuela-election-takeaways.html |url-status= live |url-access=subscription}}</ref>

The [[Carter Center]], which sent a small team of observers, stated that there was a "complete lack of transparency" and that the election "did not meet international standards", "cannot be considered democratic", and had occurred in "an environment of restricted freedoms" and "clear bias" from electoral authorities; they could not verify the results from the electoral authority.<ref name=CarterCenterBlasts/><ref name= CarterCenterPressRelease/>

The [[United Nations]] sent a small panel of experts who spent a month in Caracas, and was expected to produce only a confidential report for internal purposes. It released its report publicly on 13 August, and according to the Associated Press, "harshly criticized" the CNE for declaring Maduro the winner before having table-level results.<ref name=UNBlasts>{{cite news |url= https://apnews.com/article/venezuela-crackdown-detentions-united-nations-human-rights-cd2555ec2255f6a804a671f8723bc15b |publisher= Associated Press |date= 13 August 2024 |title= UN expert panel sent to Venezuela blasts lack of transparency in presidential elections |first= Joshua |last= Goodman |access-date= 14 August 2024}}</ref> The report stated that the premature declaration of a winner "had no precedent in contemporary democratic elections", and that the election process lacked “basic transparency and integrity".<ref name= UNExperts/> It concluded that the tally sheets produced by the opposition appeared to have security features that indicate "a key transparency safeguard may be available, as intended, with respect to any officially released results".<ref name=UNBlasts/> Venezuela's Foreign Minister [[Yván Gil]] rejected the report as false and called it part of "a series of lies" and a "far right" plot.<ref>{{cite news |url= https://www.voanews.com/a/venezuela-attacks-un-with-propaganda-accusation-for-reporting-election-transparency-issues-/7745957.html |work= Voice of America News |title= Venezuela attacks UN with 'propaganda' accusation for reporting election transparency issues |first= William |last= Echols |date= 16 August 2024 |access-date= 17 August 2024}}</ref>

===Tally sheets===
Opposition groups stated their intent the day after the election to publish the detailed electoral results in the form of scanned copies of the tally sheets ({{lang|es|actas de escrutinio}}) and other digital formats<ref name="OAS_report_VE_pres_elec_DECO">

{{cite web |title= Informe del Departamento para la Cooperación y Observación Electoral (DECO) de la Secretaría para el Fortalecimiento de la Democracia de la OEA sobre la elección presidencial de Venezuela para el Secretario General Luis Almagro |language= es |publisher= Organization of American States |date= 30 July 2024 |trans-title= Report of the Department for Electoral Cooperation and Observation (DECO) of the Secretariat for the Strengthening of Democracy of the OAS on the presidential election of Venezuela for the Secretary General Luis Almagro|url= https://www.oas.org/fpdb/press/Informe-al-SG-sobre-Elecciones-Venezuela-2024-30-de-julio-para-distribuir-(1).pdf|archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240730170718/https://www.oas.org/fpdb/press/Informe-al-SG-sobre-Elecciones-Venezuela-2024-30-de-julio-para-distribuir-(1).pdf |archive-date= 30 July 2024 |access-date= 10 August 2024 |id= Wikidata [[:d:Q128129159]] }}</ref>{{rp|21}} on a website ''resultadospresidencialesvenezuela2024.com''<ref name="opposition_results_website">{{Cite web|url=https://resultadospresidencialesvenezuela2024.com/|title=Informacion de Centros y mesas de votacion|website=resultadospresidencialesvenezuela2024.com}}</ref><ref name= APReview/> where registered voters can check the results for their place of voting. According to ''[[La Patilla]]'', Venezuelan authorities blocked access to the server on Venezuelan internet providers. ''La Patilla'' recommended the use of [[Virtual private network|VPN]]s for accessing the website.<ref name="LaPatilla_how2access_electoral_records">{{cite web|url=https://www.lapatilla.com/2024/07/30/como-acceder-a-la-pagina-web-para-verificar-las-actas-electorales-que-maduro-bloqueo-en-venezuela/|title=Cómo acceder a la página web para verificar las actas electorales que Maduro bloqueó en Venezuela|work=[[La Patilla]]|date=30 July 2024|language=es}}</ref> The opposition reported that, on 31 July, more than 44&nbsp;million website attacks were prevented, with more than 32&nbsp;million users consulting the database in 24 hours.<ref>{{cite news |url= https://eldiario.com/2024/08/01/comando-con-venezuela-mitigaron-millones-ataques-contra-la-web-revision-de-actas/amp/# |work= El Diario |date= 1 August 2024 |access-date= 1 August 2024 |language=es |title= Comando Con Venezuela informó que mitigaron más de 44 millones de ataques contra la web de revisión de actas |trans-title= Comando Con Venezuela reported that they mitigated more than 44 million attacks against the website for reviewing records}}</ref>

On 1 August, presidents [[Gabriel Boric]] of Chile, [[Gustavo Petro]] of Colombia, [[Lula da Silva]] of Brazil, and [[Andrés Manuel López Obrador]] of Mexico called for the CNE to publish its version of the tally sheets and the full vote counts.<ref name= BMCCall /><ref name= FPMomentofTruth/> The following day, the [[Supreme Tribunal of Justice (Venezuela)|Supreme Tribunal of Justice]] asked the CNE to provide the nationwide tally sheets and summed reports within three calendar days.<ref>{{cite news |title=TSJ solicita al CNE consignar actas de escrutinios a nivel nacional y las actas de totalización|trans-title=The Supreme Tribunal of Justice requests the National Electoral Council to publish the national level tally sheets and reports of totals|work=[[Efecto Cocuyo]]|language=es|date=2 August 2024|access-date=20 August 2024|url=https://efectococuyo.com/politica/tsj-solicita-al-cne-consignar-actas-de-escrutinios-a-nivel-nacional-y-las-actas-de-totalizacion/|archive-url=https://archive.today/20240803111138/https://efectococuyo.com/politica/tsj-solicita-al-cne-consignar-actas-de-escrutinios-a-nivel-nacional-y-las-actas-de-totalizacion|archive-date=3 August 2024|id=Wikidata [[:d:Q128435622]]|url-status=live}}</ref>

===Parallel vote tabulation===
In the AltaVista PVT project with a [[Preregistration (science)|preregistered]] [[sampling (statistics)|statistical sampling]] method of [[quick count|parallel vote tabulation]],<ref name="Figueiredo_method_vote_counts_limited_integrity">{{cite web |first1=Dalson |last1= Figueiredo Filho|first2=Jose Antonio |last2= Gomez Duarte (pseudonym) |first3=Raphael |last3= Nishimura |first4= Walter |last4= Mebane |author4-link=Walter Mebane|date= 28 July 2024 |title= Estimating Vote Counts with Limited Electoral Integrity |url= https://storage.googleapis.com/project-pvt-2.appspot.com/public/Alta_Vista_PPA.pdf |publisher= Google apis|archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240802012651/https://storage.googleapis.com/project-pvt-2.appspot.com/public/Alta_Vista_PPA.pdf |archive-date= 2 August 2024 |access-date= 10 August 2024|id= Wikidata [[:d:Q128304770]]}}</ref> a team of statisticians applied their method by photographing results from 997 polling stations and inferring the national vote shares. They found 66.1% for González and 31.4% for Maduro, each with an [[margin of error|error margin]] of 0.5%. The participation rate was estimated as 60.1%.<ref name="AtlanticDictatorLies">{{cite news |url= https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2024/07/venezuela-stolen-election-interview-leopoldo-lopez/679305/ |work=[[The Atlantic]] |date= 31 July 2024 |access-date= 31 July 2024| title= Venezuela's Dictator Can't Even Lie Well |first= Anne |last= Applebaum |archive-url=https://archive.today/20240731183026/https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2024/07/venezuela-stolen-election-interview-leopoldo-lopez/679305|archive-date=31 July 2024|url-status=live|quote= In the hours after the polls closed, much of the international media had refrained from stating the obvious. 'BREAKING:,' the Associated Press tweeted on Monday. 'Venezuela's President Nicolás Maduro is declared the winner in the presidential election amid opposition claims of irregularities.' But by Tuesday morning, it was absolutely clear that the election was not merely irregular or tainted or disputed: The election had been stolen.}}</ref><ref name="AltaVista_PVT_results">{{cite web |first1=Dalson |last1= Figueiredo Filho |first2= Jose Antonio |last2= Gomez Duarte (pseudonym) |first3= Raphael |last3= Nishimura |first4= Walter |last4=Mebane |author-link4= Walter Mebane |date= 31 July 2024 |title= AltaVista PVT Results |publisher= Metabase app|url= https://supervisiondev2.metabaseapp.com/public/dashboard/6b2f7b3b-16ec-4af6-84c7-69c39ee2139d?tab=16-english|archive-url= https://archive.today/20240802113205/https://supervisiondev2.metabaseapp.com/public/dashboard/6b2f7b3b-16ec-4af6-84c7-69c39ee2139d?tab=16-english|archive-date= 2 August 2024|access-date= 10 August 2024|id= Wikidata [[:d:Q128304783]]|publication-date=31 July 2024}}</ref>

===Turnout and voter changes===
According to ''[[The New York Times]]'', government officials believed that "a combination of high turnout among loyalists and suppressing the vote for the opposition" would assure a win for the incumbent party. But many voters who traditionally had supported the government had left Venezuela or had "turned from Mr. Maduro", so that "the financial muscle of an oil state to bring supporters to the polls" failed to produce the desired result. Efforts by the Maduro government to revive economic growth by privatizing the economy led to reduced public spending, including the handouts and social services traditionally used to mobilize the vote. In previous campaigns, one PSUV organizer explained, the government "gave out everything from motorbikes to refrigerators", while in this election campaign, "all she got was boxes of poor-quality food and house paint".<ref name="Kurmanaev-NYT-6-8-2024">{{cite news |last1=Kurmanaev |first1=Anatoly |title=Venezuela's Strongman Was Confident of Victory. Then Came the Shock. |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2024/08/06/world/americas/venezuela-election-maduro.html |access-date=8 August 2024 |work=New York Times |date=6 August 2024 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240807014650/https://www.nytimes.com/2024/08/06/world/americas/venezuela-election-maduro.html |archive-date= 7 August 2024 }}</ref>

=== Results announced by the National Electoral Council (CNE) ===
[[File:Elvis Amoroso.jpg|thumb|left|upright=0.8|[[Elvis Amoroso]], head of CNE, Venezuelan's electoral body]]
The CNE announced initial results on 29 July.<ref name="AlbaCTP_CNE_Maduro_victory_5120">{{cite news |title= CNE announced Nicolás Maduro Moros' victory with 51.20% |publisher= [[ALBA]] |url= https://www.albatcp.org/en/2024/07/29/cne-announced-nicolas-maduro-moros-victory-with-51-20/ |archive-url= https://archive.today/20240731163346/https://www.albatcp.org/en/2024/07/29/cne-announced-nicolas-maduro-moros-victory-with-51-20 |archive-date= 31 July 2024|date= 29 July 2024 |access-date= 10 August 2024 |id= Wikidata [[:d:Q128211222]]|url-status=live}}</ref> As of 21 August, the CNE had not released any tally sheets or voter data to support its results.<ref name=GuardianPressureGrows/><ref name= NPRContestedElection>{{cite news |publisher= NPR |date= 30 July 2024 |access-date= 30 July 2024 |url=https://www.npr.org/2024/07/29/nx-s1-5055646/venezuelas-authoritarian-leader-claims-victory-but-opposition-cries-foul |title= Protesters take to the streets in Venezuela over contested presidential election |work= All Things Considered |first1= John |last1= Otis |first2= Carrie |last2= Kahn}}</ref> On 29 July, CNE head [[Elvis Amoroso]] alleged that CNE had been the victim of a [[cyberattack]] and accused the opposition of orchestrating it;<ref>{{cite news |url= https://dolartoday.com/fiscal-saab-abre-investigacion-a-maria-corina-machado-por-supuesto-ataque-informatico-desde-macedonia-del-norte/ |work= DolarToday |date= 20 July 2024 |access-date= 31 July 2024 |title= Fiscal Saab abre investigación a María Corina Machado por supuesto ataque informático desde Macedonia del Norte |language=es |trans-title= Prosecutor Saab opens investigation into Maria Corina Machado for alleged cyber attack from North Macedonia}}</ref> no evidence was presented.<ref name=ElPaisIrPresos/><ref name= BarronsNoEvidence>{{cite news |url= https://www.barrons.com/news/no-evidence-of-venezuela-vote-hacking-says-carter-center-mission-chief-02e02904 |title= 'No Evidence' Of Venezuela Vote Hacking, Says Carter Center Mission Chief |first= Javier |last= Tovar |work= Barrons |publisher= Agence France-Presse|date= 7 August 2024 |access-date= 7 August 2024}}</ref> On both 31 July and 1 August, the CNE announced that it would release the second bulletin of the results.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Patiño |first1=Juan Pablo |title=CNE venezolano canceló, sin explicación, la entrega del segundo boletín de las elecciones |url=https://www.elcolombiano.com/internacional/cne-venezolano-cancelo-sin-explicacion-la-entrega-del-segundo-boletin-de-las-elecciones-NF25134696 |access-date=2 August 2024 |work=www.elcolombiano.com |date=1 August 2024 |language=es|trans-title= Venezuelan CNE canceled, without explanation, the delivery of the second bulletin of the elections}}</ref> On 2 August, the CNE announced a second bulletin of votes, still in favor of Maduro, but still without tally sheets or other polling station level details.<ref>{{cite news |url= https://www.infobae.com/venezuela/2024/08/02/fraude-en-venezuela-sin-mostrar-las-actas-el-cne-chavista-ratifico-la-cuestionada-victoria-de-nicolas-maduro/ |work= Infobae |date= 2 August 2024 |access-date= 2 August 2024 |language= en |title= Fraude en Venezuela: sin mostrar las actas, el CNE chavista ratificó la cuestionada victoria de Nicolás Maduro |trans-title= Fraud in Venezuela: without showing the minutes, the Chavista CNE ratified the questioned victory of Nicolás Maduro}}</ref> Jennie Lincoln, who headed the [[Carter Center]] observation of the election, rejected the results again as not being transparent, and stated that Venezuela was able to provide individual table tallies as they had done so in past elections.<ref>{{Cite news|url= https://www.ntn24.com/noticias-politica/si-es-un-numero-global-que-no-tiene-explicacion-de-las-mesas-tampoco-es-transparente-centro-carter-en-ntn24-sobre-segundo-boletin-del-cne-505966|title='Si es un número global que no tiene explicación de las mesas, tampoco es transparente': Centro Carter en NTN24 sobre segundo boletín del CNE|work= [[NTN24]] |date= 2 August 2024 |access-date= 4 August 2024 |language= es |trans-title= 'If it is a global number that has no explanation of the tables, it is not transparent either': Carter Center on NTN24 about the second CNE bulletin}}</ref>

Journalists from ''[[The Washington Post]]'' analyzed the tally sheet scans published online by the opposition, and looked at "hundreds" of physical paper tally sheets stored by the opposition in secret locations. The journalists interviewed several of the people whose signatures appear on the physical tally sheets, and stated that the physical tally sheets appear to be authentic. They state that the physical tally sheets match the corresponding online scans. The journalists analysed 23,720 of the online tally sheets—those whose QR codes they were successfully able to extract from the images, constituting 97% of the online total, finding that González won 67% of the vote and Maduro 30%.<ref name="WAPOMaduroLost">{{cite news|title= Maduro lost election, tallies collected by Venezuela's opposition show |date= 4 August 2024 |access-date= 5 August 2024 |newspaper= [[The Washington Post]] |url= https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2024/08/04/maduro-gonzalez-election-actas-analysis/ |first1= Samantha |last1= Schmidt |first2= Steven |last2= Rich |first3= Ana Vanessa |last3= Herrero |first4= Maria Luisa |last4= Paul|archive-url=https://archive.today/20240805025959/https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2024/08/04/maduro-gonzalez-election-actas-analysis|archive-date=5 August 2024|url-status=live }}</ref>

Attorney {{ill|Juan Carlos Delpino|es}}, one of the five CNE rectors,<ref name=InfobaeCNERector>{{cite news|url=https://www.infobae.com/america/agencias/2024/08/26/un-rector-del-cne-de-venezuela-denuncia-la-falta-de-transparencia-y-veracidad-de-los-resultados-electorales/|work=[[Infobae]]|access-date=26 August 2024|date=26 August 2024|language=es|title=Un rector del CNE de Venezuela denuncia la falta de transparencia y veracidad' de los resultados electorales|trans-title= A rector of the CNE of Venezuela denounces the 'lack of transparency and veracity' of the electoral results}}</ref><ref name=NBCElectoralOfficial>{{cite news|url=https://www.nbcnews.com/news/latino/venezuelan-electoral-official-condemns-grave-lack-transparency-maduros-rcna168184|date=26 August 2024|access-date=26 August 2024|work= NBC News|title=Venezuelan electoral official condemns 'grave lack of transparency' in Nicolás Maduro's re-election|publisher=Associated Press}}</ref><ref name="CNE_Authorities_2024Apr">{{cite Q|Q129846732|url-status=live}}</ref> went into hiding after the election. Delpino stated in an interview with ''The New York Times'' that he had seen no evidence of a Maduro victory, expressing personal shame that the CNE he had agreed to serve on had "failed the country". Delpino noted irregularities in the election including the absence of published vote tallies from the CNE, and a lack of CNE pre-election meetings that allowed CNE head Amoroso to make "unilateral" decisions.<ref name=NYTNoEvidence>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2024/08/26/world/americas/maduro-venezuela-election-results.html|work=The New York Times|date=26 August 2024|access-date=26 August 2024|title=No Evidence That Maduro Won, a Top Venezuelan Election Official Says|author=Turkewitz, Julie}}</ref><ref name=ElPaisDelpinoJun24>{{cite news|url=https://elpais.com/america/2024-06-12/un-rector-del-cne-de-venezuela-acusa-al-presidente-del-organo-electoral-de-retirar-la-observacion-europea-sin-consultar.html|work=El País|access-date=26 August 2024|language=es|title=Un rector del CNE de Venezuela acusa al presidente del órgano electoral de retirar la observación europea sin consultar|trans-title=A director of the CNE of Venezuela accuses the president of the electoral body of withdrawing European observation without consulting|date=12 June 2024|author=Moleiro, Alonso}}</ref>

==== Sequences of zeros in the CNE values ====
[[File:Decimales de los resultados del CNE de las elecciones presidenciales de Venezuela de 2024.gif|right|thumbnail|300x300px|Table showing percentages provided by the [[Consejo Nacional Electoral (Venezuela)|Consejo Nacional Electoral]] (CNE) to varying levels of rounding]]

The CNE's 29 July counts of 5,150,092 votes for Maduro, 4,445,978 votes for González, and 462,704 other votes and a total of 10,058,774 votes,<ref name="AlbaCTP_CNE_Maduro_victory_5120" /> released on 29 July 2024, correspond, to a precision of 5 decimal places, to 51.20000%, 44.20000%, and 4.60000%, respectively.<ref name="AlbaCTP_CNE_Maduro_victory_5120" /> In the 2 August CNE results, the invalid/null vote count is 0.41000% at a precision of 5 decimal places.<ref name="EfectoCocuyo_CNE_2nd_bulletin" /> These sequences of successive zeros were discussed as a possible sign of fraud.<ref name="ElPais_Who_won_in_VE">{{cite news|date=2 August 2024|title=¿Quién ganó en Venezuela? Los datos de la oposición son más verificables que los oficiales|language=es|trans-title=Who won in Venezuela? The opposition data are more verifiable than the official data|first=Kiko|last=LLaneras|url=https://elpais.com/america/2024-08-02/quien-gano-en-venezuela-los-datos-de-la-oposicion-son-mas-verificables-que-los-oficiales.html|work=[[El País]]|archive-url=https://archive.today/20240802072246/https://elpais.com/america/2024-08-02/quien-gano-en-venezuela-los-datos-de-la-oposicion-son-mas-verificables-que-los-oficiales.html#selection-169.0-169.2|archive-date=2 August 2024|access-date=20 August 2024|id= Wikidata [[:d:Q128332901]]|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name="ElEspectador_decimal_places" >{{cite news |url= https://www.elespectador.com/mundo/elecciones-venezuela-2024/por-que-ver-estos-decimales-nos-ayudaria-a-hablar-de-un-fraude-en-venezuela/|date= 31 July 2024 |title= ¿Por qué ver estos decimales ayudaría a hablar de un fraude en Venezuela? |work= [[El Espectador]] |language=es |trans-title=Why would seeing these decimals help to talk about fraud in Venezuela?|first=Camilo|last=Gómez Forero|id= Wikidata [[:d:Q128211710]] |archive-url= https://archive.today/20240731180640/https://www.elespectador.com/mundo/elecciones-venezuela-2024/por-que-ver-estos-decimales-nos-ayudaria-a-hablar-de-un-fraude-en-venezuela |archive-date= 31 July 2024 |access-date= 10 August 2024|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name="TTao_oddsII_VE">{{cite web |title= What are the odds, II: the Venezuelan presidential election |date= 2 August 2024 |access-date= 10 August 2024 |url= https://terrytao.wordpress.com/2024/08/02/what-are-the-odds-ii-the-venezuelan-presidential-election/ |publisher= terrytao.wordpress.com
|id= Wikidata [[:d:Q128334636]]|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240802195003/https://terrytao.wordpress.com/2024/08/02/what-are-the-odds-ii-the-venezuelan-presidential-election |archive-date= 2 August 2024|url-status=live|first=Terence|last=Tao|author-link=Terence Tao}}</ref>  Argentine journalist Matías Mowzet noticed that writing the three values as percentages [[rounding|rounded]] to five decimal places gave sequences ending in four zeros for each of the three values. The votes for Maduro, González and others correspond to the percentages 51.20000%, 44.20000% and 4.6000%, respectively.<ref name="ElEspectador_decimal_places" />

For the vote counts to correspond to percentages that have zeros in the second to fifth decimal places is an unlikely coincidence,<ref name="Infobae_burdo">{{cite news |title= El burdo cálculo matemático en la información oficial que aumenta las sospechas sobre la manipulación de la elección en Venezuela |work= Infobae |language= es |date= 30 July 2024 |id= Wikidata [[:d:Q128212016]]|url-status=live|trans-title=The crude mathematical calculation in the official information increases suspicions about the manipulation of the election in Venezuela |url= https://www.infobae.com/venezuela/2024/07/30/el-burdo-calculo-matematico-en-la-informacion-oficial-que-aumenta-las-sospechas-sobre-la-manipulacion-de-la-eleccion-en-venezuela/|archive-url= https://archive.today/20240731180614/https://www.infobae.com/venezuela/2024/07/30/el-burdo-calculo-matematico-en-la-informacion-oficial-que-aumenta-las-sospechas-sobre-la-manipulacion-de-la-eleccion-en-venezuela|archive-date= 31 July 2024|access-date= 10 August 2024}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |date=31 July 2024 |title=The decimals of the published results of the elections in Venezuela: what the official figures have been and what suspicions they raise among experts · Maldita.es - Journalism to keep you from being deceived |url=https://maldita.es/malditateexplica/20240731/decimales-resultados-elecciones-venezuela/ |access-date=1 August 2024 |website=Maldita.es—Journalism to keep you from being deceived}}</ref> with a probability of around one in a hundred million, as discussed by Kiko Llaneras, a statistician writing in ''[[El País]]'',<ref name="ElEspectador_decimal_places" /> mathematician [[Terence Tao]],<ref name="TTao_oddsII_VE" /> and statistician [[Andrew Gelman]].<ref name="CNN_after_VE_vote">{{cite Q|Q129258054|url-status=live}}</ref>  ''[[El Espectador]]'' interpreted this as likely fraud.<ref name="ElEspectador_decimal_places" /> ''[[Infobae]]'' also stated that improbability raised suspicion about the 29 July CNE statement of the results.<ref name="Infobae_burdo" />

Tao described a [[Bayesian statistics|Bayesian]] analysis considering the [[null hypothesis]] that the 29 July CNE counts are authentic, and the alternative hypothesis that they are fraudulent. He found that the probability of the official counts occurring is "extremely small" in the case of the counts being authentic (the null hypothesis) and that there is a "plausible causal chain ... that leads to an elevated probability" of the official counts occurring for the hypothesis of manipulation (the alternative hypothesis). The causal chain of the manipulation hypothesis is that a decision was made to manipulate the data, officials followed orders to report vote counts based on a given rounded percentage, and other officials raised no objections to the fabricated counts.<ref name="TTao_oddsII_VE" />

On 2 August, [[Elvis Amoroso]] made a new statement, asserting that 96.87% of the ballots had been counted, accounting for 12,335,884 valid votes and 50,785 null/invalid votes, giving a total of 12,386,669 votes cast,<ref name="EfectoCocuyo_CNE_2nd_bulletin" /><ref>{{cite web |date=2 August 2024 |title=Results of the elections in Venezuela 2024, live, The CNE again declares Maduro the winner without showing the ballots with 96.87% counted |url=https://elpais.com/america/2024-08-02/resultados-de-las-elecciones-en-venezuela-2024-en-vivo.html |access-date=2 August 2024 |website=[[El País]]}}</ref> which corresponds to 0.41000% of null/invalid votes at a precision of 5 decimal places.

=== Results announced by the Democratic Unitary Platform (PUD) ===
[[File:Mesas Gonzalez to Maduro ratio data release version1.svg|thumb|upright=1.0|González-to-Maduro vote ratio versus registered voters per mesa; the ratios scatter around one in small voting places and from one to ten in large voting places (PUD data version 1).<ref name="resultadosconvzla_csv_mesas_v1" />]]
A database which allowed Venezuelans to use their national identity card to verify vote tallies was released by the [[Unitary Platform|PUD]] on 30 July, which they said reflected 73% of the votes cast. The database shows scans of the vote tally sheets, with votes cast for each candidate at each voting place gathered during the [[#Electoral process|electoral process]]. As of 21 August,<ref name=GuardianPressureGrows/> the government has not released a similar accounting, which the [[Carter Center]] said was needed.<ref name=WSJElectionDatabase>{{cite news|url=https://www.wsj.com/world/americas/venezuelas-opposition-releases-election-database-claims-big-victory-over-strongman-maduro-fee5bc0c|work=The Wall Street Journal|url-access=subscription|date=30 July 2024|access-date=30 July 2024|title=Venezuela's Opposition Releases Election Database; Claims Big Victory Over Strongman Maduro|first1=Kejal|last1=Vyas|first2=Ryan|last2=Dubé|archive-date=30 July 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240730205829/https://www.wsj.com/world/americas/venezuelas-opposition-releases-election-database-claims-big-victory-over-strongman-maduro-fee5bc0c|url-status=live|quote=The Venezuelan opposition has moved to show concrete evidence that the election was stolen. ... The opposition said it had collected data from 73% of the country's voting stations on its own and compiled it in a publicly accessible database on Tuesday. Using their national identification, Venezuelans can sign in and review a scanned tally sheet from their voting station showing how many votes went to each candidate. ... 'I found mine, the proof is there,' said Celina Ramirez, an opposition supporter who said she was able to log into the website to locate the tally sheet from her east Caracas voting center, which she said showed González receiving the lion's share of votes. 'There's no way the regime can fool everyone with their tricks,' she added ... The Carter Center, one of the few international organizations invited to monitor the elections, has urged Venezuela's government to release comprehensive polling data at the local level, which is needed to assess the electoral process. ...The opposition hopes the release of the database will increase pressure on Maduro's autocratic regime to make public the detailed results of the election.}} Also available from [https://www.msn.com/en-us/news/world/venezuela-s-maduro-moves-to-silence-opposition-after-disputed-election/ar-BB1qTSWi MSN] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240730214546/https://www.msn.com/en-us/news/world/venezuela-s-maduro-moves-to-silence-opposition-after-disputed-election/ar-BB1qTSWi |date=30 July 2024 }}.</ref><ref name= APPaperSheets/> Opposition groups released a [[Comma-separated values|CSV]]-format file with the polling-station level data for 24,532 polling stations.<ref name="resultadosconvzla_csv_mesas_v1">{{cite web |website= resultadosconvzla.com |date= 2 August 2024 |title= Results of the 2024 Venezuelan presidential election: PUD version 1 |url= https://static.resultadosconvzla.com/RESULTADOS_2024_CSV_V1.csv|archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240802231646/https://static.resultadosconvzla.com/RESULTADOS_2024_CSV_V1.csv |archive-date= 2 August 2024
|id= Wikidata [[:d:Q128342566]]|url-status=live |access-date= 10 August 2024}}</ref> At the mesa (table) level in version 1 of the tally sheets, 86.60% of the mesas had more votes for González than for Maduro, 0.17% tied exactly, and 13.23% had more votes for Maduro.<ref name="resultadosconvzla_csv_mesas_v1" />

An independent analysis of the count released by PUD was conducted by the Associated Press and corroborated the opposition results. The Associated Press stated that it could not independently verify the authenticity of the published tally sheets.<ref name=APReview>{{cite news |url=https://apnews.com/article/venezuela-maduro-machado-biden-gonzalez-a625eb01979bc9cf5570d03242f198b1 |publisher=Associated Press |title=AP review of Venezuela opposition-provided vote tallies casts doubt on government's election results |date=2 August 2024 |access-date=3 August 2024|first1=Regina |last1=Garcia Cano |first2=Joshua |last2=Goodman |first3=Angeliki |last3=Kastanis}}</ref> On 3 August 2024, the Colombian civil society network [[Electoral Observation Mission (Colombia)|Electoral Observation Mission]] (MOE) published its analysis of the PUD results, finding them fully self-consistent. MOE called for the CNE to publish the polling station tally sheets and audit the full chain of transmission of information.<ref name="MOE_tally_sheets_VE2024">{{cite Q|Q128803681|url-status=live}}</ref> MOE stated that González necessarily won the election based on the publicly available tally sheets analysed by MOE (73.1% of the total), since the missing sheets were too few to give a majority to Maduro, even if 100% of the votes on the missing tally sheets were for Maduro.<ref name="CNN_after_VE_vote" />

A study from political scientist Dorothy Kronick, described by ''The New York Times'' as "an expert on Venezuelan electoral data at the University of California, Berkeley",<ref name=LostDecisively>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2024/07/31/world/americas/venezuela-maduro-election-results.html|title=Election Results Presented by Venezuela's Opposition Suggest Maduro Lost Decisively|author1=Kurmanaev, Anatoly|author2=Singer, Ethan|work=The New York Times|date= 31 July 2024|access-date=23 August 2024|id= {{ProQuest|3086389379}} }}</ref> stated that the opposition data "almost certainly reflects actual votes cast".<ref name=GuardianPressureGrows/><ref name=KronickValidity>{{cite web|url= https://dorothykronick.com/28J.pdf|title=On the validityy of vote counts published by the Venezuelan opposition|author=Kronick, Dorothy|date=22 August 2024|access-date=23 August 2024|publisher=DorothKronick.com}}</ref>

==== Mebane statistical analysis of opposition vote data ====
 [[File:Elecciones presidenciales de Venezuela de 2024 - Resultado por parroquias (Comando con Venezuela).svg|thumb|upright=1.0|Results by parish announced by the PUD]]
A working paper published by [[Walter Mebane]], that used statistical tools for electoral forensics, found no evidence of incremental or extreme fraud in the opposition-published results. He found no evidence of incremental or extreme fraud in the election minutes as published by the opposition. Using these minutes, he calculated that the probability of no fraud having occurred in the opposition tallies (π<sub>1</sub>) at 99.97%. He also calculated that the probability of incremental fraud having occurred (π<sub>2</sub>) at 0.0185% and that extreme fraud having occurred (π<sub>3</sub>) at 0.0114%.<ref name="Mebane">{{cite web |last1=Mebane |first1=Walter |title=eforensics Analysis of the Venezuela 2024 Presidential Elections |url=https://websites.umich.edu/~wmebane/Venezuela2024.pdf |website=umich.edu |access-date=6 August 2024}}</ref><ref name= GuardianEvidenceShows>{{cite news |url= https://www.theguardian.com/world/article/2024/aug/06/venezuela-election-maduro-analysis |work= The Guardian |title= Evidence shows Venezuela's election was stolen – but will Maduro budge?|first= Tiago |last= Rogero |date= 6 August 2024 |access-date= 6 August 2024|archive-url=https://archive.today/20240806220241/https://www.theguardian.com/world/article/2024/aug/06/venezuela-election-maduro-analysis|archive-date=6 August 2024|url-status=live}}</ref>

Mebane identified only two polling stations where fraud may have occurred; however, using a 99.5% credibility interval, it is not possible to state that this occurred in these two polls. Mebane's paper compared the results of other elections in Venezuela between 2000 and 2013. The tallies provided by the opposition in the 2024 elections have the highest probability of no fraud.<ref name= Mebane/>

== Reactions ==
On 30 July, the [[Carter Center]] issued a harsh rebuke of the election authorities,<ref name=CarterCenterBlasts>{{Cite web|url=https://apnews.com/article/venezuela-presidential-election-maduro-machado-edmundo-results-3ec88b273cabfee8e5696ff67d24186d|title=Carter Center unable to verify Venezuela election results, blasts officials for lack of transparency|date=30 July 2024|website=Associated Press}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.infobae.com/venezuela/2024/07/31/el-centro-carter-aseguro-que-las-elecciones-presidenciales-en-venezuela-no-cumplieron-las-normas-democraticas/|title=El Centro Carter consideró que las elecciones presidenciales en Venezuela 'no pueden considerarse democráticas'|language=es |trans-title= Carter Center considers Venezuelan presidential elections 'cannot be considered democratic'|date=31 July 2024|website=infobae}}</ref> stating there was a "complete lack of transparency" and that the election "cannot be considered democratic".<ref name= CarterCenterPressRelease>{{cite press release |url= https://www.cartercenter.org/news/pr/2024/venezuela-073024.html |publisher= Carter Center |date= 30 July 2024 |access-date= 31 July 2024 |title= Carter Center Statement on Venezuela Election}}</ref>

=== Fraud allegations ===
{{See also|#Sequences of zeros in the CNE values}}

[[Anne Applebaum]] wrote in ''[[The Atlantic]]'' that it "was absolutely clear by [31 July] that ... the election had been stolen".<ref name= AtlanticDictatorLies/> Independent observers have described the election results as arbitrary, even by Venezuelan standards, according to ''The Guardian''.<ref name= KnifeEdge>{{cite news |last1=Torres |first1=Patricia |last2=Phillips |first2=Tom |last3=Rogero |first3=Tiago |last4=Jones |first4=Sam |title=Venezuela on a knife-edge as opposition accuses Maduro of rigging election |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/article/2024/jul/29/venezuela-election-result-maduro-urrutia |work=The Guardian |date=29 July 2024 |access-date= 29 July 2024}}</ref>

[[Political scientist]] [[Steven Levitsky]] called the vote "one of the most egregious electoral frauds in modern Latin American history."<ref name="Turkewitz-2024a" />

Political scientist Dalson Figueiredo of the [[Federal University of Pernambuco]], one of the authors of the [[#Parallel vote tabulation|AltaVista parallel vote tabulation project]], stated: "After analyzing our own data, seeing the opposition's results and how they both match up, my conclusion is that we're witnessing the largest electoral fraud in the history of Latin America."<ref name=WAPOMaduroLost/>

On his [[blog]], [[mathematician]] [[Terence Tao]] pointed out that the election results had "oddly round percentages", suggesting that the election was fixed.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Ansede |first=Manuel |date=2024-10-12 |title=Terence Tao, mathematician: 'It's not good for something as important as AI to be a monopoly held by one or two companies' |url=https://english.elpais.com/science-tech/2024-10-12/terence-tao-mathematician-its-not-good-for-something-as-important-as-ai-to-be-a-monopoly-held-by-one-or-two-companies.html?outputType=amp |access-date=2024-10-13 |website=EL PAÍS English |language=en-us}}</ref>

===Domestic===
[[File:Machado y González protestando contra el fraude presidencial en Venezuela de 2024.jpg|thumb|upright=1.1|left|Machado (left) and González (middle) along with his wife (right), addressing the nation in front of the United Nations Development Programme office in Caracas, 2024]]

Supporting the PUD/González win announcement, [[María Corina Machado]] and [[Edmundo González Urrutia|Edmundo González]] rejected the results from the CNE and claimed victory.<ref name=APLive/> On 31 July, Maduro alleged that the US was fomenting civil war in Venezuela.<ref name=USMaduroLost/> González, at an event accompanied by Machado, said "The Venezuelans and the entire world know what happened ... Our struggle continues and we will not rest until the will of the Venezuelan people is respected".<ref name=APLive>{{cite news |last1=Garcia Cano |first1=Regina |title=Venezuela election live updates: Opposition claims victory after Maduro was declared the winner |url=https://apnews.com/live/venezuela-election-updates-maduro-machado-gonzalez |website=Associated Press |publisher=Associated Press |date=29 July 2024 |access-date=29 July 2024 |archive-date=28 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240728231556/https://apnews.com/live/venezuela-election-updates-maduro-machado-gonzalez |url-status=live }}</ref>

The [[Communist Party of Venezuela]] objected to the CNE announcement and called for the complete election results to be published.<ref name="TribunaPopular_about_election">{{cite web |url= https://prensapcv.wordpress.com/2024/07/29/comunicado-sobre-las-elecciones-presidenciales/ |work= Tribuna Popular Wordpress |title= Comunicado: Sobre las elecciones presidenciales |language= es |trans-title= Communication: About the presidential elections |date= 29 July 2024 |access-date= 30 July 2024 |archive-url= https://archive.today/20240730161552/https://prensapcv.wordpress.com/2024/07/29/comunicado-sobre-las-elecciones-presidenciales |archive-date= 30 July 2024 |url-status=live |id= Wikidata [[:d:Q128133222]] }}</ref>

Supporting the CNE's announcement of his victory, Maduro described the result as "a triumph of peace and stability".<ref>{{cite news |last1=Buschschlüter |first1=Vanessa |title=Venezuela's Maduro declared winner in disputed vote |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/cz5rj2mzgevo |publisher=[[BBC News]] |date=29 July 2024 |access-date=29 July 2024 |archive-date=29 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240729045535/https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/cz5rj2mzgevo |url-status=live }}</ref> Candidates [[Benjamín Rausseo]], Daniel Ceballos, Luis Eduardo Martínez and [[José Brito (politician)|José Brito]] recognized the official results;<ref>{{cite web|url=https://laverdad.com/rausseo-ceballos-martinez-y-brito-reconocen-resultados-emanados-por-el-cne/|title=Rausseo, Ceballos, Martínez y Brito reconocen resultados emanados por el CNE|date= 29 July 2024 |access-date= 30 July 2024|work=La Verdad|language=es}}</ref> the latter three were nominated by [[Interventions of political parties in Venezuela|intervened parties]].<ref name="da Costa-2024"/> Although still maintaining that he won, Maduro acknowledged the unrest in Venezuela. He blamed the turmoil on "international Zionism", referencing an [[Antisemitic trope#World domination|antisemitic trope]] that Jews control the world.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Cramer |first1=Philissa |title=Venezuela's Maduro blames 'international Zionism' for unrest after disputed vote |url=https://www.timesofisrael.com/venezuelas-maduro-blames-international-zionism-for-unrest-after-disputed-vote/ |work= The Times of Israel |date=8 August 2024}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Starr |first1=Michael |title=Maduro: 'International Zionism' behind civil unrest in Venezuela |url=https://www.jpost.com/western_wall/article-813522 |work=The Jerusalem Post |date=6 August 2024 |language=en}}</ref>

A [[Polls in Venezuela#Credibility of polling firms|Meganálisis poll]] of 1,007 people in Venezuela from 8 to 11 August found that 93% of respondents believe Maduro lost the election, with the majority of Venezuelans expressing anger, anxiety, indignation, and feelings of helplessness after the election. Venezuelans who responded that they were happy were 2.8%, and the poll found that 40% hoped to leave the country before the end of 2024.<ref name=HundredThousand>{{cite news |first1= Antonio Maria |last1=Delgado |first2= Syra |last2= Ortiz Blanes |title= A hundred thousand Venezuelans are considering leaving the country right now, poll says |work= Miami Herald |publisher= Yahoo News|date= 14 August 2024 |url= https://ca.news.yahoo.com/hundred-thousand-venezuelans-considering-leaving-093000006.html |access-date= 15 August 2024}}</ref>

===International===
<!--

THERE IS A SUB-ARTICLE, please review [[WP:SS]] add new content there

-->{{main|International reactions to the 2024 Venezuelan presidential election}}The election results released by the government-controlled National Electoral Council (CNE) were followed by a mixture of scepticism and criticism from the leaders of most Latin American countries. Some Latin American countries—including Cuba, Honduras, and Nicaragua—recognized and congratulated Maduro as the election winner.<ref name="reuters29jul" /><ref name=HardtoBelieve>{{cite news |first= Sam |last= Jones|url= https://www.theguardian.com/world/article/2024/jul/29/venezuela-election-result-suspicion-abroad-nicolas-maduro|title='Hard to believe': Venezuela election result met with suspicion abroad |work=The Guardian |date= 29 July 2024 |access-date= 29 July 2024}}</ref> Some world leaders expressed skepticism of the claimed results and did not recognize the CNE claims;<ref name = HardtoBelieve/><ref name=WorldLeadersCast>{{cite news |first1=Samantha |last1= Schmidt |first2=Leo |last2 = Sands |first3= Vanessa |last3= Herrero|title= World leaders cast doubt on Maduro's claim of victory in Venezuelan election |url= https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2024/07/29/venezuela-presidential-election-result-maduro/ | newspaper=[[The Washington Post]] |date= 29 July 2024 |access-date= 29 July 2024}}</ref><ref name=reuters29jul /> others including Russia, China, Iran and North Korea recognized [[Nicolás Maduro]] as the winner.<ref name=WorldLeadersCast/><ref name=TimesFlees>{{cite news|url=https://www.thetimes.com/world/latin-america/article/venezuela-opposition-leader-edmundo-gonzalez-spain-jnrgk0tnr|title=Venezuelan opposition leader Edmundo González flees to Spain|work=[[The Sunday Times]]|author=Gibbs, Stephen|date=8 September 2024|access-date=8 September 2024}}</ref>

[[File:Edmundo González recognition map.svg|thumb|upright=1.4|Map showing the countries that, together with Canada, Italy and Paraguay, have declared [[Edmundo González]] the winner of the presidential election]]

President [[Gabriel Boric]] of Chile was the first foreign leader to question the CNE result, stating that the "results are difficult to believe".<ref name=Arroyo-2024a>{{Cite web |author1=Lorena Arroyo |author2=Federico Rivas Molina |date=29 July 2024 |title=Venezuela declares Maduro winner of election, but US and others question the result |url=https://english.elpais.com/international/2024-07-29/venezuela-declares-maduro-winner-of-election-but-us-and-others-question-the-result.html |access-date=30 July 2024 |work= El País |language=en-us}}</ref> President [[Daniel Noboa]] of Ecuador warned that "that is the danger of dictatorship, and today we are witnessing how one more of them tries to take hope away from millions of Venezuelans."<ref name=reuters29jul/> Condemnation from Costa Rica, El Salvador, Peru and Uruguay described the CNE result in terms of fraud or corruption.<ref name=reuters29jul/><ref name=HardtoBelieve/><ref name=Arroyo-2024a/> Harsh criticism came from President [[Javier Milei]] of Argentina, who called Maduro a dictator.<ref name=reuters29jul /><ref name=ap29jul>{{cite web |title=Venezuela election live updates: Opposition claims victory after Maduro was declared the winner |url=https://apnews.com/live/venezuela-election-updates-maduro-machado-gonzalez |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240728145354/https://apnews.com/live/venezuela-election-updates-maduro-machado-gonzalez |archive-date=28 July 2024 |access-date=28 July 2024 |website=Associated Press}}</ref>

The three leftist presidents of Brazil, Colombia and Mexico<ref name=AtlanticDictatorLies/><ref name= GuardianEditorial>{{cite news |date= 30 July 2024 |access-date= 30 July 2024 |url= https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/article/2024/jul/30/the-guardian-view-on-venezuelas-elections-making-the-peoples-votes-count |title= The Guardian view on Venezuela's elections: making the people's votes count}}</ref><ref name=FPMomentofTruth>{{cite news |url= https://foreignpolicy.com/2024/08/01/venezuela-election-maduro-gonzalez-opposition-vote-results-protests-diplomacy/ |work= Foreign Policy |date= 1 August 2024 |access-date= 2 August 2024 |first= Catherine |last= Osborn |title= Venezuela's Post-Election Moment of Truth}}</ref> were quick in demanding that all votes be counted, along with full transparency of all ballot records from each precinct.<ref name= NegotiateStatement>{{cite news |url= https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2024-07-29/brazil-mexico-colombia-negotiate-joint-statement-on-venezuela-election |work= Bloomberg |date= 29 July 2024 |access-date= 30 July 2024 |title= Brazil, Mexico, Colombia Negotiating Joint Statement on Venezuela Election Transparency |first= Simone |last= Iglesias}}</ref><ref name=Barrons.com/><ref name=reuters29jul/>  The Colombian government called for the "total vote count, its verification and independent audit to be carried out as soon as possible".<ref name="reuters29jul" /> President [[Luís Inácio Lula da Silva]] of Brazil called the controversy a "normal" process, but asked for the release of the total vote tally.<ref name="lula-30-7">{{cite web |title=Lula sobre Venezuela: 'Apresenta a ata', diz presidente sobre impasse na eleição |url=https://www.bbc.com/portuguese/articles/cw0yzz629e8o |website=BBC News Brasil |access-date=30 July 2024 |language=pt-br |date=30 July 2024 |quote=É normal que tenha uma briga. Como resolve essa briga? Apresenta a ata}}</ref> President [[Andrés Manuel López Obrador]] of Mexico said on 30 July that the vote tallies should be publicized, but he saw no evidence of fraud.<ref>{{cite news |url= https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuelas-maduro-asks-phone-call-with-lula-says-source-2024-08-01/ |work= Reuters |date= 1 August 2024 |access-date= 1 August 2024 |title= Venezuela's Maduro asks for phone call with Lula, says source}}</ref> On 1 August, the three presidents released a joint statement of concern over post-election violence, and asking for "impartial verification of results"<ref name= FPMomentofTruth/> quickly, at the disaggregated level.<ref name= BMCCall>{{cite news |url= https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/brazilian-flag-raised-argentine-embassy-caracas-2024-08-01/ |work= Reuters |title= Brazil, Mexico and Colombia call for Venezuela to release full vote tallies |first1= Lisandra |last1= Paraguassu |first2= Leonardo |last2= Fernandez |first3= Deisy |last3= Buitrago |date= 1 August 2024 |access-date= 2 August 2024}}</ref> Officials from the three nations—whose governments are allied with Maduro according to the Associated Press (AP)—worked to seek "a solution to the country's political crisis".<ref name=APNews6Aug>{{cite web | last1=Castillo | first1=E. Eduardo | last2=Barcia Cano | first2=Regina | title=Brazil, Colombia and Mexico in talks with Venezuelan government and opposition on election crisis | website=AP News | date=6 August 2024 | url=https://apnews.com/article/venezuela-presidential-election-maduro-gonzalez-machado-39c4b72fe14c34ee63a5b7adc21a9bf9 | access-date=7 August 2024}}</ref> The AP wrote that the opposition has reason to be wary of recommendations from this group to "follow Venezuelan laws and appear before the appropriate institutions", since the "ruling party controls every aspect of government, including the justice system, and uses it to defeat and repress real and perceived opponents".<ref name= APNews6Aug/>

United States [[Secretary of State (United States)|Secretary of State]] [[Antony Blinken]] initially expressed doubts about the veracity of the results from the [[Consejo Nacional Electoral (Venezuela)|CNE]],<ref name=reuters29jul>{{cite web |title=Leaders across Americas react to Venezuela election results |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/latin-american-leaders-react-venezuela-election-results-2024-07-29/ |website=Reuters |access-date=29 July 2024}}</ref><ref name= ReutersUSAccuses>{{cite news |url= https://www.reuters.com/world/us-accuses-venezuela-electoral-manipulation-repression-2024-07-29/ |work= Reuters |date= 30 July 2024 |access-date= 30 July 2024 |title= US accuses Venezuela of election manipulation, leaves door open to sanctions |first1= Matt |last1= Spetalnick |first2= Phil |last2= Stewart}}</ref> and on 1 August, said there was "overwhelming evidence" that González won.<ref name=BBCOverwhelming>{{cite news |publisher= BBC |url= https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/cd1d10453zno |date= 1 August 2024 |access-date= 2 August 2024|title= Overwhelming evidence Venezuela opposition won election - Blinken |first1= Ione |last1= Wells |first2= Thomas |last2= Mackintosh}}</ref> He called for talks and a peaceful transition,<ref name=USMaduroLost/> but did not refer to González as ''president-elect''.<ref name= USSupports>{{cite news |url= https://www.miamiherald.com/news/nation-world/world/americas/venezuela/article290789549.html|title= U.S. supports negotiations with Maduro but won't call opposition winner president-elect |work= Miami Herald |date= 7 August 2024 |access-date= 7 August 2024 |first= Nora |last= Gamez Torres}}</ref>{{efn|The ''Washington Post'',<ref name=USMaduroLost>{{cite news |url= https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2024/08/01/venezuela-election-maduro-us/ |newspaper= The Washington Post |title= U.S. says Maduro lost Venezuelan election, calls for talks, transition |date= 1 August 2024 |access-date= 2 August 2024 |first1= Samantha |last1= Schmidt |first2= Matthew |last2= Brown|quote= Blinken did not say the United States was recognizing González as Venezuela's president.}}</ref>''The Wall Street Journal'',<ref>{{cite news |url= https://www.wsj.com/politics/elections/u-s-says-maduros-opponent-won-presidential-election-e3dbe0e5 |work= The Wall Street Journal |date= 2 August 2024 |access-date= 2 August 2024 |title= U.S. Says Maduro's opponent as winner in Venezuela election |first1= Kanishka |last1= Singh |first2= Matt |last2=Spetalnick |quote= The announcement from Washington did not go beyond congratulating him for a 'successful campaign,' the closest the U.S. has come since Sunday's contested election to recognizing Gonzalez as the OPEC nation's new leader.}}</ref> say that Blinken did not recognize González as president-elect; ''The Guardian'' says that he did.<ref>{{cite news |url= https://www.theguardian.com/world/article/2024/aug/02/venezuela-election-us-edmundo-gonzalez-maduro-results-disputed |work= night, the US secretary of state, Antony Blinken, rejected the incumbent's claims and recognised González as Venezuela's president-elect.}}</ref>}}

On 29 July, Canada's deputy prime minister [[Chrystia Freeland]] expressed that Canada had "serious concerns" about the proclaimed election results. Freeland emphasized Canada's long-standing support for Venezuela's democratic opposition and condemned the increasingly authoritarian nature of the regime.<ref name="cbc 29jul">{{Cite news |last=McKenna |first=Kate |date=29 July 2024 |title=Canada has 'serious concerns' about Venezuelan election results, Freeland says |url=https://www.cbc.ca/news/politics/canada-reax-venezuela-election-1.7278828 |access-date=29 July 2024 |work=[[CBC News]]}}</ref> In January 2025, Canada formally recognized González as president-elect. The minister of Foreign Affairs [[Mélanie Joly]] declared: "Maduro's shameless actions demonstrate that democracy and the rule of law cannot be taken for granted. We will not tolerate the erosion of the democratic process or the repression of citizens seeking to express their rights."<ref>{{Cite news |last=Phillips |first=Tom |date=10 January 2025 |title=Venezuela's Maduro sworn in amid outrage over alleged fraudulent election |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2025/jan/10/nicolas-maduro-inauguration-alleged-election-theft |work=[[The Guardian]]}}</ref>

The day after the election, nine Latin American countries (Argentina, Costa Rica, the Dominican Republic, Ecuador, Guatemala, Panama, Paraguay, Peru, and Uruguay<ref name="NineOAS">{{cite news |date=29 July 2024 |title=Nine Latin American governments call for emergency OAS meeting |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/nine-latin-american-governments-call-emergency-oas-meeting-2024-07-29/ |access-date=29 July 2024 |publisher=Reuters}}</ref><ref name="Arroyo-2024b">{{Cite web |author1=Lorena Arroyo |author2=Federico Rivas Molina |date=29 July 2024 |title=Estados Unidos, Brasil, la UE, España, Chile, Colombia y Argentina piden que se verifiquen los resultados en Venezuela |trans-title=United States, Brazil, the European Union, Spain, Chile, Colombia and Argentina ask that the results in Venezuela be verified |url=https://elpais.com/america/2024-07-29/gabriel-boric-los-resultados-de-venezuela-son-dificiles-de-creer-no-reconoceremos-ningun-resultado-que-no-sea-verificable.html |access-date=29 July 2024 |website=El País América |language=es}}</ref>) called for an emergency meeting of the [[Organization of American States]] (OAS), for 31 July.<ref name="ReutersResultsUnreliable">{{cite news |date=30 July 2024 |title=Venezuela vote results unreliable, says OAS body |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/oas-department-says-results-announced-by-venezuela-cannot-be-recognized-2024-07-30/ |access-date=30 July 2024 |work=Reuters}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |date=1 August 2009 |title=OAS - Organization of American States: Democracy for peace, security, and development |url=https://www.oas.org/en/media_center/press_release.asp?sCodigo=AVI-111/24 |access-date=30 July 2024 |website=OAS - Organization of American States |language=en}}</ref> The member states did not reach consensus on a resolution.<ref>{{cite news |work= [[NTN24]] |date= 31 July 2024 |access-date= 31 July 2024 |url= https://www.ntn24.com/noticias-politica/este-es-el-parrafo-de-la-discordia-que-impidio-un-consenso-sobre-resolucion-de-la-oea-acerca-de-venezuela-505529 |title= Este es el párrafo de la discordia que impidió un consenso sobre resolución de la OEA acerca de Venezuela |language=es |trans-title= This is the paragraph of discord that prevented a consensus on the OAS resolution on Venezuela}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |work= [[NTN24]] |date= 31 July 2024 |access-date= 31 July 2024 |url= https://www.ntn24.com/noticias-politica/la-oea-no-aprobo-la-resolucion-sobre-la-situacion-en-venezuela-asi-votaron-los-paises-de-la-region-505513 |language= es |title= La OEA no aprobó la resolución sobre la situación en Venezuela: así votaron los países de la región |trans-title= The OAS did not approve the resolution on the situation in Venezuela: this is how the countries of the region voted}}</ref> OAS Secretary General [[Luis Almagro]]—referencing the ongoing investigation in the [[International Criminal Court]] (ICC) of Venezuela for crimes against humanity—said he would petition the ICC for the arrest of Maduro. Prior to the election, Maduro had stated that if he did not win, there would be a "bloodbath, a civil war"; Almagro said Maduro was fulfilling that promise and it was time for justice.<ref name= AlmagroSolicitara>{{cite news |url= https://www.infobae.com/america/america-latina/2024/08/01/luis-almagro-solicitara-a-la-corte-penal-internacional-que-ordene-el-arresto-de-nicolas-maduro-por-haber-cometido-un-bano-de-sangre/ |work= InfoBae |date= 31 July 2024 |access-date= 1 August 2024 |language=es |title= Luis Almagro solicitará a la Corte Penal Internacional que ordene el arresto de Nicolás Maduro por haber cometido un baño de sangre |trans-title= Luis Almagro will ask the International Criminal Court to order the arrest of Nicolás Maduro for having committed a bloodbath}}</ref>

The BBC and ''The Guardian'' reported that Peru was the first country to recognize González as Venezuela's president-elect, on 30 July<ref name= PeruSeConvierte>{{cite news |url= https://www.bbc.com/mundo/articles/c6p24vjwj3vo |publisher= BBC News Mundo |date= 30 July 2024 |title= Perú se convierte en el primer país en considerar a Edmundo González como 'presidente electo' de Venezuela |language=es |trans-title= Peru becomes the first country to consider Edmundo González as 'president-elect' of Venezuela|access-date= 3 August 2024}}</ref><ref name="Phillips-2024">{{cite news |last1=Phillips |first1=Tom |last2=Gambino |first2=Lauren |date=31 July 2024 |title=Venezuela's Nicolás Maduro blames unrest on far-right conspiracy as isolation grows |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/article/2024/aug/01/venezuela-election-results-nicolas-maduro-protests-gonzalez-machado |access-date=1 August 2024 |work=The Guardian}}</ref>—a statement from the former Peruvian foreign minister that was clarified on 5 September by Peru's Council of Ministers after a new foreign minister was named.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://eldiario.com/2024/09/05/consejo-de-ministros-peru-no-ha-reconocido-a-edmundo-gonzalez-como-presidente-venezuela/|work=[[El Diario de Caracas]]|date=5 September 2024|access-date=8 September 2024|language=es|title= Consejo de Ministros de Perú aclaró que su gobierno no ha reconocido a Edmundo González como presidente electo de Venezuela|trans-title=Peru's Council of Ministers clarified that its government has not recognized Edmundo González as the elected president of Venezuela}}</ref> Peru had recalled its ambassador from Venezuela on 29 July,<ref name="reuters29jul" /><ref name="ap29jul" /> and expelled the Venezuelan diplomats from Peru the next day.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.infobae.com/america/agencias/2024/07/30/peru-expulsa-a-los-diplomaticos-venezolanos-y-les-da-72-horas-para-abandonar-el-pais/|title=Perú expulsa a los diplomáticos venezolanos y les da 72 horas para abandonar el país|date=29 July 2024|accessdate=29 July 2024|work=Infobae|language=es|trans-title = Peru expels Venezuelan diplomats and gives them 72 hours to leave the country}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url= https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/peru-orders-venezuelan-diplomats-leave-country-within-72-hours-2024-07-30/ |work= Reuters |date= 29 July 2024 |access-date= 29 July 2024 |title= Peru orders Venezuelan diplomats out after contested vote}}</ref> In response, Venezuela severed diplomatic relations with Peru.<ref name= PeruSeConvierte/><ref name= BrazilRunning/> Peruvian President [[Dina Boluarte]] reinforced on 6 September that Peru's position with respect to Venezuela had not changed under the new foreign minister, saying "We will not be part of an electoral fraud; we will not support a dictatorial government."<ref name=PeruRatifies>{{cite news|url=https://eldiario.com/2024/09/06/peru-ratifica-postura-sobre-venezuela-no-apoya-gobierno-dictatorial/|work=[[El Diario de Caracas]]|date=6 September 2024|access-date=8 September 2024|language=es|title= Perú ratifica su postura sobre Venezuela: 'No vamos a apoyar ningún gobierno dictatorial'|trans-title=Peru reaffirms its position on Venezuela: 'We will not support any dictatorial government'}}</ref>

Panama suspended diplomatic relations with Venezuela.<ref name="PanamaSuspends">{{cite news |date=29 July 2024 |title=Panama suspends diplomatic relations with Venezuela pending election review |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/panama-suspends-diplomatic-relations-with-venezuela-pending-election-review-2024-07-29/ |access-date=29 July 2024 |publisher=Reuters}}</ref> Venezuela also expelled diplomats from Argentina, Chile, Costa Rica, the Dominican Republic, Panama and Uruguay; as of 1 August, Brazil took over running the Caracas embassies of Argentina and Peru.<ref name= BrazilRunning>{{cite news |url= https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/brazilian-flag-raised-argentine-embassy-caracas-2024-08-01/ |work= Reuters |date=1 August 2024 |access-date=1 August 2024 |title=Brazil running Argentina, Peru embassies in Caracas after election-related expulsions |first1=Leonardo |last1=Fernandez |first2=Lisandra |last2=Paraguassu}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.larepublica.co/globoeconomia/el-gobierno-de-maduro-rompe-relaciones-con-argentina-panama-y-otros-cinco-paises-3918273 |language=es |work=[[La República (Colombia)|La República]] |location=Bogotá |date= 29 July 2024 |access-date=30 July 2024 |title= Perú ordena el retiro de personal venezolano luego de que Maduro cortara relaciones |trans-title= Peru orders withdrawal of Venezuelan personnel after Maduro cuts ties |first=Karen |last=Pinto Duitama}}</ref>

In November 2024, the prime minister of Italy [[Giorgia Meloni]] recognized Edmundo González as the president-elect of Venezuela.<ref>{{cite news |title=Giorgia Meloni reconoció a Edmundo González Urrutia como presidente electo de Venezuela |url=https://www.infobae.com/venezuela/2024/11/20/giorgia-meloni-reconocio-a-edmundo-gonzalez-urrutia-como-presidente-electo-de-venezuela/ |access-date=10 January 2025 |work=[[Infobae]] |date=20 November 2024 |language=es}}</ref>

== Aftermath ==
{{Main|2024 Venezuelan political crisis}}
Following the announcements of election results, a national and international [[2024 Venezuelan political crisis|political crisis]] developed.<ref name= FacesSetback>{{cite news |url= https://apnews.com/article/brazil-lula-venezuela-election-maduro-1c3afbf01f4c85e7903c2fc3d7fdbf38 |publisher= Associated Press |title= Venezuela's opposition faces setback after countries suggest repeat of presidential election |first1= Gabriela |last1= Sa Pessoa |first2= Regina |last2= Garcia Cano |date= 15 August 2024 |access-date= 16 August 2024}}</ref><ref name="Kurmanaev-NYT-6-8-2024"/><ref name=DragsOn>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuelan-opposition-protests-election-dispute-drags-2024-08-17/|title=Venezuelan opposition protests as election dispute drags on|work=Reuters|first1=Deisy|last1=Buitrago|first2=Mariela|last2=Nava|date=18 August 2024|access-date=20 August 2024}}</ref>

As of 2 September, NGO [[Foro Penal]] reported that Venezuela had 1,793 political prisoners—the highest it has had in the 21st&nbsp;century—of which 1,659, including children, were detained after the election; most have not been sentenced, but are charged with terrorism.<ref name=LastHill>{{cite news|url=https://www.infobae.com/venezuela/2024/09/10/el-dictador-enfrenta-su-ultima-colina/|work=[[Infobae]]|language=es|date=10 September 2024|access-date=10 September 2024|author=Pérez Izquierdo, Laureano|title=El dictador enfrenta su última colina|trans-title=The dictator faces his last hill}}</ref><ref name=ElDiario1793>{{cite news|url=https://eldiario.com/2024/09/07/foro-penal-reporto-1793-presos-politicos-venezuela/|work=[[El Diario de Caracas]]|language=es|date=7 September 2024|access-date=10 September 2024|author=Díaz, Jackelin|title=Foro Penal reportó 1.793 presos políticos en Venezuela|trans-title=Penal Forum reported 1,793 political prisoners in Venezuela}}</ref>

Venezuelan citizens who considered the results to be fraudulent [[2024 Venezuelan protests|took to the streets in ongoing protests]].<ref>{{cite news |last1=Goodman |first1=Joshua |last2=Garcia Cano |first2=Regina |date=29 July 2024 |title=Venezuelans take to streets of Caracas to protest Maduro's claim that he won presidential election 2024 |access-date=29 July 2024 |website=Associated Press}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |date=29 July 2024 |title= See how Venezuelans are using pots to protest Maduro's victory |url=https://edition.cnn.com/2024/07/29/world/video/venezuelans-protest-maduro-victory-cacerolazo-pozzebon-digivid |publisher= CNN |access-date= 29 July 2024}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=See angry July 2024 |access-date= 29 July 2024}}</ref> As of 15 August, 25 people had been killed during protests nationwide.<ref name= HundredThousand/> [[Amnesty International]] and other human rights organizations "condemned the repressive actions of the Nicolás Maduro regime in Venezuela and demanded that it guarantee the right to protest and full respect for the rights to life, personal integrity and freedom".<ref name=InfoBaeDR>{{cite news |url= |access-date= 1 August 2024 |first= Gastón |last= Calvo |language= es |title= Organizaciones de Derechos Humanos condenaron en conjunto las acciones represivas del régimen de Nicolás Maduro |trans-title= Human Rights Organizations jointly condemned the repressive actions of the Nicolás Maduro regime}}</ref><ref name= AICondemnViolence>{{cite press release |url=
