2024 |access-date= 1 August 2024 |title= Venezuela: International organizations condemn the high levels of violence and repression and demand that the authorities guarantee the right to protest and full respect for the rights to life, personal integrity and freedom}}</ref>

===Crackdown===
{{Further|Operation Tun Tun}}

Maduro accuses the opposition of promoting a coup.<ref name= BBCRepressionWorsens/> In a crackdown by security forces following the elections,<ref name="ReportProtesters" /><ref name= BloombergCrackdown/><ref name="MaduroBoasts">{{cite news |last1=Schmidt |first1=Samantha |title=Maduro boasts 2,200 arrests since election; rights groups say 23 dead |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2024/08/08/venezuela-election-maduro-arrests-opposition-crackdown |access-date=9 August 2024 |newspaper=Washington Post |date=8 August 2024}}</ref> he mentioned using [[Operation Tun Tun]]; [[BBC News]] stated that "rights groups say it consists of the authorities going door-to-door to detain those with links to the protests or the opposition".<ref name=BBCRepressionWorsens>{{cite news |url= https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/clynl7plg8yo |title= Venezuela security forces swoop on activists as repression worsens |publisher= BBC News |first= Ione |last= Wells |date= 8 August 2024 |access-date= 9 August 2024}}</ref> Maduro ordered two prisons to be rehabilitated to contain the large number of detainees.<ref name= IntensifiesPersecution>{{cite news |url= https://english.elpais.com/international/2024-08-09/thousands-of-arrests-and-terrorism-charges-nicolas-maduro-intensifies-persecution-of-opponents-in-venezeula.html |work= El País |date= 9 August 2024 |access-date= 9 August 2024 |title= Thousands of arrests and terrorism charges: Nicolás Maduro intensifies persecution of opponents in Venezuela}}</ref>

After [[Diosdado Cabello]] and [[Jorge Rodríguez (Venezuelan politician)|Jorge Rodríguez]] suggested that Machado and González go to prison,<ref name=ElPaisIrPresos>{{cite news |url= https://elpais.com/america/2024-07-30/resultados-de-las-elecciones-en-venezuela-2024-en-vivo.html |work= El País |date= 30 July 2024 |access-date= 31 July 2024 |title= Resultados de las elecciones en Venezuela 2024, en vivo / Jorge Rodríguez, presidente de la Asamblea: 'María Corina Machado y Edmundo González deben ir presos' |language= es |trans-title= Venezuela 2024 election results, live / Jorge Rodríguez, president of the Assembly: 'María Corina Machado and Edmundo González must go to jail' }}</ref><ref name=WaPo16Dead>{{cite news |url= https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2024/07/30/venezuela-election-protests-maduro-gonalez/ |newspaper= The Washington Post |date= 30 July 2024 |access-date= 31 July 2024 |title= At least 16 reported dead as Maduro meets Venezuelan protests with force |first1= Samantha |last1= Schmidt |first2= Ana Vanessa |last2= Herrero}}</ref> Maduro asked authorities to apply "maximum justice" and accused them of being leaders of violent groups.<ref>{{cite news |url= https://www.ntn24.com/noticias-politica/maduro-culpa-a-maria-corina-y-a-edmundo-de-violencia-criminal-y-pide-justicia-505238 |work= NTN24 |date= 30 July 2024 |access-date= 31 July 2024 |title= Maduro culpa a María Corina y a Edmundo de 'violencia criminal' y pide 'justicia' |language=es |trans-title= Maduro blames María Corina and Edmundo for 'criminal violence' and calls for 'justice'}}</ref> On 1 August, Machado published a letter in ''The Wall Street Journal'', stating that she had gone in to hiding "fearing for my life, my freedom".<ref name=GotTrounced>{{cite news |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/i-can-prove-maduro-got-trounced-venezuela-election-stolen-772d66a0 |work= The Wall Street Journal |date= 1 August 2024 |access-date= 1 August 2024 |title= I Can Prove Maduro Got Trounced |first= Maria Corina |last= Machado}}</ref> In a 19 August interview, [[Tarek William Saab|Tarek Saab]], suggested that opposition leaders could be charged as intellectual authors of the deaths that occurred in post-electoral violence.<ref name=MHCouldCharge>{{cite news|url=https://www.miamiherald.com/news/nation-world/world/americas/venezuela/article291191975.html|work=MiamiHerald|title=Venezuela could charge opposition leader Machado with murder, regime's prosecutor says|first=Antonio Maria |last=Delgado |date=19 August 2024|access-date=19 August 2024}} Also available at [https://gazette.com/ap/international/venezuela-could-charge-opposition-leader-machado-with-murder-regime-s-prosecutor-says/article_88d4dff3-eb30-5b8f-bca4-a51a69abb0ee.html Colorado Springs Gazette]</ref>

[[Freddy Superlano]], a former candidate, was detained by masked men two days after the election,<ref name="WSJElectionDatabase" /><ref name= BloombergCrackdown>{{cite news |url= https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2024-07-30/venezuela-apprehends-opposition-figure-amid-election-protests |work= Bloomberg | title= Venezuela Detains Opposition Figure Amid Post-Election Crackdown |date= 30 July 2024 |access-date= 30 July 2024| first= Andreina |last= Itriago Acosta}}</ref> and held on unknown charges at [[El Helicoide]] along with detained journalist {{ill|Roland Carreño|es}}.<ref>{{cite news |url= https://eldiario.com/2024/08/06/freddy-superlano-roland-carreno-el-helicoide/ |title= Confirmaron que Freddy Superlano y Roland Carreño se encuentran recluidos en El Helicoide|language=es |trans-title= Confirmed that Freddy Superlano and Roland Carreño are being held in El Helicoide |date= 6 August 2024 |access-date= 7 August 2024 |first= Yanuacelis |last= Aure |work= El Diario}}</ref> After the election, supporters and representatives of the opposition, as well as journalists, have been detained.<ref name=BBCRepressionWorsens/><ref>{{cite news |work= NTN24 |date= 30 July 2024 |access-date= 31 July 2024 |title= Hombres armados arrestan a Freddy Superlano y otros dos políticos opositores |language= es |trans-title= Armed men arrest Freddy Superlano and two other political opposers |url= https://www.ntn24.com/noticias-actualidad/hombres-armados-arrestan-a-freddy-superlano-y-otros-dos-politicos-opositores-505131}}</ref><ref name=ChillingVideo>{{cite news |url= https://www.infobae.com/venezuela/2024/08/08/el-escalofriante-video-con-el-que-el-regimen-de-maduro-atemoriza-a-los-venezolanos-y-se-burla-de-la-dirigente-maria-oropeza-y-de-la-oposicion/ |work= Infobae |date= 8 August 2024 |access-date= 9 August 2024 |title= El escalofriante video con el que el régimen de Maduro atemoriza a los venezolanos y se burla de la dirigente María Oropeza y de la oposición |language=es|trans-title= The chilling video with which the Maduro regime frightens Venezuelans and mocks the leader María Oropeza and the opposition}}</ref><ref name= VOAonWSJ/> Opposition leaders said that citizens who witnessed the [[#Electoral process|vote tally sheets in the electoral process]] (poll watchers) were persecuted and detained.<ref name= ReportProtesters>{{cite news |url= https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2024/07/31/venezuela-election-maduro-protest-crackdown/ |newspaper= The Washington Post |date= 31 July 2024 |access-date= 1 August 2024 |title= Maduro urges Venezuelans to report protesters who question his reelection |first1= Ana Vanessa |last1= Herrero |first2= Maria Luisa |last2= Paul |first3= Samantha |last3= Schmidt}}</ref>

The press and social media have been subject to censorship.<ref name= VOAonWSJ>{{cite news |url= https://www.vozdeamerica.com/a/the-wall-street-journal-se-suma-a-la-lista-de-sitios-web-bloqueados-en-venezuela-y-se-registran-detenciones-de-trabajadores-de-la-prensa/7727406.html |work= Voice of America |title= The Wall Street Journal se suma a los sitios web bloqueados en Venezuela, donde se registran detenciones de comunicadores|language=es |trans-title= The Wall Street Journal joins the list of websites blocked in Venezuela, where journalists have been arrested |date= 2 August 2024 |access-date= 7 August 2024}}</ref><ref name="BBC-XBan">{{cite news |title=Venezuela: Nicolás Maduro bans X for 10 days over Elon Musk row |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/c5ypx0p84rgo |access-date=9 August 2024 |publisher= [[BBC News]]}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url= https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuelas-maduro-signs-decree-blocking-x-access-10-days-2024-08-08/ |title= Venezuela's Maduro signs decree blocking X access in country for 10 days |date= 9 August 2024 |access-date= 9 August 2024 |work= Reuters}}</ref> The legislature passed a new law "to more tightly regulate non-governmental organizations, amid criticism of a government crackdown".<ref name=RegulateNGO>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuela-legislators-approve-law-regulate-ngos-2024-08-15/ |title= Venezuela legislators approve law to regulate NGOs|work=Reuters|date=15 August 2024|access-date=20 August 2024}}</ref>

=== Transparency in vote reporting and Supreme Court ruling===
{{Main|2024 Venezuelan political crisis#Transparency in vote reporting and Supreme Court ruling}}
Opposition leaders, world leaders and observers urged Maduro to make the vote tallies at the polling station level public,<ref name= BBCStayinPower/> which had not happened as of 21 August.<ref name=GuardianPressureGrows/> Refusing to cede power,<ref name=GuardianRefusal /> Maduro instead asked the [[Supreme Tribunal of Justice (Venezuela)|Supreme Tribunal of Justice]] on 1 August to audit and approve the results.<ref name=ReutersCourtRatifies/><!--The president, a long-time ruling party official before he rose to the presidency, had asked the court to verify the results.--><ref name= BBCStayinPower/><ref name=CriesFoul/><ref name=APCourtCertifies/>

The BBC stated that the TSJ review is "likely to be conducted behind closed doors" where only members will see the tallies. The [[Carter Center]], anticipating this move, stated that "the TSJ is another government institution, appointed by the government ... &nbsp;not an independent assessment".<ref name= BBCStayinPower/> ''[[Efecto Cocuyo]]'' questioned the independence of the TSJ observers.<ref name="EfectoCocuyo_who_TSJ_experts">{{cite news|url=https://efectococuyo.com/politica/quienes-son-los-peritos-del-tsj-que-verifican-material-del-28-de-julio/|url-status=live|title=¿Quiénes son los peritos del TSJ que verifican material del 28 de julio?|trans-title=Who are the TSJ experts verifying the documents of 28 July? |language=es|work=[[Efecto Cocuyo]]|date=20 August 2024|archive-url=https://archive.today/20240822130632/https://efectococuyo.com/politica/quienes-son-los-peritos-del-tsj-que-verifican-material-del-28-de-julio|archive-date=22 August 2024|id=Wikidata [[:d:Q129576388]]}} Citing Smartmatic: {{cite web|url=https://www.smartmatic.com/us/media/smartmatic-statement-on-the-recent-constituent-assembly-election-in-venezuela/?__cf_chl_f_tk=emoAi2qyzK2UZsB1J3pdUkigiCdGTp7xujw_N0BWung-1724434394-0.0.1.1-5097|title=Smartmatic Statement on the recent Constituent Assembly Election in Venezuela|publisher=Smartmatic|date=2 August 2017|access-date=23 August 2024|id= Wikidata [[:d:Q129572081]]|archive-date=20 August 2024|archive-url= https://archive.today/20240820182010/https://www.smartmatic.com/us/media/smartmatic-statement-on-the-recent-constituent-assembly-election-in-venezuela/|url-status=live}}</ref>

As anticipated,<ref name=BBCStayinPower/><ref name=LoyaltoMaduro>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2024/08/22/world/americas/venezuela-supreme-court-maduro-election.html|work=The New York Times|title=Venezuela's Supreme Court, Loyal to Maduro, Rules Him Election Winner|date=22 August 2024|access-date=23 August 2024|author1=Turkewitz, Julie|author2= Glatsky, Genevieve |quote= The decision surprised few Venezuelans, as the court has long been used to rubber-stamp the policies of Mr. Maduro, who is likely to use this ruling to strengthen his claim to the presidency.}}</ref><ref name=HandPicked>{{cite news|url=https://www.wsj.com/world/americas/venezuelas-supreme-court-backs-maduro-as-election-winner-93f5d184|title=Maduro's Hand-Picked Supreme Court Calls Him Venezuela's Election Winner|work=The Wall Street Journal|date=22 August 2023|access-date=23 August 2024|author=Vyas, Kejal|quote=The court's ruling was expected, as it is stacked with loyalists to Maduro's ruling Socialist Party.}}</ref><ref name=ElPaisVenezuelaCourt>{{cite news|url=https://english.elpais.com/international/2024-08-23/venezuelas-supreme-court-a-tribunal-that-dispenses-justice-tailored-to-nicolas-maduros-needs.html |work=El País|date=23 August 2024|access-date=23 August 2024|title=Venezuela's Supreme Court, a tribunal that dispenses justice tailored to Nicolás Maduro's needs}}</ref> after reviewing materials submitted, the Supreme Justice Tribunal (TSJ), composed of justices loyal to Maduro, validated the CNE's statements of a win by Maduro; the opposition and other observers have characterized their ruling as invalid, stating that the high court has no constitutional authority over elections.<ref name=GuardianPressureGrows>{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/article/2024/aug/22/maduro-accused-power-grab-top-court-endorses-venezuela-election-win|title=Pressure grows on Maduro after top court endorses Venezuela election win|work=The Guardian|author=Phillips, Tom|date=22 August 2024|access-date=23 August 2024}}</ref><ref name=ReutersCourtRatifies>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuelas-top-court-ratifies-maduro-election-win-government-tightens-control-2024-08-22/|title=Venezuela's top court ratifies Maduro election win as government tightens control|work=Reuters|date=22 August 2024|access-date=22 August 2024}}</ref><ref name=APCourtCertifies>{{cite news|url=https://apnews.com/article/venezuela-election-supreme-court-certifies-maduro-39d9f3b9beb0fe96fa052e4d2a3c106b|publisher=Associated Press|title=Venezuela's Supreme Court certifies Maduro's claims that he won presidential election|date=22 August 2024|access-date=23 August 2024|quote=Its decision, read Thursday in an event attended by senior officials and foreign diplomats, came in response to a request by Maduro to review vote totals showing he had won by more than 1 million votes.}}</ref><ref name=LoyaltoMaduro/> The court stated that the opposition vote tallies were falsified; the Associated Press wrote that the Maduro administration "has claimed—without evidence—that a foreign cyberattack staged by hackers from North Macedonia delayed the vote counting on election night and publication of the disaggregated results."<ref name=APCourtCertifies/>

[[NTN24]] reported that on 26 August, the CNE webpage was briefly accessible. During the period of access, some people were able to view the names of witnesses of the ''actas'' and check if they matched what the opposition had reported on ''resultadosporvenezuela.com''. According to NTN24, the names were found to match.<ref name=CNEOpen>{{cite news|url=https://www.ntn24.com/noticias-actualidad/acceso-que-se-abrio-por-una-hora-en-el-portal-del-cne-demostro-que-las-actas-de-la-oposicion-coincidian-509995|work=[[NTN24]]|date=27 August 2024|access-date=27 August 2024|language=es|title=Acceso que se abrió por una hora en el portal del CNE demostró que las actas de la oposición coincidían|trans-title=Access that was opened for one hour on the CNE portal showed that the opposition's records coincided}}</ref>

=== González arrest warrant and exile ===
[[Caryslia Rodríguez]], president of the high court, said that a criminal investigation would be conducted regarding "presumably false" results that were published;<ref name="ReutersCourtRatifies" /> González was summoned to appear on accusations, among others, of usurping the CNE's functions by uploading election records to ''www.resultadosconvzla.com'';<ref name=NTN24FormallySummons>{{cite news|url=https://www.ntn24.com/noticias-judicial/fiscalia-venezolana-cita-formalmente-al-excandidato-edmundo-gonzalez-y-lo-acusa-de-graves-delitos-509601|work=[[NTN24]]|date=24 August 2024|access-date=24 August 2024|language=es|title=Fiscalía venezolana cita formalmente al excandidato Edmundo González y lo acusa de graves delitos|trans-title=Venezuelan Prosecutor's Office formally summons former candidate Edmundo González and accuses him of serious crimes}}</ref> he did not appear for the 26 August summons,<ref name=ChangeinLife>{{cite news|url=https://english.elpais.com/international/2024-08-26/the-change-in-the-life-of-edmundo-gonzalez-from-unknown-diplomat-to-vortex-of-the-venezuelan-crisis.html|work=[[El País]]|access-date=26 August 2024|title=The change in the life of Edmundo González: From unknown diplomat to vortex of the Venezuelan crisis|date=26 August 2024|author=Moleiro, Alonso}}</ref><ref name=ReutersSecondSummons>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuelan-attorney-generals-office-issues-second-summons-opposition-leader-2024-08-26/|work=Reuters|access-date=26 August 2024|title=Venezuelan attorney general's office issues second summons for opposition leader Gonzalez|date=26 August 2024}}</ref> or the second summons on 27 August.<ref name=AFPSecondSummons>{{cite news|url=https://www.barrons.com/news/venezuela-opposition-candidate-ignores-second-summons-c6cc5d29|work=Barron's|publisher=Agence France-Press|date=27 August 2024|access-date=27 August 2024|title=Venezuela Opposition Candidate Ignores Second Summons|author=Tovar, Javier}}</ref>

After he failed to respond to a third summons, an arrest warrant was issued on 2 September for González for crimes including criminal association and conspiracy after prosecutor Luis Ernesto Dueñez Reyes "requested Gonzalez be arrested for usurpation of functions, falsification of public documents, instigation to disobey the law, conspiracy and association", according to Reuters.<ref name=APArrestWarrant>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/venezuela-attorney-general-requests-arrest-warrant-opposition-leader-gonzalez-2024-09-02/|work=Reuters|date=2 September 2024|access-date=3 September 2024|title=Venezuela issues arrest warrant for opposition leader Gonzalez, AG says|author1=Sequera, Vivian|author2=Armas, Mayela}}</ref><ref name=GuardianArrestWarrant>{{cite news |url= https://www.theguardian.com/world/article/2024/sep/03/edmundo-gonzalez-venezuela-election-opposition-leader-prosecutors-arrest-warrant|work=The Guardian|date=2 September 2024|access-date=3 September 2024|title=Venezuela judge issues arrest warrant for opposition leader after disputed election|author= Phillips, Tom}}</ref> González sought refuge for several days in the Spanish embassy in Caracas, and was granted asylum, leaving on a Spanish Armed Forces flight for Madrid on 7 September 2024.<ref name=ElDiarioAsylum>{{cite news|url=https://eldiario.com/2024/09/07/edmundo-gonzalez-abandono-venezuela-asilo-espana/|work=[[El Diario de Caracas]]|date= 7 September 2024|access-date=8 September 2024|language=es|title=Edmundo González abandonó Venezuela tras solicitar asilo político en España|trans-title=Edmundo González left Venezuela after requesting political asylum in Spain}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/c14zdypxr7no|publisher= BBC News|date=8 September 2024|access-date=8 September 2024|title=Venezuela's opposition leader leaves country for Spain}}</ref><ref name=ElMundoNegotiatingExile>{{cite news |url= https://www.elmundo.es/internacional/2024/09/08/66dd0f9afc6c83894b8b4580.html|work=[[El Mundo (Spain)|El Mundo]]|language=es|date=8 September 2024|access-date=8 September 2024|title=Edmundo González vuela a Madrid tras negociar su exilio|trans-title=Edmundo González flies to Madrid after negotiating his exile|author1= Lozano, Daniel|author2= Piña, Raúl}}</ref>

=== Transition proposals ===
{{Main|2024 Venezuelan political crisis#Transition proposals}}
Negotiated [[peaceful transition of power]] proposals include an exit deal<ref name="o850">{{cite web | last=Abrams | first=Elliott | title=Can Maduro Be Negotiated Out of Venezuela? | website=Council on Foreign Relations | date=19 July 2024 | url=https://www.cfr.org/blog/can-maduro-be-negotiated-out-venezuela | access-date=29 July 2024 | archive-date=25 July 2024 | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240725045624/https://www.cfr.org/blog/can-maduro-be-negotiated-out-venezuela | url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="wp27jul">{{cite news | last1=Schmidt | first1=Samantha | last2=Herrero | first2=Ana Vanessa | title=If Maduro loses, will he cede power? Venezuela's election, explained. | newspaper=The Washington Post | date=27 July 2024 | url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2024/07/27/venezuela-election-maduro-gonzalez-machado/ | access-date=27
